O vos, tres chiers filz, je vos ai acomplit cest livre qui est li derriens de la science de medicine ensamble l’emplissement de lui, et ai fait la fin per ses expositions et par ses declarations.	I have brought you to this book, which is the conclusion of medical science, and I have completed it with its explanations and declarations.
Et m’est venu en vision que je le vos acomplisse avec cest traitier, qui est partie de l’uevre de mains, c’est a savoir «cyrurgie».	And in my vision, it came to me that I would complete this treatise with it, which is part of the work of hands, that is to say "surgery".
Et por ceu que l’uevre de mains est fortraite en nostre region et est etraingie dou tout en tout, si est perie li science et decopee, et n’est riens demorez de li fuers que les petites descriptions en livres des anciens que les mains ont muees.	And because the work of hands is well-established in our region and is widely known from one place to another, it has a well-deserved reputation and deserves no less respect than any other science or art; nor are there any great delays in its progress due to the small descriptions found in books by the ancient physicians who wrote about the movements of the hands.
Et de ceu est venue li error et li vanitez, et sont closes les ententions et est aloignie li science.	And from this error and vanity have come, and intentions are closed and science is remote.
Or me semble que je la vuel vivifier ensamble l’ordination de cest traitier selonc la voie d’exposition et de declaration et de l’abreviation; et venrai ensamble les formes des ferremens de cautere, et des autres estrumens de l’uevre avec l’ajostement de la declaration et de preparation de li, sicom il est mestier.	For it seems to me that I can revive it with the order of this treatise, in accordance with the method of exposition and declaration and abbreviation; and I will come with the forms of the tools for cauterizing, and of the other instruments for the work, with the preparation and arrangement of them, as is necessary.
Et por la raison de ceu que nuls boins maistres de mains n’est trovez en nostre tens, est li ars de medicine eslongié.	And because there are no good doctors of hands to be found in our land, therefore the art of medicine is abandoned.
Et covient celui qui s’en entremet sormonter en la science d’anathomie, si com Galiens dit, tant qu’il saiche la juement des menbres, et les formes et les conjunctions et les separations d’aus, et aient connissance des osses et des nerf et des brais et le nombre d’ous, et le demenement et des voines movans et des reposans, et dou leu de lor issue.	And he who confronts this matter must rise to the science of anatomy, as Galen says, so that he knows the judgment of the limbs, and their forms and joints and separations of bones, and has knowledge of the nerves and arteries and veins and number of bones, and the movement and moving veins and resting veins, and the place of their issue.
Et por ceu dist Ypocras que li nons avec le non est mout, et avec l’uevre est poc; et meismement en l’art de main.	And because, as Hipocrates says, the one that is with the hand is not without and the work is not with it; and most especially in the art of the hands.
Nos vos disons en l’introite de cest livre que qui n’est conissans des choses devant dites, si se gart qu’il ne chiece en error et qu’il n’ocie les homes; ensi que j’ai veut maintes fois plusors de ces qui s’entremettent de ceste science et si s’abandonent sen science et sens experiment.	We tell you in the introduction of this book that who is not knowledgeable about the things mentioned above should refrain from trying to treat people; thus, I have often warned many of those who confront this art and abandon their knowledge and experience.
Car je vis un fol mire qui copa I apostume de scrophules ou col d’une femme, et copa les arteres dou col; por coi tant de sanc issit hors que li femme cheit morte entre ses mains.	I saw a foolish man who chopped off an abscess on the neck of a woman, and he also chopped the arteries in her neck; therefore so much blood flowed out that the woman died between his hands.
Et vis I autre mire qui traït une piere d’un home d’eaige, et li piere estoit grans; si emporta avec li une piece de la vessie, et fut mors li hons dedens III jors.	And I saw another foolish man who was treating a stone in a man's bladder, and the stone was large; he brought out a piece of the bladder with it, and he died three days later.
Et je i avoie ja esteit apelez por lou traire, et vis la disposition dou malaide et la grandor de la piere, et soi bien s’on lou tailloit il en morroit.	And I have already seen it called upon to operate, and I saw the dislocation of the patient and the size of the stone, and if they operated on him he would die.
Et vis I autre mire qui prist en cure I duc de nostre terre qui avoit la jambe brisie, et avec la briseure ot plaie; et li mires plains d’ignorance estraint la brisure sus la plaie as esteles par fort lieure, et ne lassa a la plaie point de xalain, et le lassa ensi I termine; et li comanda qu’il ne la desliast mie; et demora ensi que li jambe fut toute enflee et li piez et vint a perdition.	And I saw another foolish man who took ill our duke, who had his leg broken, and with the break there was a wound; and the stupid doctor pulls out the break onto the wound with great violence, leaving no scar on the wound, and leaves it like that; and he ordered that he not put it back; and he waited so long that the leg became completely infected and the bones came to destruction.
Je fuis apelez por venir a lui, et me hastai por venir deslier la jambe; et quant je l’oi desloie si fut em pais et ne sentit point de dolor.	I was called to go to him, and I hurried to dislodge his leg; and when I had dislodged it, he was at peace and felt no pain.
Mais toute voie li corruptions estoit ja confermee ou membre, et ne la poi saner; et ne cessa li corrution d’aler par le membre tant que li membres fut dou tout perdus.	But all the ways that corruption entered into the limb were confirmed, and I could not heal it; and the corruption did not cease to spread through the limb until the limbs were completely lost.
Et vis I autre mire qui effondra I apostume enchancreit, et puis enflama per le malice de sa signorie.	And I saw another thing that would shatter an abscess full of pus, and then inflame by the evil of its lordship.
Car chancre, quant il est purs d’umor melancolique, ne covient mie qu’on i(l) touche de fer s’il n’est en teil leu c’on puisse toute oster ce que est corrumpus.	For chaf, when it is purred with melancholy humor, does not come except one touch iron in a place where it can be all opened out what is corrupted.
Et por ceu, treschier filz, vos est besoig que vos sachiez que oevre de mains est devisee en II divisions: c’est asavoir, huevre ou il a peril en plusors dispositions; et je mostrerai en chescun leu de cest livre ou il a paour et peril.	And for this reason, very crafty son, you must know that work of hands is divided into II divisions: namely, where there is danger in many dispositions; and I will show in each of these in this book where there is fear and danger.
Por coi il est besoig que vos vos en gardez, si que li fol mire ne puissent mal parler de vos Si prenez vos armes en cusenson, et entreprenez vos malaides legierement et fermement, et usez de la millor voie si que per la graice de Deu vos venez a salut et soiez loez; et lassiez les maladies espoantables de grief saniteit; et ostez vos armes de ceu que vos fait douter, et aiez foit en vos si que vos puissiez venir de cestui monde a l’autre de gloire.	For so that you may keep it, so that the little child does not speak ill of you; If you take your weapons in agreement, and undertake your diseases lightly and firmly, and use the better way so that through the grace of God you come to salvation and be free; and leave behind you the expected diseases of grief health; and lay aside your weapons from him who makes you doubt, and have faith in yourself so that you may come from this world to the other of glory.
Galiens dist en aucuns de ses amonestemens: «Ne prenez mie en cure male maladie, que vos ne soiez apelez fol mire.	Galien includes some of his warnings in: "Do not take on a disease that is difficult to treat, lest you be called a foolish person.
» J’ai deviseit cest traitier selonc III chapitres.	I have devised this treatise according to three chapters.
Li premiers chapitres est des cauteres de feu et dé cauteres de medicine ague, et est li chapitres ordenez de lou chief jusques as piez; et des formes des estrumens, et des ferremens de cautere, et de tout ceu qui est necessaire en l’ueuvre.	The first chapters are about fire cauterizations and water-based medicine, and the subsequent chapters are ordered from top to bottom, including the forms of instruments, the fieriness of cauterization, and all that is necessary in this work.
Li secons chapitres si est de taillier et de percier, et des ventouses et des plaies, et des estractions des saiettes, et des semblans choses; et est li chapitres ordenez et les formes des estrumens.	The second chapter deals with matters of cutting and piercing, with sucking cups, wounds, extraction of arrows, and similar things; the chapter contains instructions on techniques and the form of instruments.
Li tiers chapitres est de restorer les dislocations et des torcions, et des semblans choses; et est ordeneiz des lou chief jusc’as piez, et des formes des estrumens.	The third chapter deals with restoring dislocations and torments, and similar things; it also contains instructions on the shape of tools up to the point where they are sharp, and the forms of instruments.
Ainsois que nos nos remembriens de l’uevre, il covient que je die la qualiteit de l’aide et dou nuisement de chescune complexion.	Thus we remember the work, it is necessary that I speak of the quality of help and the harm of each kind.
Je dis que li qualiteis de l’aide, et dou nuisement, est li plus longe parole et subtilz science et li secrez reponus; et de ceu parlerent li plusors des saiges, et s’acorderent a ceu; et me soffisent poc lor paroles, car je redous la longesce.	I say that the quality of help and harm is the longest word and subtlest science and most hidden answer; and many wise people would speak of it, and agree with it; and I am satisfied with few words, for I shorten the length.
Je dis que cautere aide universement a toute complexion ou il a matiere, fuer que II complexions: c’est a savoir complexion chaude sens matere, et complexion seche sens matere.	I say that fire is help to all complexions or it has matter, except for two complexions: namely, complexions of heat and matter, and dry complexions without matter.
En complexion chaude et seche ensamble matiere, deviserent aucun et dirent que cautere i est grans aide; et li autre dirent le contraire: que cautere ne vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de sechour.	In hot and dry complexions together with matter, they all agreed that cauterization is great help; but one said the opposite: that cautery is no good for disease caused by heat and dryness.
Car li nature dou feu si est chaude, et ne doit mie estre cureiz de chaude maladie par chalor, ne per sechour; et dist cil qui dist lou contraire que cautere fait grant aide a maladie chaude et seche que vient en cors des homes.	For the nature of fire is so hot, and it should not be used for curing diseases caused by heat and dryness; and he who said that cauterization helps a great deal in curing diseases caused by heat and dryness said the opposite: that cautery is good for no disease caused by heat and dryness.
Car quant tu comperes le cors de l’ome et sa moistor a la complexion dou feu, tu trueves le cors froit.	For when you compare the body of the man and his moisture to the complexion of fire, you find the body cold.
Et je m’acorde a ceste parole.	And I agree with this word.
Car je l’ai troveit aucune fois per experiment.	For I have never found it by experience.
Et toute voie, ne s’en entremette mie fuers que cil qui l’a esproveit, et qui conoit par lonc usaige le chapistre des cauteres, et la diversiteit des complexions des homes, et les dispositions et les causes de lor maladies, et les sorvenues et l’espaice dou tens; des autres complexions n’avons nos mie paour, meismement em maladies froides et moistes.	For no way does it harm but that which has tried it, and who knows by long practice the effects of cauterization, and the differences in the complexions of men, their conditions and causes of disease, and the season; for we fear not the effects on cold and moist complexions, even though they have diseases.
Et tuit li mire s’asemblerent et s’acorderent au cautere.	And all this comes together and agrees with the fire cautery.
Et sachiez, filz, que cautere ensamble feu si est des secrez des cures, et de plus grant bonteit que cautere de medicine ardant.	And know, children, that a fire cautery is good for secretions of healing, and of greater goodness than an arding medicine cautery.
Car li feus est simples, et ne vient mie fuers que au membre qui est cuis, et ne nuit a autre membre se poc nom.	For fire is simple, and comes only to the member that is cooked, and does not harm another member so much as one name.
Les medicines ardans vienent de membre a autre en aloignant, et font venir au membre maladies de grief sanation; et par aventure ocit lou malaide Li feus por sa hautece et por la bonteit de sa substance ne fait mie ceu, s’il n’i a superfluiteit.	The burning medicines come from one member to another by moving away, and bring diseases of great healing to the member; and perhaps fire, for its greatness and for the goodness of its substance, does not hurt if there is no excess.
Et ceu vos ai je troveit par experiment et par la longesce dou servise et de l’estude que j’ai mis en l’art, et esteit sus la verteit des choses; et por ceu je m’escuse de la longesce de la parole, car il ne me plait mie que je vos oste le secreit qui est reponus ou feu, et la qualiteit de l’uevre, coment il deboute les maladies des cors, si com li philosophe le dit en demostrant; or le recevez en vos pensees.	And I have found it by experience and by the length of service and study that I have put into this art, and it is based on the truth of things; and therefore I beg your pardon for the length of the speech, for it does not please me to deprive you of the secret that is found in fire, and the quality of the work, as the philosopher says in proving; or take it into consideration.
Et sachiez, fil, que il s’acorderent en quel tens doient estre faites les cauteres, et eslirent prientens.	And know, son, that these cauterizations should be made at certain times, and they should be prayed over.
Et je dis que cautere est covenable en tous tens, por ceu que li nuisemens sorvenans est desoz mis par l’aide dou cautere; et meismement se li cauteres est por dolors necessaires fors et hastans que ne puent atendre le tens que plus grans malice ne veigne au membre.	And I say that cauterization is appropriate at all times, because the harm that overtakes is prevented by the aid of cauterization; and most especially, the cauterization is for necessary pains without delay that cannot wait until the time when greater illness comes to the limb.
Et n’i pensez onques, chier fil, si com font li fol mire; car a la maladie qui est sanee par cautere n’a point de revenue; et il le dient ensi; mais il n’est mie si com il cuident, por ce que cauteres nen est que medicine qui mue la complexion, et seche les humors que sont cause de la dolor, et vaut mues que medicine por le hastement de sa valor, et por la vertut de son oevre et de sa signorie.	And do not think, my son, as they say; for in the disease that is healed by cauterization there is no return; and it serves thus: but it is not so much as they think, because cauterization is a medicine that changes the complexion, dries up the humors which are causes of pain, and does good rather than medicine for the speed of its effect, and for its virtue and dignity.
Et possans chose est que li maladie viegne aucune fois selonc la complexion dou malaide et lou leu de la maladie et sa vertut; et sont assemblees en lui les superfluitez par l’aquisition des viandes et des semblans choses, se ce n’est cauteres administrez em leu ou il ait poc de superfluitez et de moistor, si com cauteres de dens por la dolor, et les semblans choses, et teil dolor ne revient mie; mais ce avient poc.	And that which is possible for the disease to come according to the complexion of the patient and the place of the disease and its virtue; and are gathered in him the excesses by the acquisition of meat and similar things, except if cauterizes are administered at the place where he has little excess and moisture, as cauterizes of density from pain, and similar things, and partial pain does not return but it happened a little.
Et mout de gens n’entendent mie por coi cauteres est apelez li derriens de medecine, et c’est voir; mais il ne croient mie que cauteres vaille aprés medicine, mais lor ententions est fause, et est cauteres li derriens de medicine por ceu que quant nos aministrons manieres de cures en aucune maladie et elles ne valent, adonc administrons nos le cautere, et il vaut.	And many people do not understand why the cauterizes are called the remedies of medicine, and that is true; but they do not believe that the cauterizes are worth anything after the medicine, but their intentions are wrong, and the cauterizes are the remedies of medicine because when we administered ways of cure in no disease and they did not work, then let us administer the cauterize, and it works.
Adonques apert bien que cauteres est li derriens de medicine, ne mie selonc l’entention des folz mires.	Therefore, understand well that the cauterizes are the remedies of medicine, not because of the intention of the foolish people.
Li ancien dirent que cauteres d’estrument d’or est muedres que de fer, et ne dirent ceu fuers que por la qualiteit de l’or et por la hautece de sa substance; et dirent que li leus de cautere ne fait mie porriture, mais ceu n’est mie voir car je l’ai esprovei, et ai troveit que c’est voir en aucuns homes; et cauteres d’or vaut mues que de fer, si com il lou dirent.	Li ancien dirent que cauteres d'estrument d'or est muedres que de fer, et ne dirent ceu fuers que por la qualite de l'or et por la hautece de sa substance; et dirent que li leus de cautere ne fait mie porriture, mais ceu n'est mie voir car je l'ai esprovei, et ai troveit que c'est voir en aucuns homes; et cauteres d'or vaut mues que de fer, si com il lou dirent.
Et toutevoie quant tu chaufes estrument d’or, tu ne seis mie quant il est chaus par la color de l’or, et s’est tantost refroidiez; et s’on le chaufe trop; si font au feu; et ensi i a assez d’empechement.	The ancient ones said that gold cauterization instruments are more efficacious than those of iron, and they said that the heat of gold is greater in quality and substance; and they said that the heating of the tip does not cause inflammation, but this is not true because I have tested it, and I have found that it does occur in some people; and gold cauterization instruments are more effective than those of iron, as they say. However, when you heat up a gold instrument, you will find that it becomes cold quickly; and if you heat it too much, it melts into the fire; and thus there is sufficient impediment.
Et por ce usons nos de cautere de feir que nos l’avons mues apparilliet a nostre oevre.	And for this we use fire cautery, which we have prepared for our work.
Or vos ai ordeneit cest chapitre des lou chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que li voie soit plus legiere a trover.	Or you may order this chapter of the heart until it is easier to find the vein.
dou cautere olivaire	The olive oil cautery
Cist cauteres vaut a moistor et a froidor sus lou cerveil, et en i a dous c’on fait par la cause d’une maladie qui est apelee «soda», et par la cause de maintes humors qui dessendent dou chief as eulz, et as oreilles, et por multitude de songes et dolor de dens et dolor de gorge, et meismement a toutes maladies qui vienent de froidor si com paralisie et sode et apoplexie et semblans maladies.	The olive oil cautery is useful for the head, and by reason of moisture and cold, and for many ailments that arise in the hair, and in the ears, and for a multitude of pains and headaches and pains in the jaw and throat, and most particularly for all diseases that come from coldness such as paralysis, sodiness, apoplexia, and similar illnesses.
Li forme de cest cautere si est que li malaides soit espurgiez par medicine solutive mondifiant le chief III nuis ou IIII, selonc ceu que li vertus et li eaige et li acostumance dou malaide le puet soffrir; et puis fai rere lou chief dou malaide.	The form of this cautery is that the disease should be expelled by a liquid medicine that softens the head in three or four days, according to what the virtue and the age and the habit of the patient can bear; and then wash the head of the patient.
Et puis le fai seoir croisiet entre tes mains, et mettre ses mains sor som peis; aprés met la racine de ta palme sus la racine de son neis entre ses II eulz; et lai ou venra tes dois moiens, si saigne d’enche puis eschaufe le cautere qui est apelé «olivare», de coi ci est li forme:	And then place the fire between your hands, and put his hands on some stone; after that put the root of your palm on the root of its nail between its two nails; and let the two edges come together, so it bleeds a little, then heat the cautery which is called 'olivare', from which there comes this form:
Et le met sor le leu signiet d’encre, et fai en dessendant et en estraignant ta main poc et poc en trestornant; puis lieve ta main isnelement, et rewarde le leu se tu vois l’os I sol petit; et se tu ne lou vois, si rencomence le cautere tant que tu voies l’os si com je lou t’ai dit; aprés pren I poc de seil, et met en awe et molle coton dedens, et met sor le leu, et li laisse III jors; aprés met sus cotun moilliet en burre; et laisse sus tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés cure la plaie de l’oignement qui est apelez «tetrafarmaçon», tant qu’il soit sanez.	And then place the fire between your hands, and put his hands on some stone; after that put the root of your palm on the root of its nail between its two nails; and let the two edges come together, so it bleeds a little, then heat the cautery which is called 'olivare', from which there comes this form:
Et se dirent li ancien, que quant plus demoure overte li plaie, plus s’espurge; et por ce si aide mues.	And the old man said, "The longer the wound remains open, the more it will fester; and for this reason if it is moved or touched.
Et dirent aucun de ces que on doit tant lassier le cautere que partie de l’os soit arse, et puis rese on ceu qui est ars de l’os, et soit curez.	And they said that one must leave the burn unhealed until the burned part of the bone is eaten away, and then cut off what has been eaten away from the bone, and heal it.
Et dient li autre c’on doit le cautere tant lassier sus, et bouter si fort c’on abaite de l’os ausi large comme I vertoil que les femmes mettent en lor fusez por ceu que les humors issent mues hors; et doit on lassier la plaie longement overte; aprés le doit on curer et sodeir.	And another said, "One must leave the burn unhealed for as long as possible, and then cut so hard that the humors can exit through the wound; and one must leave the wound open for a long time; afterwards, it should be healed and dressed.
Et ces II manieres de cauteres ne me semblent mie estre bones dou tout en tout, fuers qu’en aucuns homes ou il ait voie de paor; et mues me semble que je lou doie laissier; car li chiés li est afoiblis par les solutions continuees de nature, si com nos le tesmoignons ens autres membres; et meisme quant li chiés dou malaide est foibles par nature, et li premiere semblance de cautere est plus salve et muedre por moi, et de celi use je oevre en donques emsamble salut.	And these two ways of treating burns do not seem good to me in all cases, except when there is doubt; and I believe that I should leave it alone; for the joints are weakened by continued motion, as we have seen in other members; and moreover, when the joint of the patient is weak by nature, and the first appearance of a burn seems more healthy and peaceful to me, and so I use it with care until it heals completely.
de l’anciainne dolor dou chief	of the ancient pain of the head
Quant en tout le chief vient dolor croniques, et dure longement, si doit user li malaides yeris et pilules qui sont apelees «cochie», et d’espurgement de chief et d’oiles et d’emplastres; et s’on li fait le cautere que nos avons devant dit, et il ne vaut.	When the whole head feels chronic pain and lasts a long time, the patient should use herbal remedies and treatments called 'cochier', and head rinses and oils and ointments; and if it is done the fire cautery we have mentioned above, and it does not help.
Pren warde se li chiés dou malade est de fort nature, et qu’il ne soit trop froit; adonques le cauterize desoz celui cautere un poc que nos avons dit desus.	Take care that the patient's neck is of strong nature, and that he is not too cold; then cauterize it lightly as we have mentioned above.
Aprés fai cautere sus chescune corne dou chief jusc’a l’os, si com devant avons dit, et fai I cautere ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz»; et est I leus en coi on met ventouses; et alige ta main si que tu ne voises mie jusc’a l’os: li malaides sent trop plus grant dolor en cest cautere que as autres, et je em parlerai aillors; et covient que li cauteres des cornes soient plus subtis que cil dont on cautere la moieneteit dou chief, et c’est li forme:	After you have made the fire cautery on each side of the neck up to the bone, as we have said above, and made it at the place called 'vesselz'; then put the cupping glasses; and hold your hand so that you do not see the bones at all: the patient feels too much pain in this cauterization than in others, and I will speak about it later; and it is necessary for the cuppings on the neck to be made thinner than those with which we cauterize the hairline of the head, and this is the form:
dou cautere dou chief	To cauterize the head
Quant en une partie dou chief vient dolor sodaine, et est estendue li maladie jusc’a l’oil, et li chiés est espurgiez par medicines mondifians, et on a fait les autres cures que j’ai dit en la division des maladies, et tout ceu ne profite mie: adonques li fai cauteres selonc II manieres, c’est a savoir de medicine ague et de feir.	When sudden pain in the head appears and spreads up to the oil, and the shoulder is cleansed with medicinal poisons, and other cures are performed as mentioned in the division of diseases, and all this does not help: then do cauterization according to two ways, that is to say, with water medicine and fire.
Li cauteres de medicine ague si est que tu preignes une doce d’alz, et oste l’escorce et le recope I poc as II chiés, et puis fent la temple ou li dolor tient en teil maniere que tu puisses reponre la doce d’alz desoz le cuir; et quant elle sera reponuee si le lie et l’estraint bien et le laisse ensi XII houres; et puis le deslie et trait fuers la doce d’ail, et laisse la plaie ensi II jors ou III; puis met sus cotun plongiet en burre tant que porreture en isse.	The cauterization with water medicine is such that you squeeze a sweet almand from the peel and scrape off the skin and dip it into the shoulder in two places, and then put the poultice made of cotton in butter on it as long as possible; and then, when it has been there for twelve or thirteen hours, take it off and treat with garlic poultice, and leave the wound open for two or three days; then put a cotton poultice dipped in butter on it.
Aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues si fai ceu d’aucunes medicines comburans que j’ai escrites ou dozime traitier des medicines comburans.	After the cure of injury as long as it is healthy; and if you see that this one of some burning medicines that I have written or dozed out in the second treatment of burning medicines.
Li cautere de fer si est selonc ceste meniere.	The fire cautery, if done according to this method.
Chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	Heat the cauterizer so that it is hot:
Et est apelez «clos» por ceu que li chief est fait a la forme d’un clo ou il ait I poc de corbeure, et em mileu a une petite apparance; et le met sor le leu dolorous, et tien ta main et trestorne le feir un poc legierement, tant que li moitiez de l’espés dou keur soit arse; et lieve ta main que li artere n’arde, que est defuers, et decorre habundance de sanc.	And call it 'clos' because the head is made in the form of a Clo or there is I poc of curb, and halfway to a small appearance; and put it on the painful place, and hold your hand and turn the fire slightly, until half of the pain of the cure is burned; and remove your hand that the artery does not burn, which is gone, and run abundance of blood.
Aprés met coton en awe de seil, et met sor le leu par III jors; puis i met coton moilliet em burre, et puis cure le leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vuelz cauterize ceste emigraine avec le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare», a tout la pointe, et te garde de coper l’artere en ceste emigraine qui n’est mie anciaine.	After put cotton in the place, and put it on for III days; then I put wet cotton in butter, and then cure the painful place with injury as long as it is healthy; and if you want to cauterize this headache with the cauterizer that is called 'cultellare', at all points, and keep away from capping the artery in this headache which is not old.
de emigraine	of migraine
Quant tu cures emigraine si com nos avons devant dit en divisions des maladies, et ne profite mie, et vois que li cauteres devant dis de la medicine et dou fer ne li soffit mie, adonques covient il que tu eschaufes le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare» tant qu’il soit blans; et seigne ainsois sor le leu doillant une ligne de demi doi de lonc, et oste ta main une fois, et l’estrain que tu ne coper l’artere et que ne viegnes jusc’a l’os; et te warde de la mandibule que muet quant on menjut, et li ners n’ait regart que la muet et que spasmus ne veigne a malaide, et te warde de decorrement de sanc de l’artere quant elle sera copee, ou copement ait grant paour et meismement a celui que ne s’i conoit, et qui n’est estudians et esprovez; et laisse l’uevre em mi voie; mais je vos dirai coment on restainche sanc quant li artere est copee, et je vos mostrerai a leu ou il afiert en cest livre.	When you treat migraine, as we have said before in the division of diseases, and do not benefit from it, and see that the cautery mentioned before, made with fire, does not suit him, then it is necessary that you heat the cautery called "cultellare" until it is white; and sign thereon on the pain a line half an inch long, and lift your hand once, and squeeze it so that you do not cover the artery and do not come to the bone; and guard the jaw that mutates when he swallows, and let the rest be as it is, and that the spasm does not come to the disease, and guard the detachment of the blood from the artery when it is cut, or has a great fear and least known by those who are students and proven; and leave the work in its place; but I will tell you how to stop pain when the artery is cut, and I will show you where it comes in this book.
Et se tu vois que cist cauteres ne soffise mie a la maladie, et li malaides est soffrans, cauterize le enmi le chief ausi com nos avons dit, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et se tu vues, aministre le cautere que nos avons dit ou chapistre de l’estraction de l’artere, avec le cautere qui ait II coutelz; et est cist cauteres millors de celui et plus aidans.	And if you see that this fire cautery does not suit the disease, and the patient is suffering, cauterize him with a knife at the base as we have said, and cure the wound until it heals; and if you see, administer the cautery that we have said, or the extract of the artery, with the cautery that has two knives; and this cautery is better than that and more helpful.
de la dolor des oreilles de part froidor	The pain in the ears from cold
Quant en l’oreille vient dolor de froit, et on i a ovreit de medicines solutives et des autres cures que nos avons dit en la division, et li dolors ne se muet, adonques eschaufe cest cautere qui est apelez «poins», de coi ci est li forme:	When there is pain in the ears from cold, and one has applied dissolved medicines and other treatments that we have mentioned in the section on division, and the pain does not subside, then apply this fire cautery, which is called "poins", whose form is as follows:
Aprés pointoie tout entor l’oreille malaide, ou entor les II se la dolor tient en ambedous, et t’esloigne un poc ensus de la racine de l’oreille puis que tu as signiet le leu d’enche; et ait X poins entor chescune oreille; aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	After applying the fire cautery around the entire ear that is hurting, or around both ears where the pain is located at the ear lobe, and moving away from the root of the ear as you have found the sensitive spot; make X points around each ear; after this, cure the area until it is healed.
de la torture de la bouche	of the torture of the mouth
Torture qui doit estre curee par cautere nen est fuers que de celles que muevent de fleume, si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladie; et ne faire point de cautere as semblances que vienent de sechor et de spame de ners.	Which must be cured by fire, is only that which moves from fluome, as we have said in the division of diseases; and not to make fire at the appearances which come from scorch and spume of fish.
Quant tu cures ceste semblance de torture qui muet de fleume d’ydres et d’espurgemens de chief et de gargarisme, et ceu ne vaut, adonc covient que tu cauterizes le malaide de III cauteres: l’une en la racine de l’oreille, et l’autre un poc defuers la temple, et le tier en l’ajostement des II levres; et met le cautere en la partie qui apert saine, et li fai cautere endroit le chief de l’oreille desus un poc desoz la corne dou chief, et un autre en la temple ausi longe com uns poce; et laisse le cautere tant sus que li moitiez dou keur soit arse; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	When you cure this appearance of torture which moves from fluome of the head and gargling, and this does not work, then you should make three cauterizations: one in the root of the ear, and another a little further down the temple, and the third in the joining of the two lips; and place the fire in the part which is healthy, and let it burn half of what has been heated; and this is the form of the fire:
Et est li semblance dou cutellaire que nos avons mise devant, mais il est un poc plus subtilz et covient que li coutelz soit un poc plus gros; aprés cure lou leu si com j’ai devant dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And it is the appearance of the cuttlefish that we have put in front, but it is a little more subtle and it is necessary that the knife be a little thicker; after treatment the place as I said before, until it is healthy.
Quant apoplexie est ancieinne et tu la cures ensi com nos avons dit, et il ne profite mie, et li malaides n’ait fievre, adonques li fai IIII cauteres: II sus les II cornes dou chief, et I emmi le chief, et I ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz» si com nos avons devant dit, et lou derrien cautere sus la bouche de l’estomac; et soit curez si com nos avons dit devant.	When apoplexy is old and you treat it in this way as we have said, it does not benefit, and the patient has no fever, then do IV cauterizations: II on the II horns of the head, and I cut off the head, and I put it out, which is called a "vessel", as we have said before, and the last cauterization on the mouth of the stomach; and let it be cured in this way as we have said before.
de litargie	of lime
A cest maladie covient doner au malaide yeres grans et pilules mondifians le cerveil; aprés reis lou chief dou malaide tout, et li met sus l’occipite l’emplaustre de sinapi qui est escrit ou traitier des emplastres; et c’est li maniere dou cautere: si lou fai si com j’ai dit.	For this disease it is necessary to give the patient many great and pilules medicinals to the brain; after re-shaping the head of the patient, put on the occiput the dye of saffron which is written or made into pills; and this is the way of cauterizing: do so as I have said.
S’il est sanez ensi, boin est; et s’il ne l’est, se li fai III cauteres des emmi le chief en dessendant jusc’a col, et ait d’espaice entre chescun cautere I doi de gros; et le cure si com les autres, et se tu i vues ajoster, et li malaides est soffrans, se li fai I cautere en mileu; et se mestiers est, II autres sus les II cornes, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «olivare», si com j’ai devant dit.	If he is well here, it is good; and if not, three fire cauteries of the head at the root, leaving space between each one of two inches in length; and cure him as with the others, and if you see them stir, the patient suffers, do one cautery in the middle; and if the business is done, two more on the two horns, and cure him until he is well; and let the cauteries which are called 'olive' be done, as I have said before.
de la froidor dou chief	of the head
Il covient que li chief soit mundifiez de yeres et de ceu que nos avons devant dit; aprés reis le chief dou malaide, puis li fai cautere emmi le chief et sus chescune corne, et I derrier et III sus l’espinee dou col; et se tu en as plus mestier, et li cors est moiste et li malaides est soffrans, et li maladie est fors, se li fai IIII cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos; et li laisse tant que li plus dou keur soit ars, et lieve ta main; aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «olivare» que nos avons devant dit.	It is necessary that the head be washed and cleaned of dirt and everything that we have said before; then, when you wash the head of the patient, make a fire cautery at the root of the hair, leaving space between each one of two inches in length; and cure him as with the others, and if you see them stir, the patient suffers, and let one cautery be done in the middle; and if the business is done, two more on the two horns, and cure him until he is well; and let the cauteries which are called 'olive' be done, as we have said before.
de l’epilempsie	of epilepsy
Li epilentiques ne doit useir de cautere fuers que cil qui est fleumatique, et covient premier mondifier le cerveil de yeres et d’autres cures que nos avons dites en la division quant li malaides est grans et soffrans de penre medicine.	For those who have epilepsy, the fire cautery should only be used if they are feverish; first, it is necessary to wash the skull and then to administer other remedies that we have described in the section on treatment when the patient is severe and suffering from fever.
Et se c’est uns enfes qui ne lou puisse soffrir, se li fai gargarisme et mastication mondifiant le cerveil sovent avec bones viandes; aprés li reis lou chief em mileu, et i fai I cautere selonc ce que nos avons dit devant, et I cautere sus lou vassel, et sus chescune corne; et se li malaides est fors et soffrans, se li fai cauteres si com j’ai dit a celui qui ait paralisie et mollification de cors, sus l’espinee dou dos et dou col, et soit li cauteres olivier selonc la maniere que j’ai dit.	And if it is a child who cannot tolerate the pain, make gargling and chewing to wash out the skull regularly with good meat; after that, place the skull in water, and perform the cauterization as we have described above, and cauterize the neck and each horn; and if the patient is feverish and suffering, perform the cauterization as I have said for those who are paralyzed and have a softening of the limbs, on the spine of the back and the neck, and make the olive cauterization according to the method that I have described.
Se li malaides est enfes, se li fai I cautere subtil selonc ceste maniere:	If the patient is ill, then make the fire cautery according to this method:
Quant par la cause de melancolie sunt les superfluitez ou les moistors corrumpues et fleume grosse, adonques lou cauterize de teils cauteres com nos avons dit a celui qui ait paralisie.	When due to melancholy there are excesses or corrupt and thick moisture, then you make the fire cautery in parts as we have said to one who has paralysis.
Et se par la cause de melancolie est li superfluitez declinans a melancolie, et est li cors dou malaide moistes, adonc li done a boivre chose par coi li cervelz soit mundifiez, selonc ceu qu’il est devant en la division.	And if due to melancholy is the decline of excesses to melancholy, and the patient's body is moist, then he should drink something so that the brain is purified, according to what is before it in the division.
Aprés reis lou chief dou malaide; aprés fai I torteil de lin bien fait, ausi com I cercle, si le met emmi le chief; et li malaides sié croisiez, et soit bien tenus de toutes pars; aprés presente le linement, et vaut mues de burre de berbis ancien; et lou chaufe a feu tempreement, si que li dois s’on li boute le puisse soffrir; aprés vuide le cercle par dedens emmi le chief, et lou laisse refroidier; et fai ce a malaide chescune semaine une fois avec autre governement boin, tant qu’il soit sanez.	After carefully considering the head of the patient; then make a well-made turban of linen, also as a circle, so place it on the head; and let the patient lie comfortably in bed; after this present the unguentation, and apply hot oil of old castor beans; and let the turban cool down; and do this to the patient once every week with good order, until he is well.
Ou se tu vues cauterize lou en faisant poins plusors a tot le cautere.	If you see him cauterize himself by making many punctures all over his body.
Ceste maniere de cautere amoistit le cerveil igaument; et puis met sus coton moilliet en burre et en graisse de geline.	This way of cauterizing moistens the skull and then puts cotton wetted with bur and goat's fat on it.
de l’awe des eulz	of the hair
Quant awe vient premierement as eulz par les signes que j’ai dit en la division, adonques encomence et done boivre au malaide chose mundifiant le chief, et le warde de toutes moistors, et lou fai suer ou bain plusors fois a jeun.	When it comes first to the hair by the signs that I have said in the division, then begin and make the patient sweat or bathe many times on an empty stomach;
Aprés li comande a rere son chief, et li fai cautere emmi le chief, et li fai II cauteres sus les II temples se li dessendemens de l’awe est as II eulz ensamble, ou en I se li dessendemens est en I; et cope a tout le cautere toutes les voines et les arteres que sont desoz le keur, et soient li cautere lonc selon lou large de la temple; et te warde de decorrement de sanc, et se tu vois trop de sanc issir, si li estainche de teil pooir com tu as.	After that he orders him to run his hand over his head, and makes him cauterize his head, and makes two cauterization on the temples according to the width of the head; and guards against a fever rising, and if you see too much blood coming out, then stop it with a cloth.
Et je t’enseignerai en l’estraction des arteres et a l’incision la cautele coment tu l’estencheras; et aucune fois fait on cautere ou hatereil desoz les II os derrier.	And I will teach you how to cauterize the arteries and how to cut them with caution, and never cauterize or sear the two bones behind.
dou cors des larmes	the heart of tears
Quant les larmes des eulz sont ancienes et acostumees et sont sus les voines, ou delez les arteres que sont en l’aparance dou chief defors; et on voit que c’est des superfluitez froides fleumatiques, adonques li fai le cautere que j’ai dit en l’encomencement de l’awe dessendant as eulz: I cautere emmi le chief, et II cauteres sus les II temples, et II cauteres ou haiterel desoz les II os; et s’il i a besoigne plus, si le cauterize saigement desus le sorcil a tout I petit cautere.	When the tears of the eyes are old and accustomed and lie in the veins, or cauterize the arteries which are in appearance at the top of the head; and one can see that it is of cold, phlegmatic superfluity, therefore I do the cautery that I have said at the beginning of the awaking of the blood flowing out from the eyes: I cauterize the top, and two cauterizes over the two temples, and two cauterizes where haters lie the two bones; and if it is necessary more, if he cauterizes carefully above the palate with all small cautery.
dou cors des larmes par dedens les eulz	the heart of tears within the eyes
Quant tu le medicines selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et il ne profite mie, adonques done a boivre a malaide III nuis cochies; aprés li reis le chief, et li fai cautere ou mileu dou cautere olivaire; et fai II cauteres dou cautere qui est apelez «clavilis» sus les II sorcis, un poc desoz les chevous; et te warde de l’artere que tu ne la coper.	When you have the medicine according to what we said in the division, and it does not benefit, then done three times drink the drug of sickness III; after he takes the head, and make a cautery in the middle of the cautery olive; and do II cauteries of the cautery that is called "clavilis" on the II points, a little shampoo the hair; and guard the artery so you do not cover it.
Et c’est li forme dou cautere qui est apelez «clavilis»:	This is the form of the cautery that is called "clavilis":
Quant li papiere de l’oil est mollifie de maladie et de moistor, adonques la cautarize de cest cautere qui est apelez «olivare».	When the paper of the oil is softened with disease and moisture, then the cauterization of this cautery that is called "olive".
de coi ci est li forme:	so that this is the form:
Et se tu vues si fai II cauteres sus les II sorcis ausi lons com li sorcilz sont; et n’i lassiez mie la main fors que tant que li tierce partie de la papiere soit arse, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit.	And if you see that you do II cauteries on the II points as long as the points are; and do not leave your hand off until the third part of the paper is burned, according to the way I have said.
dou poil qui point l’oil	dou poil qui point l’oil
Aucune fois avient que li poil des oilz sont convertit au pardedens, et poignent l’oil, et i fait on cauteres selonc II manieres: c’est a savoir de feu, ou de medicine ardant.	For the hair that points to the oil, and when they touch the oil, it is done with two methods: that is to say, by fire or by burning medicine.
Ou cautere de feu comande au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient lons et igals; et s’il le poignent a lor nassance, se li estraint les eulz qu’il ne se muevent tant qu’il naissent.	For the fire cautery, instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even; and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
Quant il naissent et i sont igalz, adonques met le malaide en ton sain; aprés seigne sus la papiere des eulz une figure que soit ausi com li fuelle dou mirte, et soit li comencemens dou signe delez les poilz; puis i met coton moilliet en glaire d’uef et muscillaige de persillion sus l’oil, puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	When they grow and are equal, then put the patient to your head; after that, sign on the paper of the eyes a figure that is also like the furrow of the apple of the ear, and this is the beginning of the mark of the hairs; then put cotton wet in wax and muscatel of persillion on the oil, then heat the cautery so that it is this form:
Aprés cauterize sus la figure que tu as signiet poc et poc mout de fois, que li keurs soit ars lai endroit; et li signes de la santeit de l’uevre est que tu voies la papiere retraite, et les poilz levez a la pointure de l’oil; adonques lieve ta main, et laisse ensi III jors, puis i met coton moilliet en burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	After you have cauterized the figure little by little many times, so that the scar is burned in place; and the signs of the health of the work are that you see the paper retreat, and the hairs rise to the length of the oil; then gently lift your hand, and leave it like this for III days, then put cotton soaked in milk in a pad until the scorching is gone; after the cure of wound dressing as long as it is healed.
Et se aprés ceu vienent li poilz, et li papiere est mollifie adonques rencomence le cautere sus cel leu meisme, si com tu as fait premiers; et se li poil sont defuer, si le cauterize tant que li papiere soit levee a son leu natureil, et soit igals, et ne poignent mie li poil l’oil.	And if after these come the hairs, and the paper is softened then start again the cautery on that middle level, as you did before; and if the hairs are gone, then cauterize until the paper returns to its natural level, and is even, and do not touch the hair with the oil.
Li cauteres de medicine ardant est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient grans et igalz, puis fai de parchemin la forme de la foille de mirte; puis pren de savon fransois et de vive chalz, de chescun une .З., et broie ensamble bien; et le fai hastanment, si qu’il ne refroide, puis en espant sus la forme que tu es fait sicom la foille dou mirte, et met sus la papiere des eulz; et se li maladie tient en I oil soulement, si doit on ovrer en I, et se en ambedous ausi; et met desoz l’oil coton moilliet en abin d’uef; et li chiés dou malaide soit en ton sain et met ton doi mostrant sus la medicine, et presse I poc et lou muef toutes les fois que li malaide sent mordication de la medicine, car il sent mordication ausi com de feu.	The medical cautery of burning is that you command the patient to let the hairs grow long and even, then make from parchment the shape of a fern; then take French soap and hot water, each of 1/4, and grind them together well; and do it hurriedly, so that it does not cool down again, then spread on the paper with the eyes; and if the disease only comes out in one oil, then must be done in one also, and both at once; and put cotton soaked in milk in an oven; and the patient's joint should be in your hand, and place your thumb on the medicine, and press it little by little each time the patient feels tingling from the medicine, for he feels tingling too like fire.
Quant tu as ceu fait longement, si oste la medicine a ton doit.	Once you have had this for a long time, keep the medicine in your mouth.
Et quant li mordication sera passee, si leve le leu d’awe, et rewarde se tu vois la papiere levee ausi com s’ele estoit levee par constraignement de feu ou par incision; et s’il est ensi, si est bien.	And when the pain has passed, raise the shoulder up, and test whether you can see the bone raised as if it had been lifted by fire or by incision; and if so, it is good.
Se ceu non, si remet encor de la medicine sus lou leu ou li medicine n’ait ovreit, tant que tes ovraiges soit igalz, et tes eulz mis a point; puis met sus coton moilliet en burre tant que li keurs ars soit cheus, aprés cure le leu de l’oignement qui est apelez «dyafenis» et d’autre, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If not, put more medicine on the spot where the medicine has not worked, as long as your hairs are long and even, and your eyes steady; then put cotton wetted in vinegar on the sore, after which cure the injury called 'diapnis' and others, until it is healed.
Et se t’est mestier que tu te warde bien a ton ovraige par grant warde qu’il ne chiece point de la medicine as eulz.	And if you must care for your injury with great caution so that the medicine does not cause any harm to your hairs.
Et se li papiere devient mole aprés, et li poil poignent en l’oil, si recomence la medicine sus celui leu qui est mollifiez de la papiere proprement, ensi com tu as fait devant; aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et c’est li forme de la fuelle dou mirte:	And if the paper becomes soft, and the hair pricks into the oil, then begin again with the medicine on the same spot which has become soft from the paper, in the same way as you have done before; after which cure it until it is healed; and this is the method of the powder of mirabille.
Et saichés que li eul des homes sont divers en grandor et en petitece, et selonc ceu soit tes constraignemens; et ne soit mie reponue li droite voie a celui cui est li estude de cest art.	And know that the eyes of men are different in size and shape, and according to this, their measurements should be taken; and do not go against the natural order of things in this matter.
de la cure de fistule par cautere	Of the treatment of fistulas by cauterization:
Quant tu cures fistule si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladies, et tes cures ne profitent mie, adonques covient il que tu li fais cautere selonc ceste maniere.	When you treat a fistula as we have explained in the division of diseases, and your treatments do not benefit them, then it is necessary that you perform cauterization according to this method.
Comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain; et teigne li menistres son chief entre tes mains en teil maniere qu’il ne se mueve, ne ne demoinne son chief; aprés met coton moilliet en abin d’uef ou en jus de persillion sus l’oil; aprés chaufe le cautere qui est teilz: et est chevez au chief si com li forme d’une penne de vouteul, ensamble la queil soit li cautere; se tu vues, si soit apointé des l’un chief dusc’a l’autre, et se tu vues, si soit ausi com une tente; mais toutevoie, cist qui est chevez vaut mues por ton ovraige.	 Instruct the patient to place his head in your lap; and dunk the hairpins in a bowl of melted wax or juice of blackberry jam on oil; then heat the cauterizer gradually; and put it to the scalp as if it were the shape of a feather, together with the hairpin; if you see, then aim for one hair at a time from one side of the head to the other, and if you cannot see, then do it like a tent; but in any case, this that is placed on top should be moved for your work.
Aprés presse la fistule s’ele est overte, et en trai la porriture, et la seche; et s’ele est close, si la oevre, et trai fuers la bowe; aprés met sus le cautere chaut forment, et tien ta main au cautere a la partie dou neif ensus de l’oil, que ta mains ne faice folie; et met le cautere en la graisse de l’oil, et la corromp.	After compressing the fistula is opened, and treat it with sweat, and dry it out; and if it's closed, then operate, and firmly hold the blade; after place the hot cautery very closely, and keep your hand on the cautery in the part that goes above the oil, so that your hands don't go wild; and place the cautery into the fat of the oil, and corrupt it.
Se tu viens au comencement dou cautere jusc’a l’os, si serait bien.	If you come to the beginning of the cauterizing only just to the bone, that would be good.
Se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere encor une fois, et autre se tu en as mestier, et le laisse III jors; aprés i met sus coton moilliet en burre, et lou cure de l’oignement desiccatif tant qu’il soit sanez, et se XL jors passent qu’il ne soit sanez, si met sus medicine ague corrosive tant que li os soit descovers; et lou reis selonc ceu que il venrait en son chapistre.	If not, then start cauterizing again, and if you need to do it more, and let it sit for III days; after put cotton wet in oil on it, and treat the infected area with dry medicine until it is well, and if it takes XL days that it isn't well, then put a corrosive oil on it, and mend it according to what came out in the chapter.
Et i a une maniere de cautere de fistule que aucun des anciens dirent.	And there is a way of cauterizing fistulas which none of the ancients said.
Entens a fistule, et fens le leu; aprés met en la fendure I camahan subtil de coi ci est li forme:	Hear me on a way to cauterize a fistula, something that no ancient writer has mentioned. After you've opened the site, place a very thin blade in the opening to ensure it is shaped correctly:
et i font a la quantiteit d’une .З. de plonc; et tien ta main ou camahan fermement, et ne se mueve li malaides nes point, que li plons fondus ne corre a son oil; et covient c’on mette sus l’oil a malaide coton moilliet en abin d’uefz ou en awe: li plonc si art lou leu de fistule, et lou saine per mervillouse saniteit.	Take a quantity of melting wax and hold it firmly in your hand so that the wax does not move at all, so that the melted wax does not flow onto the oil; and you should put cotton wicks in water or in ash where there is oil: the wax applied thus wonderfully heals the fistula, and cures with miraculous health.
Et se li fistule est sanee per le cautere que nos avons dit, c’est boin.	If the fistula has been cured by the cauterization that we have described, it is good.
Se ce non, si covient aministrer pertus au neif, et ramener la fistule au cors dou neif selonc ceu qu’il covient en som propre leu.	If not, then you should administer a sharp instrument to the nose, and bring the fistula to the nose's own place according to that which is fitting in its own place.
des crevaices en levres	The crevices in the lips
Mout de fois avienent crevaices en levres que sont apelees «poil», et meismement en levres des enfans.	The mouths of times have had crevices in the lips that are called "hair", and most often in the lips of children.
Quant tu cures ces crevaices de ceu que nos avons dit en divisions, et li cure ne profite, adonques eschaufe I petit cautere cultellaire selonc ceste forme:	When you treat these crevices as we have said in the divisions, and the cure does not take effect, then heat a small surgical scalpel according to this form:
Et le met hastanment en celles crevaices tant qu’il viegne jusc’a font; aprés cure le leu de cerote tant qu’il soit sanez.	And put it carefully in those crevices until it comes out; then clean the area with cauterizing liquid as long as it is clean.
de l’aposteme de la goule	of the abscess of the throat
Quant apostume vient en la racine de la goule ou en l’uve, ou ou palais, ou as racines des dens, aprés fait porriture et ront et est enveillis et devient fistule; et tu le cures si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie: adonques covient il que tu aies I cautere selonc la quantiteit de la fistule; aprés le bote ou pertus de la fistule, et tien ta main tant que li fer chaus viegne au font de li, et ou derrien leu; et fai ensi une fois ou II, aprés le cure de ce que nos avons dit en cures, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il est curez ensi, c’est boin; et se ceu non, si covient descovrir le leu et oster l’os corrumput, selonc ceu que vos le troverez en son chapistre.	When the abscess comes in the root of the throat or in the larynx or at the roots of the teeth, after having made pustules and rot and it becomes a fistula; and you treat it as we have said in the divisions, but it does not benefit: then you must have fire according to the quantity of the fistula; after having boiled or pierced the fistula, and holding your hand until the iron comes out at its root, and doing so once or twice, after treating it as we have said in the treatments, until it is healthy; and if it is cured in this way, it is good; and if not, then you must uncover the place and cut off the corrupted bone, according to what you will find in his chapter.
dou movement des dens	the movement of teeth
Quant les gencives sont mollifies par moistor et les dens muevent, et tu le cures per medicines et ceu ne vaut, adonc met le chief dou malaide en ton sain; aprés eschaufe le cautere dont li forme venra ci aprés en teil maniere que tu mettes une cainne sor le dent; et met dedens le cautere chaut hastanment, et tien tant ta main que li malaides sente la chalor venant a la racine dou dent; aprés lieve ta main et rencomence le cautere selonc ta volenteit; aprés emplisse li malaides sa bouche d’awe salee, et la teigne une houre et raiche fuers.	When the gums are softened by moisture and the teeth move, and you treat it with medicines, then place the head of the patient in your lap; then heat the cautery until its form comes out in this way that you put a string on the tooth; and insert the cautery hotly inside, and hold your hand so that the patient feels the heat coming to the root of the tooth; then release your hand and repeat the cautery according to your will; then fill the patient's mouth with salt water, and leave it for an hour and wash it.
Et en teil maniere li dens qui estoit movans si est confermez, et li gencive mollifie restrainte, et li moistors corrumpue sechie.	And in this way the tooth that was moving is fixed, and the gums that were softened are tightened, and the moisture that had corrupted it is dried up.
de la dolor des dens	of tooth pain
Quant dolor de dens vient por froidor, ou il i a froidor ou veir, et les cures de medicine ne valent, adonc i ait mestier de cautere selonc II manieres: et cautere de burre et cautere de feu.	When toothache comes from cold, or there is coldness or fever, and medicines do not help, then there are two ways to treat it: the fire cautery and the butter cautery.
Cautere de burre si est telz que tu preignes burre de vaiche, et le bout en une cuillier de fer ou d’arain; aprés pren coton et envolope sus la pointe d’une tente, et la moille en burre bulit, et met sus le dent dolant hastanment et tien tant qu’il soit refroidiez; et ensi fai sovent tant que sa vertus viegne a la racine de la dent, et se tu vues si moille laine et coton en burre froit, et met sus le dent doillant, et met sus I fer chaut tant que li feus viegne au chevement dou dent.	Cautery with butter if it is such that you squeeze butter from a goat, and the tip in a spoon of iron or brass; after take cotton and wrap over the tip of a tent, and the moist in butter melted, and put on the tooth aching gently and keep until it has cooled down; and so often as its virtue comes to the root of the tooth, and see if such wet cotton and wool in butter frozen, and put on the aching tooth, and put on a iron hot as the fire comes to the root of the tooth.
Li cauteres ensamble feu si est telz que tu preignes uns cainne de fer ou d’arain, et soit grosse si que li feus ne viegne a la bouche dou malaide; aprés chaufe le cautere, de coi li forme venra ci aprés, et le met sus le dent et tien ta main tant que li cauteres soit refroidiez; fai ceu sovent, car li dolor sera ostee celui jor meisme ou l’endemain.	Cautery with fire if it is such that you squeeze a iron bar or a brass one, and it is thick so that the fire does not come to the mouth of the patient; after heat the cautery, so that it becomes cold then put it on the tooth and hold your hand until the cautery has cooled down; do this often because the pain will be intense the next day or the day after.
Et covient que li malaides emplisse sa bouche de boin burre en l’empressement de cel cautere, et puis le raiche fuer; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	And it is necessary that the patient fill his mouth with good butter in the application of this fire cautery, and then eat it up; and this is the form of the cautery.
Et fai cautere dou queil chief que tu voudras, et selonc ceu que tu as pooir; et c’est li forme de la caine:	And make the cautery on the head as you will, and according to what power you have; and this is the form of the cane:
des scrophules	from the scalp
Quant les scrophules sont de fleume et de moistors froides, et ne sont obeissans a digestion par medicines, adonques eschaufe le cautere cheveit de coi ci aprés vient li forme, et ait II aovertures por les fumees a issir au cautere de l’autre partie; et met le cautere chaut sus l’apostume une fois, ou II se mestier est, tant qu’il viegne au font de l’apostume; et se li apostume est petis si met cautere selonc la quantiteit de l’apostume, et le laisse ensi III jors; et met sus coton moilliet em burre tant que li arsure soit ostee; aprés cure le leu d’oignemens et de tentes tant qu’il soit sanez. Li forme de la cainne:	The shape of the cane:
Quant les moistors vainquent sus les chenals dou pormon, et meismement quant ce vient de froide complexion, adonc covient que li malaides soit voidiez premiers par medicines solutives; aprés li fai cautere a la racine de la gorge, et te garde que tu ne venir mie jusc’a la gorge, et n’ardre dou keur mais c’un poc.	When the moisture prevails over the cheeks and especially when it comes from cold complexion, then it is appropriate that the patient be first voided by soluble medicines; afterwards, a fire cautery is made at the root of the throat, and you must not come up to the throat, and dare only to touch a little.
Aprés li fai I autre cautere a la jointure dou col au chief de l’espinee, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» de coi nos avons la forme devant; et cure le leu si com nos avons devant dit tant qu’il soit sanez.	Afterwards, another fire cautery is made at the joint of the neck to the head of the spine, and let be the cauteries which are called 'clavicles' from which we have the form before; and heal the place as we have said before until it is healthy.
de la toust	of the toast

de la menoison	from the hospital
Quant solution de ventre vient de froidor et de moistor, tant que li vertus retentive et digestive qui est ou stomac et en l’intestine est afleboie, et ne puet estre curez par manieres de cures; et tu vois le malaide bien soffrant et de fort vertut, si fai I grant cautere sus l’estomac selonc ceu qu’il en a parleit ci devant ou cautere de l’estomac, au cautere circule; et IIII cauteres entor la boude subtilz a tout I cautere clavile subtil, et II cauteres sus les hainches.	When the solution of the stomach comes from cold and moisture, as long as the virtues that remain in it and digest in the stomach are affloated, and cannot be cured by any means of treatment; and you see the patient very ill and of great virtue, so do I make a great cauterization on the stomach according to what he has spoken before or the cauterization of the stomach, circulating; and four cauterizations around the navel finely in all cauterizations, and two cauterizations on the hips.
Et se tu vois les moistors habundans et le malaide soffrant, se li fai cautere sus le poignil, et I cautere sus chaicun yle, et II petis cauteres sus l’estomac delez le grant, car li cure est profitans quant il i a bone aide.	And if you see the moistures abundant and the patient suffering, make a cautery on the hand, and a cautery on each finger, and two small cauteries in the stomach, for the cure is profitable when there is good help.
de la cure des emorroydes	for the cure of hemorrhoids
Quant les emorroydes sont ou fondement, ou une ou plusors, et sont ancienes et sont de grosses humors froides et moistes corrumpues, et sont curees si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie, si fai cauteres: III sus l’espine dou dos, celi qui est tout defuers desoz almecdate poc et poc en triangulant, et I cautere desoz la boude II dois; et se tu penses que ses estomac soit refroidiez, et li viande ne cuise, et on voit enfler la faice, adonques li faice on I grant cautere sus le stomac, si com il est devant dit, et I autre sus le foie, et I autre sus la mice a tout le cautere clavile; et laisse le cautere overt lonc tens. Aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	After treatment, let it rest until it is healthy again.
de la charnositeit qui est nommee «thelul»	of the carnage which is called "thenul
Quant tu copes althelul, si eschaufe le cautere qui semble I raseur, et puis le met tout embraseit sus cel althelul copeit; et i laisse tant ta main que li cauteres viegne a la naissance de la voine, de coi li sans cort; fai ceu une fois ou II, et s’il i a mout d’althelul, si cauterize chaicun si com nos avons dit; aprés les cure d’oignemens profitans tant qu’il soient sanez; et se tu cauterizes d’un cautere grant sus alchatim, si avra plus grant aide.	When treating the carnage (thenul), if it is hot, use a fire cautery and burn it until it heals; then treat with oils that benefit it until it is healthy again; and if you treat with a large cautery on the skin, it will be more effective. Do this once or twice, and if there is much carnage, as we have said, use a fire cautery; after treating with beneficial oils until they are healthy; and if you treat with a large cautery on the skin, it will be more effective.
de plaie mal curee	of wounds not properly treated
Quant li malaides ne puet soffrir tailleure ne overture, que nos raconterons en son leu, si vient teil maladie que ne puet estre sanee fuer que par cautere.	When the patient cannot tolerate a wound being sutured or opened, which we will describe in its own time, then comes a disease that cannot be healed except by cauterization.
Quant a aucun vient fistule, et est enveillie et giete porriture et moistors corrumpues, si la doies prover a tot une tente subtil, et garde que tu saiches a tot la tente combien elle a de parfont.	When there is no opening for the wind, and it has become inflamed and covered with pus and moisture, if you give it an extensive treatment, and be careful that you know exactly how much of the treatment is enough.
Aprés eschaufe le cautere qui semble I raseur, et le boute en la fistule selonc la quantiteit que li tente i est entrée, et rencomence lou cautere tant que cil cors porris et corrumpus soient ars, une fois, ou II ou III, selonc la quantiteit de som besoing; et te warde d’ardre lé nerf qui sunt enqui, et des grans voinnes.	After you have heated the cauterizer that seems like a razor, and you pour it into the fistula according to the quantity that the tent has entered, and restart the cauterization as long as those corroded and corrupted parts are burned, once or twice, according to the quantity of medicine needed; and be careful not to harm the nerves that are nearby, and great veins.
se li fistule vait au cors de la vesie et a l’intestine, si te warde de ces leus, et ne faire ceu fuers que en leu charnut, et pense qu’ele n’est mie persans; aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez, et se li leus est saielez, et les matieres sont ostees lonc tens, adonc saiches que li leus est sanez entierement; et se les matieres ne sont ostees, saiche que li leus est troez, et corrumpus li os au font; et ensi com un de ces que nos dirons en son leu.	If the fistula goes into the belly and intestines, be careful of these parts, and do not do any surgery except in the charned area, and think that it is not dangerous; then cure that area as long as it is healthy, and if the area has healed, and the matter has been dried up for a long time, then know that the area is completely cured; and if the matter has not dried up, know that the area has become three parts, and the bone is corrupted at the bottom; and thus, as one of these things that we will say in its place.
de la maladie des reins	of the disease of the kidneys
Quant dolor de froit vient as rains, et de grosse ventositeit, et ne prent talant de femme, adonc covient il que tu li fais cautere sus les rains d’une part et d’autre au cautere clavile que nos avons devant dit; et se nos le cauterizons em mileu, si avra III cauteres en ligne, et se feront plus grant aide.	When the pain of the kidneys comes with a strong wind and does not respond to treatment from women, then you should make a fire cautery on each kidney from side to side with the clove cauterizer that we have mentioned above; and if we apply it in the middle, there will be three cauterizations in a line, and it will do more good.
de la vessie	of the bladder
Quant li vessie est mole et foible de froit et de moistor, si que li malaides retient l’urine, adonc li fai cautere en la partie defuers sus la vessie, la ou encomencent li poil dou poignil, et I a destre et I a senestre, et soit chescuns cauteres si lons com li nous d’un poce; et li fais I cautere defuers le dos, ou II se tu en as besoing; et soit li cauteres clavile selon la forme devant dite.	When the bladder is soft and weak due to cold and moisture, causing the patient to retain urine, then you should make a fire cautery in the area behind the bladder, where the hair grows on the penis, and do so on both sides, making each cauterization as long as one of your fingers; and you should also make a fire cautery behind, where it is needed; and let the cauterizations be clove-shaped according to the form described above.
de la marris	of the mare
Quant li marrix est froide et moiste, et ne laisse mie por ceu a concevoir, et les flors sont corrumpues et lor termines tarde; et quant elles vienent, si sent grant dolor: adonques covient il c’on li faice III cauteres entor la boude, si com nos avons dit ou cautere de la vessie, et II cauteres defuers le dos; et soit li cauteres clavile, si com nos avons dit.	When the marriage bed is cold and moist, and does not allow for conception, and the flowers are rotten and late in blooming; and when they do come, it causes great pain: then three cauterizations should be performed around the loins, as we said in the cauterization of the bladder, and two cauterizations at the back; and the cauterizations should be claved, as we have said.
de la hainche	of the hips
Quant les moistors viscouses dessendent a la boiste de la hainche, et por ceste cause si se muet de son leu, et li signes est que li cuisse est plus longe que li autre quant on le mesure ensamble; et est trovez li leus dou departement vuis, si covient que tu cauterizes le malaide sus la boiste de la hainche a I cautere semblant au cercle, et seigne devant le leu entor la boiste si com elle torne, si que li boiste soit dedens le cercle; et si soit li cauteres telz com cil dont on a cauterizeit le stomac.	When the viscous moisture descends into the hip cavity, and for this reason it moves out of place, and the sign is that the thigh is farther away from the other when measured together; and the joints are found to be sore, then you should perform a seemingly circular cauterization on the malaide [patient] in the hip cavity, and sign in front of the joint as she turns, so that the cavity is within the circle; and if so, the cauterization should be like those we have spoken of for the stomach.
Et se cist cauteres ne t’est presens, se li fai III cauteres de l’olivaire grans, et soit li cauteres ausi parfont com tous li keurs; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if this fire cautery is not present with you, make three cauterizations with the olive oil, and let the cauterizations also be complete like all the others; and treat it until it is well.
de la dolor de la hainche	of the pain of the hip
Quant dolor vient en la boiste de la hainche, et c’est de froidor et de moistor, et li malaides est curez de ceu que nos avons dit en la division et li cure ne vaut, et li maladie est anciene: adonc covient il que tu purges le malaide des grosses humors de pilules fetides, ou autres pilules bones semblans.	When the pain comes in the hip joint, and it is from cold and moisture, and the patient is cured of what we have said in the division, and the cure does not work, and the disease is old: then you must purge the patient with large pills of fetid humors, or other bad-looking pills.
Aprés li fai cautere; et li maniere dou cautere si est selonc II manieres: c’est a savoir ensamble medicines ardans, et cautere de feu.	After that, make the cauterization; and the method of the cauterization is as follows: namely, together with burning medicines, and fire cauterization.
Cautere de feu si est selonc mout de manieres, desquelz li uns est telz: que tu cauterize sus la boiste de la hainche III cauteres triangulalz selonc ceste forme, et i fai bone profunditeit et grant, et ait entre chaicun cautere d’espaice la groissece d’un doi, et soit li cauteres olivaire; aucune fois fait on cautere en mileu sus lou chief de la hainche, por coi il en i a IIII selonc ceste forme:	Fire cauterization is according to many methods, some of which are: you make three triangular cauterizations according to this form on the hip joint, and you make them with great depth and width, and there is between each cauterization the thickness of a finger, and you make olive oil cauterizations; you never make cauterizations in the middle on top of the head of the hip joint, for there are four according to this form.
Et se tu vues, si le cauterize au cautere dou cercle que nos avons devant dit en la dislocation de la hainche; mais fai en teil maniere que li cercles conteigne toute la hainche, et tous li espés dou keur soit ars.	And if you see that the cautery at the circle that we have spoken of before in the dislocation of the hip; but do it in such a way that the circles contain all the hip, and all the flesh around the hole is burned.
Et c’est li maniere c’on fait en sciatique, quant li dolor tient en la hainche, et ne parvient mie jusc’a la cuisse ne jusc’a la jambe.	This is how it is done for sciatica, when the pain persists in the hip and does not reach the thigh or leg.
Et s’ele vient jusc’a la cuisse et la jambe, se li fai II cauteres lai ou li malaides dit que li dolor li tient, et I cautere desus la cheville IIII dois, a la partie senestre un poc; et soit li cauteres cutellaire, et soit arse li espesseté dou keur; et se li malaides sent que li dolor s’estende jusc’a dois dou piet ou pres d’enqui, se le cauterize la ou il sent la dolor III poins ou IIII au cautere qui est apelez «poins».	And if it comes up to the thigh and leg, two cauterizations are made where the patient says the pain is felt, and one cauterization above the ankle three times; either cutaneous cauterization or burning the flesh around the hole; and if the patient feels that the pain extends to two or four toes or near the ankle, cauterize there with the "poins" cautery.
Et se mestiers est, se li en fai plus; et se il seit que li dolor soit desoz le genoil vers la cuisse, se li fais cautere au cautere cutellaire ou circulaire, et te done bien garde en tous tes cauteres que tu n’i lassier mie tant le cautere que tu brules les ners et les grans arteres, et que tu ne faices au malaide plus grant nuisance et contraction.	And if he is skilled in this, let him do more; and if he knows that the pain is in the groin toward the thigh, let him make a cautery with a knife or a circular tool, and give him good care in all your cauteries so that you do not let go of the cautery as much as the cautery burns the nerves and large arteries, and do not cause the patient more harm and contraction.
Et je meisme ai veus plusors qui ont fait cautere sus la cheville dou piet, et li lasserent tant que li jambe fut toute enflee, et li piez ausi, et fut perciez et corrumpus toz li piez.	And I have also seen many who have made a cautery on the heel of the foot, and left it so that the leg was all folded up, and the toes too, and it became perforate and corrupt all the toes.
Aprés une solution de ventre dont il ot la mort.	After a solution of the abdomen in which he died.
Et se li dolors est en II parties ensamble, fai cautere en l’une et en l’autre, selonc ceste maniere.	And if the pain is in two parts together, make cautery in one and in the other, according to this manner.
