Et li saige dirent en la cautere de la hainche, de coi ci est li maniere, fai I tel fer et soit au chief ausi gros com uns nauvillon de dacte, ou un poc moins, et soit par entrechetres et soit des l’un entrechetres jusc’a l’autre d’espaice la quantiteit d’un nou de poce; et soient li entrechetres aovers de II pars, et soient aussi comme noez, et i ait I mainche de fer bien fait; et c’est li forme:	And the sagely said in the cautery of the hunchback, for this is the manner, make it one large and thick as a fingernail, or a little smaller, and space between them the quantity of a pea; and may the between-teeth be on both sides, and they are also like fingers, and there is always a little metal made well; and this is the form:
Et soit eschaufez tant qu’il soit toz rouges et giete senteles, et puis le mette on sus la boiste de la hainche malaide, et soit tornez sus lou sain costeit; et lou cauterize une fois I cautere reont et lou laisse III jors; et puis fai emplaustre de burre, et laisse la plaie aoverte lonc tens; aprés la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	And let it be heated until it is completely red and hot, and then put it on the chest of the ill person, and turn it around the ribs; and let him cauterize once and let him rest for three days; and then make an ointment of butter, and leave the open wound exposed for a long time; after the healing with ointment until he is well.
Albucasim dit que nos usons poc de cest cautere por la paor de son regart, et se voions poc qui en usent; et toutevoie ceu est des boins cauteres, qui le puet soffrir, et lai ou il s’afiert.	Albucasim says that we should use little of this cautery because of the danger of regurgitation, and few people use it; but this is a good cauterization, which can bear it, and let it be applied where it needs to be.
Li cauteres de medicine ardant si est que tu faices I estrument a entrechetres en coi dessende li marge de la porte, et soit d’arain ou de fer a une paroit longe, et en la hautece ait II nous, et ait entre chaicun la quantiteit de la groissece d’un doi; et soient overt defuer et desus, et se joignent ensamble selonc ceste forme:	The medical cauterization with hot instruments is such that you make a tool with a gap in the middle of which one edge is made of iron or brass and the other of wood, so that it has two lengths, each of which is twice its thickness; and let them open and close on both sides, and join together according to this shape:
Aprés met sus la boiste de la hainche au malaide gisant sor suin costeit sain, et apresse ta main mout sus la boiste de la hainche; aprés giete entre les II cercles de l’awe chaude qui soit chaufee au feu I poc, et li laisse une houre dou tens, et soffre li malaides la chalor et l’arsure de li.	After you put your hand up under the hip of the horse that lies on its side on the ground, and press hard up against it; after you put a hot stone in the fire for an hour, and leave it there for a while, and suffer the pain and burning of the horse.
Car il i trueve mordication ausi com de feu; et quant li mordications iert passee, se lieve ta main avec l’estrument et leve la hainche d’awe douce, et laisse ensi III jors, et met sus burre tant que ceu qui est noir de l’eschaudure soit osteit; et lou laisse III jors que porriture en istrait; et ceu serait li derriene aide aprés le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	For it is the same with the horse's hot bit as with fire; and when the bit has done its work, you remove your hand from the instrument and lift up the horse's back with a gentle stroke, and leave it so for three days, and put on butter until what is black with scorching is healed over; and let it be three days before washing. And this would help the horse behind after the treatment of onions as long as it is well.
Et se li dolor s’est estendue jusc’a la cuisse ou jusc’a la jambe, se li fai I estrument que teigne awe selonc ceu que tu as fait en la hainche igaument; et c’est li maniere de l’awe chaude, et je l’ai escripte ou traitier de la rectification de medicine.	And if the pain extends to the thigh or leg, you make an instrument that will rub according to what you have done in the hip, and this is the way of hot stone, and I have written it up or the treatment of correction of medicine.
Pren alcali et chaulz vive, autant de l’une com de l’autre, et les broie ensamble, et les met en I nuef pot.	Take alkali and living chalc, as much of one as of the other, and grind them together, and put them in a nine-pot.
ou il ait I petit pertuis defuer se que li pointe d’un raisor i puisse entreir; et met desor celui pot I autre pot bien plombeit, et met sus alcali et chalz et awe douce sus, tant qu’il en i ait I doi desus les poudres cant tu l’avras bien preingte a ta main; et le laisse ensi tant qu’il en dessende awe ague et chiece ou pot plombeit, puis pren toute cele awe, et la giete sus chalz et sus alcali si com devant.	Take alkaline and live char, as much of one as of the other, and grind them together, and put them in a nine-pot. There should be a small gap between the two so that the tip of a rod can pass through; and place that pot on top of another well-plastered pot, and put alkali and char and soft water on it, so much as to make two layers above the powders while you stir them with your hand; and leave it like that until it has soaked up enough water and dried out slightly; then take all of that water, and pour it over the char and alkali just as mentioned before.
Et lors si sera mout ague et est aministree en mou d’ovraiges de medicine et en cauteres d’autres membres Car elle fait auteil oevre com feus, et si a autres medicines dont on cauterize bien la hainche ensi com tesisie et miel anacardi et chalz avec savon, toutes ces choses mellees ensamble.	And so, when it is well-moistened and dried out somewhat in the works of medicine and other cauterizations, for it does the same work as fire; and with other medicines, which are well-blended with this, like theriac and myrrh and char with soap, all these things mixed together.
Et Galiens nos raconte une cure dont uns hons fut curez de la dolor de la hainche et de la voine sciatique, et lou loe mout, et dit que on n’i fist autre cure, et qu’il en fut sanez a une soule fois quant on ot fait ceste cure, et il se fut baigniez si com il l’enseigne ci aprés.	And Galiens tells us of a remedy where a honorable man was cured of the pain in his hip and sciatic nerve, and he muttered it, and said that no other cure was made, and he was healed at one soul time when this cure was done, and he bathed himself as it is taught hereafter.
Et dist en teil maniere que tu preignes dou litargire vert fres et sec, et le broie mout avec I poc de graisse, et met sus la hainche et sus la cuisse et sus la jambe ou la dolor tient, et la lie; et li laisse III houres et par la quantiteit que li malaides ne sente plus l’arsure.	And he said in this way that you grind the green and fresh lime and dry it, and pound a little with fat, and put it on the hip and thigh and leg where the pain is, and let it sit; and leave it for III hours and by the quantity that the patient no longer feels the burning.
Et puis le fai entrer ou bain tant que li cors li soit un poc arousez, et lou fai entrer ou lit, et li dolor s’en ira toute et sera sanez.	And then let him enter or bathe as much as his body is a little awakened, and let him enter the bed, and the pain will go away all and be healed.
Et saiches que nuls ne doit user de cautere de telz medicines, se ceu n’est aprés l’evacuation de cors.	And know that no one should use fire cautery with such medicines unless after the evacuation of blood.
Et Dyascorides dist que quant li voine sciatique est cauterizee de fiens de chievre, si i aide mout; et doit estre fais li cauteres en teil maniere.	And Dyascorides says that when the sciatic vein is cauterized with the end of a goat's horn, it should help much; and it must be done in such a way.
Prenez lainne et la beurez d’oile vielz, et metez sus la fossete qui est entre le pouce dou piez et l’autre qui est apelez foscile.	Take another and rub it with old oil, and put it on the pit that is between the thumb of your hand and the other which is called the finger.
Aprés pren fiens de chievre sec, et l’empren a feu tant qu’il soit charbons, et lou met sus la laine, et le laisse tant qu’il soit estains; et refai encor ensi, et ne cesser de faire ensi tant que tu penses par sens qu’il viegne jusc’a la hainche, et que li dolor soit cessee; et cist manieres de cautere est apelez «cautere de chievre».	Afterwards take a piece of dry goat's horn, and rub it with fire until it is red hot, and lay it on the wool, and let it be until it has cooled down; and do it again in the same way, and do not cease to do it thus as long as you think that it comes up to the knee, and that the pain ceases; and this way of cauterizing is called "cauterize with a goat's horn".
de la dolor dou dos	of the back's pain
Quant dolor vient au dos, ou par cheoir ou de percussion ou par trop grant evacuation, ou par semblans de matiere espandue froide, a nule de ces semblances ne vaut cauteres, fuer que a celi qui vient de infusion de froide matiere.	When pain comes to the back, or from shaking, or from too much blood flowing out, or from the appearance of cold material spreading out, there is no remedy for any of these things that is worth trying, except for those that come from an infusion of cold material.
Il covient c’aprés ceu que li malaides est voidiez de pilules fetides ou d’autres semblans, que on li faice sus lou dos, lai ou li dolor tient, trois lignes signies d’enche, et en chescune ligne V cauteres ou plus selonc la vertut et la quantiteit que li malaides puet soffrir; et soit fait li cauteres selonc le cautere qui est apelez «poins»; et se tu vues, fai III cauteres ou IIII au cautere clavile moien selonc ceste forme:	When the patient is voiding foul bile or other stuff, let it be done to him on his back, where the pain is, three lines signed with a inch, and in each line V cauterizations or more according to the virtue and the quantity that the patient can bear; and let the cauterization be done according to the cauterization called "point"; and if you see, do III cauterizations or IV at the clavicle cauterization according to this form:
Maintes fois vient ceste maladie as petis enfans, et li signes de l’encomencement si est qu’il ont estroite alainne quant il se lievent, et paor; et tu trueves en la derriene espinee dou dos et en nous l’apparance qui vient sus les autres espinees.	This disease often comes in small children, and the signs of its beginning are that they have tight posture when they stand up, and fear; and you will find in the back lower spine and on the back the appearance that comes on top of the other spines.
Quant tu vois ceu et tu le vues curer, si le cauterize au cautere de celcle selonc ceste forme.	When you see this man and you treat him, if you use fire cautery according to this form.
Si que li cautere porpreigne chescune partie de l’espinee egaument.	So that the fire cautery is applied equally to each part of the spine.
Et se tu vues, si cauterize entor l’espinee au cautere poignant II lignes ou III, et soient li poins pres l’uns de l’autre.	And if you see this, then cauterize between the spines with a fire that is two or three lines long, and let the pokes be close to each other.
Aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez selonc ceu que nos avons dit, et warde que tu n’amenistrer cautere en gilbositeit qui soit en spame de nerf.	After treating the area until it is healthy according to what we have said, be careful not to apply fire cautery to gangrene that is in the flesh near a nerve.
de la dolor des jointes	of the joints' pain
Quant dolor de jointes sunt de moistors que sont espandues a chaicun membre dou cors, et quant dolor vient em piez, que li mire apelent «podagre» proprement, et quant elle est de froide cause et cures de medicines ne la puent curer, si est curez par cauteres en teil maniere: fai li mout de cauteres entor la jointure dou piet, et soit li cauteres olivaire selonc ceste forme:	When joint pain is caused by moisture that spreads to each limb, and when the pain comes in pieces, what is called "podagra" properly, and when it is caused by cold and cannot be cured with medicines, then it is cured with fire cautery in this way: Make the fire cautery between the joint of the foot, and let the cautery be olive-colored according to this form:
Et s’il i a besoigne que tu poignes sus la faice dou piet, se li fai cautere a tot le cautere c’on claime «point».	And if it is necessary that you touch on the face of the foot, then make a fire cautery with all the fire cautery that is claimed "point".
Et se les dolors viegnent jusc’a genous et as autres jointures, et ceu avient maintes fois, se li fai cautere sus chaicun genoil III cauteres ou IIII de chescunne partie, a tout le cautere olivaire; et se tu as mestier de plus, si en fai plus, mais n’i tenir mie ta main fuers que tant que li espés dou keur soit ars.	And if the pains come up just to the knees and to other joints, and this happens many times, then make a fire cautery on each knee three cauterizes or four of each part, with all the olive fire cautery; and if you need more, then do more, but do not hold your hand out too long except when the skin of the cure is burned.
Et se les dolors dessendent jusc’a genoil et au dos, se li aministre le cautere que nos avons dit en son chapistre.	And if the pains come down to the knees and back, then administer the cautery that we have spoken of in this chapter.
Et se les dolors sunt as mains, si fai poins entor le foscile II lignes; et s’il remaint point de dolor as dois, si fai poins sus chescune jointe et sus lou poil de la main; et se les dolors vienent jusc’as coutes ou jusc’as espaules, si cauterize chescune partie, et fai boin governement au malaide et penre medicines.	And if the pains are in the hands, then make a point of burning the skin with two lines; and if there is still pain in the two joints and the hair of the hand; and if the pains come up just to the elbows or just to the shoulders, then cauterize each part, and govern well the patient and give medicine.
Car se tu li fais boin governement et tu purges fleume, si sera saneis a l’aide de Deu.	For if you do this good governance and you purify pus, then will you be healed with the help of God.
de la routure dou syfac	of the rupture of the syrup
Quant routure vient en angres, et li bouelz dessendent as coions et c’est novelement, si covient que quant tu lou vues curer, qu’il ne menjuce mie celui jor; et qu’il use choses qui laichent lou ventre, si que li fiens dessende de son ventre; aprés le fai seoir sus son dos entre tes mains, et li comande qu’il teigne son alaine tant que li boueil soient repairiet, et les ramoinne a tes dois, et seigne d’enche desoz la routure sus l’os dou poignil, et a tout un signe que soit semblans a la moitiet d’un cercle a desus dou cors; puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	When rupture comes in the throat, and the belly descends as it grows worse, so that when you look at him you do not see anything; and he uses things that leave his belly empty, so that the end descends from his belly; after that, he sits down on his back between your hands, and orders him to wet his armpits until his fever is gone, and he takes them in your hands, and signs with his hand above the rupture on the bone of the arm, and all in a sign that is like a half-circle from the neck; then heat the fire according to this form:
tant qu’il soit blans et qu’il giete senteles.	until it is white and it drips with sweat.
Puis ramoine les bouels a lor leu; et li ministres teigne sa main sus qu’il ne retornent arrier; et oevre bien les cuisses au malaide, et met desoz lui I cussin et I serjant sus les cuisses, et I autre sus lou pis qui li teigne les mains; puis met le cautere sus lou signe a tout ta main, et lou tien droit et lou tien tant que tu ateignes l’os, et se tu ne l’ateins la premiere fois, si le rencomence encor une autre tant que tu viegnes jusc’a l’os; et te warde subtilment que li boueil ne saille quant tu fais lou cautere; que tu ne le brulasses; et que par ceu li malaides ne muere, ou autre malz.	Then put the balls in their place; and the assistant holds his hand so that they do not turn back; and well operate on the legs of the sick person, and put a tourniquet on him and a serjant on his legs, and another on his feet which hold his hands; then put the cautery on his bones with your whole hand, and keep it firm and as long as you reach the bone, and if you do not hit it the first time, so you begin again another so that you come to the bone; and be careful that the ball does not slip when you make the cautery; that you do not burn him; and that by this the sick person does not die, or any other evil.
Et saiches que quant tu ne viens jusc’a l’os au cautere, tes ovraiges ne vaut rien.	And know that when you come up to the bone with the cautery, your work is worth nothing.
Et covient que li cauteres des enfans soit subtilz selonc la mesure d’ous, et des grans gens aussi grans selonc lor mesure; aprés III jors cure lou leu dou cautere de burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés le cure d’autres oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez, et gise li malaides XL jors sus son dos tant que li plaie soit bien soudee; et covient que ses norrissemens soit lassatis longement, si que li boueil ne saillent quant il se preigdra d’aler en chambres.	And it is appropriate that the cauterization of children be done with care according to their size, and for adults also according to their size; after three days cure the place of the cautery with butter as long as the scorching is bone; after this cure other remedies as long as he is healed, and let the sick person lie on his back for XL days until the wound is well fixed; and it is appropriate that his bandages be loosened slowly, so that the ball does not slip when he goes to bed.
Et aprés XL jors, quant il se voudra lever, se li amenistre une faixe bien faite, et la porse XL autres jors; et ait boin repos, qu’il se travaille poc et se warde de trop grant repletion de boivre et de mengier, et de trop haut braire; et quant il fait cest enseignement si est sanez entierement.	And after forty days, when he wants to get up, a well-made girdle is brought to him and worn for forty other days; and good rest, so that he works little and guards against too much drinking and eating, and too loud shouting; and when he has done this teaching, then is he completely healed.
Et je dirai ci aprés la cure de taillier en son chapistre.	And I will say here the cure for cutting in his ointment.
de la routure dou ventre	of the rupture of the belly
Quant routures vienent en autres ventres et sont connisans, et tu vues qu’elles ne croissent plus, se li fai I cautere dou cautere reont selonc sa quantiteit, et soit ars li tiers dou keur; aprés le cure selonc ceu que nos avons dit; et aucun des anciens ont dit c’on le doit cauterizer au cautere a III angles selonc ceste forme:	When ruptures come in other bellies and are known, and you see that they no longer grow, the cautery of cautery is made according to its quantity, and let him be burned according to this; after the cure according to what we have said; and no one of the ancients has said that it should be cauterized at three angles according to this shape:
mais signe premier le leu d’enche et fai une ligne per la largesce desus la routure, et une autre defuers, et main ta main emmi a tout le cautere clavile.	but the first sign is the edge of the navel and make a line across the width above the rupture, and another below it, and with your hand hold all the cautery knife-edge.
Mais li premiers cauteres est plus legiers et muedres.	But the first caustics are lighter and milder.
de dolor anciene en aucun membre	of old pain in any member
Quant dolor vient en aucun membre, ou de cheoir ou de ferir, et cele dolor tient lonc tens, et li cure de medicine n’i vaut, adonc covient qu’il soit cauterizeis au cautere qui est apelez «poins», et soit li cauteres selonc la longesce dou membre et la petitece et sa foibleteit et sa vertut et sa location de torcions et de sa dolor.	When pain comes in any member, or from shaking or hurting, and this pain lasts a long time, and the medicine cure does not help, then it is necessary that he be cauterized with the caustic which is called "poins", and the caustic be made according to the length of the member and its smallness and its feebleness and its virtue and its location from twists and its pain.
s’il est sanez dou premier cautere, c’est bien; se ceu nom, recomence I autre cautere sus celui, car teilz costume est qu’il se doit muer au membre que li est prochiens, por coi il covient que tu faices les cauteres tant que li malaides soit saneis.	If he is well after the first caustic, it is good; but if not, begin again another caustic on that one, for the habit is that it must run to the member that is nearest, so that you must make the caustics as long as the patient is ill.
de meselerie	of liveliness
Li meseil sont aidiet aucune fois par cautere par grant aide, et meismement li maladie que vient de la putrefaction de fleume et de melancolie.	The mesele are aided by the caustic no more than once by great aid, and most often the disease comes from the putrefaction of the phlegm and melancholy.
Cant tu la vues cauterizer, pren warde se li maladie est au comencement, et s’ele est curee selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et ne dessent ne ne demoure, et tu doutes que li corruption ne porpreigne tout le malaide, adonques li fai V cauteres sus lou chief: I emmi le chief a nouf, et l’autre vers lou front a la fin des chevous; et II sus les II cornes, et I derrierre sus le haiterel; et i laise tant ta main que li cauteres viegne jusc’a l’os, et tant que les escorces en issent fors si que les vapors des grosses humors s’en puissent issir; et le cauterize sus la mice selonc ce qu’il est devant.	Cant tu la vues cauterizer, pren warde se li maladie est au comencement, et s’ele est curee selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et ne dessent ne ne demoure, et tu doutes que li corruption ne porpreigne tout le malaide, adonques li fai V cauteres sus lou chief: I emmi le chief a nouf, et l'autre vers lou front a la fin des chevois; et II sus les II cornes, et I derrierre sur le haiterel; et i laise tant ta main que li cauteres viegne jusc'a l'os, et tant que les escorces en issent fors si que les vapors des grosses humors s'en puissent issir; et le cauterize sus la mice selonc ce qu'il est devant.
Et se li meselerie est partout esparse; et elle pert manifestement, si covient que tu lou cauterizes de ces cauteres que nos avons dit ou chief, et I cautere en som lou neis, et II cauteres sus l’espinee dou col, et VI cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos, et I grant sus la crupie et I autre delez, et II sus les II espaules; et II sus les coutes, et II sus les tendrons dou pis, et I sus chascune jointe des mains et des piez, et sus les fosses des mains; et te warde des ners que sunt sus lou derrien calcant, que tu ne les bruler; et aucune fois fait om cautere sus l’os dou poignil, et I autre sus l’os de l’estomac, et I autre sus lou foie.	Now you can start the cauterizer, be mindful that the disease is just beginning, and if it is healed according to what we have said in the division, and does not get worse or stay the same, and you doubt that corruption will spread throughout the whole body, then apply V cauters to the top of the head: I cut the hair off the top of the head, and the other towards the front at the end of the hair; and II on the two horns, and I behind on the nape; and I let my hand move so that the cauterizer comes up to the bone, and as long as the scabs come out without hindering, so that the vapors of the great humors can come out; and cauterize on the skin according to what it is in front. And if it is scattered everywhere; and it obviously loses, so that you apply the cauters that we have said, or chief, and I cauterize in the navel, and II cauterizes on the spine of the neck, and VI cauterizes on the spine of the back, and I large one on the skull and another delicate one, and II on the two shoulders; and II on the ribs, and II on the tendon of the wrist, and I on each joint of the hands and feet, and on the pits of the hands; and be careful of the nerves that run down the back, that you do not burn them; and never apply a cauterizer to the bone of the hand or arm, or another to the stomach bone, or another to the liver.
Et saiches que quant plus i fais de cautere, plus li fais d’aide, et mues li profite; et saiches que li malaides ne sent point de dolor au cautere si com li sain le sentent, por ce que li cors est ja toz corrumpus.	And know that the more I make of cauterization, the more I do of aid, and it profits him; and know that the patient feels no pain at the cauterization as those who are healthy feel it, for this reason that his body is already very corrupted.
Et covient ke li cautere soient grant et petit selonc les membres et les jointures, selonc ceu que vos lou troverez en manieres des fers.	And let the cauterization be great and small according to the members and joints, according to what you will find in the manner of irons.
Aprés cure lou leu de farine de veces avec miel et autres cures tant qu’il soit saneis.	After treatment, put flour on his head with honey and other treatments until he is healed.
Quant enfleure vient en aucun membre et est curee par medicines et oiles et emplastres, et il n’est mie sanez, adonques li fai cauteres sus le membre selonc la grandour et la petitece dou membre; et soit li cauteres un poc entrans en l’espés dou keur; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the swelling comes to any member and is treated with medicines, oils, and plasters, and it is not healed, then make cauterization on the member according to its size; and let the cauterization be a little bit entering into the flesh of the cure; then treat with ointments until he is healed.
Et aucune fois fait on cautere et a la main et au piet et au dos, a l’issue dou nerf que muet le membre, et ensi si est ostee li enfleure; et toutevoie ne s’en entremette nuls s’il n’est conoissans des membres et des issues des ners movans lou cors.	And never does one do cauterization and with the hand and the foot and the back, to the exit of the nerve that silences the member, and thus if it is osteated; and yet nothing interferes there if it is not known of the members and the exits of the moving nerves of the body.
de albaras	of blisters
Quant li maladie qui est apelee «albaras» est enveillie, et li engien de medicine n’i valent rien, adonques le cauterize d’un cautere un poc parfont, selonc la quantiteit de l’espés dou keur, tant que li blenchour soit ostee, et soit muee sa color; puis le cure de farine de veces et de lentilles avec oile roset et foilles de plantain, et sanc de colon et sanc d’alondre, de chescun une partie; et soit mellez tout ensamble, et soit liiez d’un drapel, et soit aers au leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the disease called "albaras" is aggravated, and the medicine does not help, then cauterize with a fire cauldron perfectly, according to the quantity of the cure of the wound, until the blister is opened, and its color changes; then cure with flour and lentils with oil and plantain leaves, and hay and almond wine, each of them in part; and mix everything together, and bind it with a bandage, and apply it to the affected area until it heals.
li cure de chancre par cautere	The treatment for syphilis with fire cautery.
Quant chancre vient au comencement, et tu lou vues arrester, si le cauterize au cautere qui semble I cercle, tout entor au tour dou chancre.	When the wart first appears and you have stopped its spread, apply fire cautery to the wart, which seems like a circle, all around the edge of the wart.
Et toutevoie li saige dirent que on faice cautere ausi au mileu dou chancre; et toutevoie ceu ne me semble mie boin, car je redous que il ne soit ulcerez et corrumpus, et je l’ai ja veut avenir aucune fois; et plus droituriere chose est qu’il soit cauteriés entor, au cautere qui est apelez «circule», si com nos avons dit en mout de cauteres.	And yet some say that fire cautery should also be applied to the center of the wart; but this I do not believe is good, for then it might become ulcerated and corrupted, and I have never heard of this being done successfully; rather, it is better to apply fire cautery all around, with the fire called 'circle', as we have said in many cauterizations.
de l’enfleure qui ne puet meurer	of the growth that cannot die
Quant aucuns ait une maladie qui est apelee «adubelati», et elle tarde de meurer ou por la superfluiteit qu’ele fait ou por l’eaige dou malaide quant il est decrepites (c’est a dire trop vielz) et il a poc de sanc, ou por lou tens; et tu la vues haster de meurer: adonques le cauterize entor de mout de petis cauteres en poignant; aprés le laisse ensi.	When anyone has a disease called 'adubelati', and it takes a long time to die or because of the overflow of the illness or because the person is very old and has little blood, or because they are short of breath; then hasten to kill them: then apply small fire cauterizations all around, piercing with them; and then leave it like this.
Car elle se hastera de meureir.	For she will hasten to die.
Et se tu la vues percier a tout le cautere, si chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	And if you saw her pierced at all the cautery, let the cautery be hot in which this shape is:
Et met ta main en mileu de cele maladie qui est apellee «adubelati» tant que li cauteres ait perciet lou keur, et soit telz li cauteres que li malaides lou sente defuers en teil maniere que li cours de la porriture soit alegis.	And place your hand in the middle of this disease called "adubelati" as long as the cautery has pierced the cure, and make such cauteries that the patient feels a coldness in some way that the course of the corruption is stopped.
Aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	After the cure until he is completely healed.
li cure dou feu par fer	the fire cure by iron
Une autre maniere de maladie i a qui est apelee «corrodens», et n’est autre chose que une mengeson de membre, car ele menjut les membres ausi com li feus les leignes seches.	Another disease is called "corrodens", and it is not something else than a mingling of members, for she mingles the members as the fire dries up the wood.
Se tu vois ceste maladie en leu qui puisse soffrir cautere ensamble feu, adonques eschaufe les cauteres clavile mout petit et grant, selonc ceu qu’il covient au leu ou li maladie est; aprés le cauterize de toutes pars tant que tu erraiche toute la corruption, et nen remaigne rien de li, que tout ceu qui est corrumpus ne soit osteit.	If you see this disease in the light that can be cured together with fire, then heat the clavicles of the cautery small and large, according to what is appropriate for the place where the disease is; after the cure on all sides until it is completely healed, and nothing remains of it, that all that is corrupted is removed.
Et puis le laisse III jors, et met sus les leus cauterizez soffre broiet avec oile tant que les eschaudures dou feu soient ostees, et toute li corruption.	And then leave it for three days, and put on the fire-cured spots suffer bruise with oil as soon as the burns of fire are healed, and all corruption.
Aprés lou cure d’oignemens engendrans char.	After the cure of ointments generating chapped.
Et se tu vois aprés III jors que chars saine ne naisse, c’est boin; et se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere sus ceu qui est demoreit des leus corrumpus.	And if after three days the chapped skin does not heal, it is good; and if not, begin again the cauterization on that which has remained corrupted.
Et ceste mengeson est aucune fois esteit curee de medicine ague en leu de cautere de feu; mais toutevoie cautere de feu est de plus grant aide, et j’ai ja dit la cure de la medicine ague en la division: pren la quant tu en as mestier.	And this ointment is never once cured with medicine that is fire-cured; but nevertheless fire-curing is of greater help, and I have already said the cure of the medicine that is a fire in division: take it when you need it.
des porrelz qui vienent as piez	of onions that come to the tip
Mout de fois avient que as piez par defuers naist une maladie qui est apelee «clos» selonc nostre entencion, et est une grosse chose fautree qui blece lou piet.	Mouth of times comes that at the tips by accident there is a disease which is called "close" according to our intention, and it is a large ugly thing that bleeds the foot.
Et li cauteres de ceste maladie si est selonc II manieres.	And these treatments for this disease are according to two ways.
C’est a savoir cautere de feu, et cautere d’aigue chaude.	It is known as fire cautery and water cautery.
Cautere de feu si est que tu eschaufe I cautere cheveit ausi com est une penne de vouteul, et soit fait de boin fer a la mesure qu’il puisse porpenre le clou de toutes pars, et qu’il i ait subtilz marges; aprés le met tout chaut sus lou clou, et torne ta main tot entor le clou tant qu’il viegne au font dou clou; et lou laisse ensi III jors tant qu’il encomence giter porriture; puis li fai un emplaustre de malves savaiges broiies avec seil, et laisse l’emplaustre sus toute la nuit, et li clous cherra et sera desracinez de ses racines.	Fire cautery is when you heat a metal spike as if it were a feather, making sure to make it narrow with thick margins; then, place it directly on the nail, turning your hand in order to push it all the way down until it reaches the nail's base; leave it like that for three days before starting to apply rubies crushed with salt; leave the ointment on all night, and the nail will fall off and be completely rootless.
Puis cure le leu d’oignement enjanrant char tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then treat the sore with oil of saffron for as long as it remains healthy.
Et s’il sont convertit par defuers lou cors, et maintes fois avient et en mains et em piez, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere d’aigue chaude; et est en teil maniere: pren une cainne d’arain ou de fer, ou une penne de vouteul, et met sus lou clou et l’althelul, c’est asavoir porrelz verrues; et met la cainne sus si qu’ele porpreigne tout entor, puis i met un poc d’awe chaude, et retien bien ta main, et presse ta main en tornant si que li marge de la cainne viegne a la racine dou clou, et puisse trover l’aigue chaude voie parfonde jusc’a la racine; et soffre li malaides un poc la mordication de l’aigue chaude une houre; puis le laisse ensi, et il se derracinera tous a tout ses racines.	And if the course of the disease is reversed and it heals again, then treat it with the water cautery: Take a piece of iron or steel, or a feather from a vulture's wing, and place it on the nail and the callus, that is to say, make it rot all around; then put some hot water on it, and firmly hold your hand back, and turn it so that the edge of the piece comes up to the nail’s root, and can find the deep path of the water; and let the patient feel a little pain from the hot water for an hour; then leave it, and it will completely fall off its roots.
Ensi fai un aprés autre, tant que tu esraiches toz ces qui sont au cors, puis les cure des oignemens qui engenrent char.	Make another one like this until you have removed all those who are at heart, then treat the causes that generate bitterness.
li cure dou trembler	to cure the shaking
Quant aucuns tremble de froidor de ners, ou de fievre quartaine ou d’autre, si covient que tu li faices IIII cauteres ou IV sus l’espinee dou dos, I cautere entre chescune espinee; et I cautere ou pez, et I sus l’estomac au cautere olivaire; si laissera lou trembler, et se hastera li santez de la maladie froide.	When some shake from cold, or from the quartain fever or other, it is necessary that you make four or five cauterizes on the spine of the back, one cauterize between each spine; and one cauterize at the feet, and one on the stomach with olive cauterizing liquid; so will they stop shaking, and will hasten the healing of the cold disease.
des pustules puans	of pus-filled blisters
Aucune fois apperent par defuers le cors bathes, ou pustules puans, que vienent de grosses matieres corrumpues.	Once apparent by means of discharges from the body, or pustules that come from corrupt matter.
si covient au premier quant eles apperent que on faice cautere sus chescun chief de la pustule: un cautere subtil de fust de mirte, de coi li pointe soit emprise au feu, ou de racine de aristologe longe, ou au cautere lenticulaire.	If it appears first that one make a cauterize on each head of the pustule: a fine cauterize from the stem of the mistletoe, so that it takes hold of fire, or from the root of the aristolochia long, or with the lente-shaped cauterize.
Et aucune fois les cauterize on au comencement quant il aperent, selonc ceste maniere, et il ne puent croistre des enqui en avant, mais est desrompue li superfluitez dont il vienent, et sont sanez; mais il covient que ceu soit fait aprés l’evacuation de sanc.	And at no time are they cauterized in the beginning when they appear according to this way, and they cannot grow any longer than that, but the superfluity which comes from it is interrupted, and they are healed; but it is necessary that this be done after the evacuation of blood.
quant li artere est copee	When the artery is cut off
Maintes fois avient grans decorremens de sanc de l’artere qui est copee a la plaie que vient au pardefuers, ou a l’incision de l’aposteme, ou au cautere dou membre, et as semblans choses; et est mout grief chose d’estenchier.	Many times a great disturbance of blood comes from the artery that is cut off at the wound that comes to the skin, or to the incision of an abscess, or to the cauterization of the member, and similar things; and it is a painful thing to stop bleeding.
Et toutevoie quant ceu avient a aucun, si te haste de mettre ton doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne, et l’estrain mout tant que li sans soit apaisiez desoz ton doi, et que goute n’en isse plus; puis met au feu les cauteres olivaire plusors petis et grans tant qu’il soient tuit rouge; puis empren I, ou grant ou petit selonc la plaie et lou leu en coi li artere est route, et met le cautere sus cele voine ou tu tiens ton doi, et tien le cautere tant sus que li sans soit restainchiez.	And whenever he has any, then you quickly put your index finger on the wound of the vein, and strain it so much that your blood is stopped by your finger, and no more drops; then take fire-olive oil, large or small according to the wound and its place, and set all of it on fire; then take I, or a great or a small according to the wound and its place, and put the cauterization on that vein where you hold your finger, and keep the cauterization there until the blood is stopped.
Et s’il saut fuers quant tu lieves ton doi desus la voinne, et li cauteres estint, si pren hastivement I autre des cauteres qui sont au feu.	And if you raise it quickly when you feel your second pain in the vein, and the cautery is extinguished, take another cautery from the fire quickly.
Et ne cesser de faire ceu l’un aprés l’autre tant que li sans soit estenchiez; et warde que tu n’ardes lou nerf qui est delez, et que autre malice ne viegne sus lou malaide; et saiches que quant sans decourt de l’artere, c’on ne lou puet mie bien restenchier meismement quant li artere est grans, se ceu n’est par une des IIII manieres que nos avons dit: ou par cautere, ou par extraction quant ele n’est mie traite, ou par fort liement de fil, ou par medicines mises sus qui ont pooir de restenchier sanc; et soit liee et estrainte avennament.	And do not stop doing one after the other until the pain subsides; and be careful that you do not burn the nerve that is delicate, and that another evil does not come upon the patient; and know that when the artery is cut short of the vein, it can no longer be well treated unless by one of the four ways we have mentioned: or by cauterization, or by extraction if it has not yet been treated, or by firmly tying a thread, or by medicines placed on it that have the power to stop the pain; and bind and stretch it properly.
Qui i amenistrera restenchement de liier estroitement de drapelz ou de metre choses ardans sus, ou autres semblans choses, se n’i profite se poc non.	Who will administer the tight binding with strips of cloth or other burning things, or similar things, will profit if he does not harm.
Et se ce avient a aucun et il n’ait mie mire ne medicine present, si doit mettre son doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne si com nos avons dit, et bien estrendre tant qu’il soit restenchiez desus la plaie et desus la voinne; et ne remuer lou doit, mais lou moille d’awe froide sovent que soit mout froide tant que li sans soit congelez et engrossiez et restenchiez; et faice des enqui en avant ceu dont il a mestier de cauteres et de medicines.	Et si ce arrive à aucun et il n'ait mie merdé ni médecine présent, si doit mettre son doi indice sur la plaie de la veine si com nous avons dit, et bien étendre tant qu'il soit renflé dessus la plaie et dessus la veine; et ne remuer lou doigt, mais lou mouille d'eau froide souvent que soit mout froide tant que le sang soit congelez et épaissié et renflé; et fais des enfers en avant ceu dont il a mestier de cautères et de médicaments.
Ci encomence li secons livre des cures de taille	Here begins the second book of treatments for diseases related to the body's cuts and wounds.
Nos vos avons dit ou premier chapistre toute maladie en coi il covient cautere de feu, ou de medicine ardans, et les oquisons et les causes et les estrumens et les formes des cauteres; et ai mis celui chapistre des lou chief jusc’a piez, et je irai en cest chapistre par celi meisme voie por ceu c’on trueve plus legierement ceu c’on voura.	We have told you in the first chapter about diseases that require fire treatments, or burning medicines, and the squirts and causes and instruments and shapes of the treatments; and I put this chapter from the lower part of the body up to the waist, and I will go through this chapter with the same middle path for those who are troubled more leichtly than those who are in great pain.
Et ainsois que je encomence ceu, il covient, chier fil, que vos aprenez que en cest chapistre a plus de peril et de paor que ou premier des cauteres, et por ceu il covient plus grant cautele.	And so, since I am beginning this, it is necessary, dear sir, that you learn that in this chapter there is more danger and fear than in the first of the cauterizations, and for this reason greater caution is required.
Car en l’ovraige de cest chapistre avient maintes fois evacuation de sanc a l’ovrir la voinne, et a l’incision sus aposteme, et as cures des plaies, et a l’estraction des saiettes, et a l’incision sus la piere, et les semblans choses; ou il a doutance et paor, et en vient li mors a plusors.	For in the work of this chapter, there is often the evacuation of blood when opening a vein, and incising an abscess, and in the treatment of wounds, and in the extraction of arrows, and in cutting into stones, and similar things; where there is doubt and fear, and many die.
Et je vos amoneste que vos n’entreprenez folie.	And I warn you that you should not undertake madness.
Car mout de manieres de gens vienent en cures.	For in many ways people come to healing.
si vienent de telz qui s’aïrent si avec lor maladie qu’il muerent legierement por la forsenerie qu’il trueve de sa maladie, et de la grandour de son malice; et de ces doit on avoir paor.	If they come from those who with their disease have died so easily that they could not bear the pain of their illness and the great evil of their disease; and of this one should be afraid.
Et de ces i a qui te done son sens, et dit: «atendez, je sui garis»; et li maladie est despitouse.	And of these I have told you what they mean, and said: "Wait, I am ready"; and the disease is contemptible.
Il ne covient mie que vos vos consentez a ces qui vienent a vos qui ont ceste maniere, mais mettez plus grant cusanson en vostre honor qu’en vostre covoitise, et n’ovrez mie folement mais saigement de ceu dont vos estes certain, et dont vos poez avoir pris et los; et usez de pronostication et de indication en cures de vos malaides a coi salus soit convertie; et ceu vos aidera a aquester bone renommee, et gloire, et memoire de loenge.	It is fitting that you grant these the honor they deserve, but show greater compassion than covetousness towards your neighbors, and do not venture rashly into the business of others; and in the treatment of your patients, use prophecy and indication so that health may be restored; and he who helps you to acquire a good reputation, glory, and memory, will aid you in earning these things.
Tres chier fil, Nostres Sires vos doint boin entendement et droiture, et se vos vuelle espireir de la sainte inspiration de sa main, amen.	Very dear sir, our Lords give you good understanding and righteousness, and may you strive for the holy inspiration of His hand, amen.
Or je vos ai ordeneit cest chapistre en devisant par chapistres, selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre des cauteres, que je vos ai deviseit des le chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que vos trovez plus legierement ceu dont vos avrez mestier.	Or I have ordered this chapter in devising by chapters, according to that which is before or after the chapter of the cauterizing, which I have devised for you from the top up to the tip, so that you may find more easily that which will be your need.
dou chief plein d’aigue	dough of water
Saiches que ceste maladie vient mout de fois as enfans a l’enfanter, et quant li baille estraint trop fort le chief de l’enfant; et aucune fois vient ceu de cause reponue que on ne seit.	I know that this disease often comes to infants and when the child cries too much, pulling hard on the head of the child; and never do I hear a reason for it.
Et je ne vis onques ceste maladie fuers qu’en enfans, et a toz ces que j’ai veus se hastait li mors; et por ceu me semble qu’il me vaut mues lassier l’ovraige en teilz cures.	And I have never seen this disease come to adults, and all those whom I have seen die young; and for this reason it seems to me that we should be more cautious in the treatment of it.
Et je vis I enfant de coi li chiés estoit plains d’aigue, et li chief engroissoit chescun jor tant qu’il ne lou pooit sostenir; et crut tant li moistor qu’il fut mors, et ceste moistor si est assemblee desoz l’os sus lou syphac, entre lou keur et l’os; et li ovraiges si est telz se li moistor est entre lou keur et l’os, et li apostemes est petis, que tu fendes emmi lou chief une fendure large; et soit ausi longe com II nous, tant que li mostor corre; et vez ci la forme dou spatumile:	And I saw a child whose shoulder was plain with water, and the head grew heavier every day until he could no longer hold it up; and so much moisture gathered between the shoulder blade and the bone that it came to the surface, splitting the skin; and let there be such a distance between them as there is in us, while the moisture runs; and see here the shape of the splint:
Se li moistor est plus creue, et li aposteme soit plus grans, si fai II fendures en maniere d’une croix, selonc ceste forme:	If the moisture is deeper, and the abscess is larger, then make two incisions in the form of a cross, according to this shape:
Et se li moistor est desoz l’os, et li signes que tu vois les commissures dou chief overtes de chescune partie, et li aigue saut fuer quant tu la presses de ta main au dedens, et ceu ne t’est mie reponut: si covient que tu fendes enmi lou chief III fendures selonc ceste maniere:	If the moisture has broken the bone, and the signs you see are that the cheekbones are out of place on either side, and the fluid springs out when you press it with your hand, and does not return: then you should make three incisions along the cheekbone in this way:
Et aprés l’incision estrai la moistor toute fuers.	And after the incision, remove all the moisture.
Aprés estraint les fendures de drapelz et de poudres, et i met vin et oile, et laisse ensi jusc’a cinquieme jor; puis le deslie, et cure la plaie par tentes et par oignemens, et laisse estraindre le chief egaument, et done mengier au malaide viande seche de poc de moistor tant que li membre soit confortez et sanez.	After that, remove the bandages and powders, and put wine and oil on it, and leave it like that for five days; then remove it, and treat the wound with poultices and ointments, and let the head heal evenly, and feed the patient dried meat in small amounts of moisture until the member is comfortable and healthy.
Et une autre maniere d’incision est que tu regardes ou apert li grandor de l’aposteme, et li assemblé de l’aigue; car aucune fois est elle devant; aucune fois derrier; aucune fois en destre; et aucune fois en senestre.	And another way to incise is that you look at the opening of the anus, and the gathering of the needle; because there is never before; never behind; never on the right; and never on the left.
Taille donques lai ou li aposteme apert, et l’emplissement de l’aigue, et lou fent selonc ce que tu en as le pooir; et warde que tu ne coper l’artere; et veigne flun de sanc, si que li malaides muere dou decorrement de sanc et de l’evacuation de moistor.	So cut there where the anus opens, and the thread gathers, and do as you are able; and beware that you do not cover the artery; and be careful of blood loss, so that the patient dies from blood loss and from the evacuation of moisture.
de reume	In summary:
Quant il avient a aucun une maladie qui est apelee «catarre» as eulz ou au pis, et li maladie est anciainne, et li cure de medicine ne profite mie, adonques li derraine cure si est li cauteres avec ceu c’on li copera les II arteres.	When someone has a disease called "catarrah" or "phthisis," and the disease is old, and the medical treatment does not benefit, then the following treatment is good: cauterize with fire.
Il covient donques, cant tu les vues coper, que li malaides faice rere son chief; aprés li frotte lou leu d’un drapel aspre tant que les arteres aperent, puis estraingne li malaides son col a tout I drapel; puis regarde ou li voine bait, et li leus de l’une et de l’autre sont aprés les oreilles, et poc sont reponues; puis signe les leus d’enche, puis cope l’une et l’autre d’un spatumile agut de II pars, tant que li taille veigne jusc’a l’os, et ceu soit par lou large dou chief.	When the patient's vision is blurred, and the disease is old and medicine is of no use, then the following treatment is good: cauterize with fire. When you have covered their eyes, make the patient raise his head; after that, scrub the place where the arteries are visible with an rough cloth until they appear; then remove the patient's hair from all parts; then look at where the vein runs, and the veins on both sides of the nose are stretched; then cut them with a sharp knife, so that it comes to the bone, and do the same with this one;
Et se tu vues, boute le spatumile desoz l’artere et la cope au desus, en taillant ausi com II dois au traver.	And if you see, plug the tube up the artery and cover it with a bandage, cutting too far as I have said above.
Et quant li voinne est copee, si saut li sans en haut continuelment fuers.	When the vein is covered, let the blood flow continuously upward.
Et se li artere n’apert au sentir, si covient que tu mesures la quantiteit de l’espaice de III dois, puis seigne d’enche et fent jusc’a l’os; et ceu qu’il covient dou sanc mettre fuers si est VI c/, et par aventure un poc plus ou moins, selonc ce que li malaides puet soffrir, et la repletion de l’artere; puis regarde la plaie: s’il remaint sus l’os point dou syphac, si le cope que apostemes chaus n’i veigne, puis estrain la plaie et lie, et la cure d’oignement tant qu’ele soit sanee.	And if the artery does not open to the sense, then measure the quantity of the space of III parts, then sign of incision and cut down to the bone; and what is necessary to let the blood flow outside so it is VI c/, and perhaps a little more or less, according to what the patient can suffer, and the repletion of the artery; then look at the wound: if it remains on the bone no syphac, if the apostemes bandages do not come off, then extract the wound and wrap it up, and the cure with ointment until it is healed.
de emigrainne	of grinding
Quant emigrainne anciaine vient, et catarre agut, por les moistors des larmes et les chalors en temples et sode anciene forsenee et semblans choses, et il est medicinez par manieres de cures de medicine et tout ceu ne li profite mie, si estraions les arteres des temples et lou cauterizons, si com nos avons conteit.	When the old man comes, and has catarrh, because of the moisture from tears and heat in the temples and old sores and similar things, he is medicined with the methods of medicine and all that does him no good, then we extract the arteries from the temples and cauterize them, as we have told.
Et li maniere de l’estraction d’elles si est que li malaides faice rere les poilz de ses temples, et entende a l’artere qui apert en la temple, car elle apert bien par son batement, et est poc reponue fuers que en aucuns homes qui sont trop froit; et s’elle est reponue, si estraigne son col li malaides d’aucuns drapelz, puis frote le leu d’aucun aspre drap, et arose le leu d’aigue chaude tant que li artere apere manifestement; puis pren le spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	And the way of extracting them is that the patient should let the hairs on his temples grow again, and listen to the artery that opens in the temple, because it opens well by its beating, and is not too tight except in some men who are too cold; and if it is re-tightened, then take off his collar from some sheets, then rub the place with any rough cloth, and raise the place with hot water until the artery appears clearly; then take the spatumile where this is the form:
puis escorche le cuir legierement tant que tu veignes a l’artere, puis la trai en haut as pinceures, et la depart bien des toiles que sont desoz li de chescune partie; et se li artere est subtilz, si la torne a la pointe de l’uncine, puis la cope de celle partie selonc la quantiteit des II chiés.	puis escorche le cuir legierement tant que tu veignes a l'artere, puis la trai en haut as pinceures, et la depart bien des toiles que sont desoz li de chescune partie; et s'il est subtilz, si la tornetz a la pointe de l'uncine, puis la cope de celle partie selonc la quantité des II chiés.
Car s’elle n’est copee, si ne saut mie li sans dou tout en tout.	For if it is not cut, then it will not be safe in all respects.
Et trai dou sanc des VI c/, jusc’a III; et se li artere est grans, si covient que tu la lies en II leus d’un fil double fort de soie, que porriture n’i veigne devant le soudement de la plaie, et veigne decorremens de sanc; puis cope la superfluiteit qui est entre les II liiens en celle houre meisme, et puis, se tu vues, si lou cauterize dou cautere cutellaire jusc’a l’os tant que li chiés soient copez; et c’est li muedre oevre, se li malaides n’a fievre et il est de chaude complexion.	And cut the blood of the VI degrees down to III; and if the artery is large, then bind it with two strong silk threads, so that bleeding does not occur before the wound heals, and let the excess flow between the II lines in this very hour, and then, if you see fit, then cauterize with the fire cautery up to the bone as soon as the II lines are cut; and this is the operation of the muedre oevre, provided that the patient does not have a fever and has a warm complexion.
Car li cauteres est aide por finir les moistors: por ceu est il de plus grant aide as moistors.	For the fire cautery is aid for ending moisture: for this is more great aid than for moisture.
Ou il covient por l’estraction des arteres que om emplisse lou leu de viel coton et mette on sus tentes bien faites; et quant on les desliera, si soit curez de medicines seches que font naistre char, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se sans cort de l’artere tant dis com tu i oevres, si te haste dou coper par cautere, ou tu emple lou leu de vitriole et l’estrain a ta main que li sans soit estainchiez; et se tu n’as ceu present, si met sor le leu ton doit tant que li sans soit congelez, et arose le leu d’aigue froide tant que li sans cesse, et soit estraint si com il covient; et ceu qui est muedre et plus legier en l’estraction de l’artere est que tu cauterizes la voinne de cest cautere trenchant de II pars, mais li trenchant soient bien espés por warder plus longement lor chalor.	For in the extraction of arteries it is fit that one fill the place with fine cotton and put on well-made tent; and when you separate them, so be cured with dry medicines that make char, and with tents, until they are healthy; and if without a cover of the artery there be much pain, then hasten to cauterize by fire, or employ the leach of vitriol and strain it in your hand that the pain be taken away; and if you have not this present, put on the place your thumb so long as the pain cease, and rise the leach of cold water so long as the pain continue, and be extracted as it is fit; and that which is sore and lighter in extraction of the artery is that you cauterize the vein with a sharp edge from two sides, but let the cutting be well-spaced that it last longer on the heat.
Car quant li estrumens est trop tenves, si tient moins sa chalor.	For when the instrument is too soft, then it holds less heat.
Et doit avoir entre les II coutelz I doit de gros d’espaice, et puis quant tu as signiet d’enche les II leus, et tu mes lou fer ardant sus tant qu’il viegne jusc’a l’os, et cope la voinne en II leus; et soient esloigniet entre les II chiés car il n’est mie soudez de cest cautere dou tout en tout; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	And it should have between the two tools a space of one inch, and then when you have struck on both sides, and you put hot iron on until it comes to the bone, and split the vein in two places; and keep the two joints apart because it is not soldered with this cautery from top to bottom; and this is the form of the cautery:
des larmes	tears
Quant les larmes des eulz sont dessendans des voinnes que sont sus lou test dou chief de fuer, et il ne profite mie cure de medicine c’on i faice, et tu vois la faice dou malaide enrougir, et sent ou front ambulation si com de fremis; et sui oil sont tenve et moiste si que li poil des papieres sont cheut, et sont eschaufees les papieres, et escorchies de l’ardor des larmes, si ait mestier de ceste cure.	When the tears of the eyes come down from the veins that are on the forehead of the head of force, and this medicine does not benefit, and you see the face of the patient turn black, and feel a feverish movement as if it were trembling; and if the hair of the brows is loose and moist so that the hair falls, and the brows are burnt, and scarred by the heat of the tears, then it is necessary to use this cure.
Et l’apelerent li ancien «cure contuse», et est que tu faices a rere au malaide qui a ceste maladie les poilz qu’il ait ou front, puis li fai III fendures ou front igalment selonc la longesce dou front; et soit l’une des fendures ausi com II doi tout emmi lou front en avalant aval jusc’a neif, et les autres II as II costelz par desus les papieres, et te garde de l’incision des arteres que sont as II costez par desus les papieres; et aloigne ta main de la continuation des II mandibules, et soit chescune plaie la quantiteit de III dois au traver joins; et aies apparillie une piece d’esponge et mout de drapelz ses por essuer lou sanc, puis boute le spatumile agut de II pars de coi ci est li forme:	And they called it the ancient 'cure for contusions', and this is what you do to the patient who has this disease in his or her hair; then he makes III cuts on the hairline evenly according to the length of the forehead; and one of the cuts is like II two everything cut off the forehead moving upward until it reaches the nose, and the other two are II at II costules above the paper, and keep from cutting the arteries that are at II costules above the paper; and remove your hand from the continuation of the II mandibles, and each wound has III degrees joined together; and you arrange a piece of sponge and mop up his blood, then pour the spatumil obtained from II parts where this form is:
des l’incision qui est dever la temple jusc’a la seconde incision; et escorche tout le keur qui est entre les II fendures a tot lou syfac qui est sus l’os, puis fai autreteil des la moiene incision jusc’a l’autre seconde, et puis estrai fuer cest spatumile.	After the incision that is to be made on the temple until the second incision; and peel off all the scabs that are between the II cuts until all the bone is exposed, then do the same thing from the middle incision until the other second one, and then remove this spatumil thoroughly.
si boute en la premiere fendure l’estrument qui est apelez «cultellaire», et est tresbien trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part est souef, ne mie trenchans, et c’est li forme:	if you dip the instrument which is called "culteller", and it is very well sharpened on one side, and on the other side is smooth, not sharpened, and this is its shape:
Et met le costeit taillant vers la char aerse au keur, et lou costeit souef vers l’os, et lou boute tant qu’il veigne a la moiene fendure.	And place the edge-biting towards the back at the corner, and the edge-biting smooth towards the bone, and dip it so that it comes to the middle cut.
Et cope toz les vasselz que dessendent dou chief as eulz tant que l’incision soit continue jusc’a ceu qui apert dou keur, et puis autreteil fai en la moiene fendure jusc’a l’autre defuer; et puis estrai dou sanc igalment, et espresse lou leu por le sanc pris; puis met en chescune fendure une tente de viel coton, et met sus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile et en aisil, et garde que apostemes chaus n’i veigne; et au tier jor deslie lou liien, et i amenistre grant planteit d’aigue tede, puis lou cure d’oignement basilicon avec oile roset, et d’autres cures dont on cure plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And cover all the vessels that descend from the top at the edge with long hairs until the incision is continuous up to that which opens at the corner, and then another way: make the incision in the middle as much as it takes; and then remove the hair evenly, and express the blood clearly; then put in each incision a little of veiled cotton, and put wet drapings made of wine and oil and honey, and keep so that the abscesses do not come out; and on the third day loosen the bandage, and put there a great deal of cold water, then cure with basilicon ointment made of oil and rosewater, and other cures for wounds, as much as it is cured.
dou reume des eulz	Dou reume des eulz
Quant a aucun vienent catarre agut acostumeement, et tu vois les eulz tenves et petis, et afoiblir la veue, et les papieres brulees; et li poil chieent, et ou chief en parfont a dolor ague, et li malaides esternue; adonques saiches par ces accidens que celles matieres et cil catharre ne vient fuer que de maintes voines, et li muedre cure que i est, si est ceste.	When there is no catarrh of long-standing habit, and you see the hairs thin and small, and a weakening of vision, and burnt paper; and the hair falls out, and at which pain the patient suffers, and he sneezes; then know that from these accidents, those matters and this catarrh do not come except from many veins, and the cure that is given to it, if such is the case, is this.
Et est que tu comande au malaide a rere son front, puis fai une grant fendure emmi lou front, et une autre dou large I poc.	And you command the patient to re-open his forehead, then make a deep cut across the forehead, and another from one side to the other.
Et comence des la fendure de la temple senestre a la temple destre, et soit li incision jusc’a l’os; et esloigne ta main des ners des temples que muevent au mengier; et quant li os est descovers, si essue tout le sanc a une esponge, et puis desevre entre les II levres de la fendure et i met coton viel, et tentes de lin; puis lie desus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile, et te garde d’aposteme chaut; quant il est ostez, si covient que tu frottes l’os tant que chars i comence a naistre, puis le cure de choses exiccatives, que font enjanrer char.	And you begin the cut from the left temple to the right, and make an incision up to the bone; and keep your hand away from the nerves that move when he hiccups; and when the bone is exposed, if you dip all the blood in a sponge, and then wash between the II lips of the incision with cotton wetted with wine and oil, and you keep it hot with a hot cloth; when it is healed, if you rub the bone until it starts to grow again, then cure it with drying things, which cause hiccups.
En teil maniere: pren II parties de flor de froment, et de colofoine IIII parties, et en fai emplaustre; et l’aministre en ces plaies por enjanrer char per tout.	In this manner: take two parts of flour and three parts of colofone and make a paste; and administer this to the wounds in order to stop pain throughout.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	the bulging of the ears
Tout ceu que chiet ens oreilles est une des IIII choses: ou grains, ou beste, ou piere de mine ou semblans chose si com fer; ou semence, si com jaisses, feves, pois; ou chose defluans si com aigue et aisilz et semblans choses.	All that hangs from ears is one of the four things: grain, beast, stone, or similar thing as iron; seed, as oats, beans, peas; flowing thing as water and similar things.
Quant il chiet en l’oreille piere ou autre maniere de chose que ne s’ajoste mie a l’oreille, ne ne croist en l’oreille, si met l’oreille au solel.	When it hangs in the ear a stone or other thing that does not fit into the ear, do not put the ear to the sun.
Se tu vois la piere, si distille aucun poc d’oile violet ou oile de sisament, puis i amenistre extraction; et lou fai esternuer de condisi, et li estoupe les narines quant li esternuemens vient, et met entor l’oreille pieces de drapelz ou laine; et estent l’oreille au desus.	If you see the stone, do not pour in any oil of violet or oil of sesame, then perform extraction; and when the stirring comes, it is to be pushed with a piece of cloth or wool; and place the ear upside down.
Mout de fois vient fuer par ceste cure; et s’elle ne vient fuer, se li amenistre extraction as pinceures subtilz, de coi ci est li forme:	Mouth times comes through with this treatment; and if it does not come through, you must give it a subtle extraction, from which there is the form:
S’elle saut fuer as pinceures, c’est boin; se ceu non, si amenistre extraction a l’oncine subtil de petite doubleure; et s’elle ne saut par ceu, si fai une caine d’arain et boute lou chief de la cainne ou pertuis de l’oreille fort, et estoupe ceu qui est entor la cainne de cire mole si que li vens n’i puisse entrer avec la cainne; puis le trai fuer forment, car mout de fois vient fuer si com nos avons dit; et s’elle ne vient fuer en teil maniere, si prent glut de coi en prent les oisiaus, et met en som aucun estrument qui soit a point por ceu faire, et met un poc de coton entor; puis presse le glut sus la piere ou quel chose que ce soit, et trai fuer.	If it comes through with the pinches, it is good; but if not, give extraction to the soft one with a small double edge; and if it does not come through in this way, make a hole of air and bottle up chief of the hole or pierce of the ear very well, and stop what is inside the hole with soft wax so that the wine cannot enter with the hole; then treat firmly, for many times comes through as we have said; and if it does not come through in some way, take glut of what in taking the hairs, and put to some instrument which is right for this, and put a little cotton inside; then press the glut on the stone or something, and treat firmly.
Et s’elle ne saut fuer de toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si te haste de fendre l’oreille ainsois que aposteme chalz i veigne, et spasme; et li maniere de la fendure si est que tu faices premier sainier lou malaide de la cephalique, et estrai dou sanc selonc la mesure de sa vertu, puis fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains et li torne l’oreille au desus, et fent une petite fendure en la racine de l’oreille a la graisse ou leu dependant; et soit li fendure ausi com une lune, tant que tu viegnes a la piere, puis l’oste selonc ton pooir, et la suce hastanment a ta bouche; et la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if she does not recover from all these things that we have said, then you hasten to split the ear so that it splits, and spasms; and the way of the split is that you first heal the patient from the headache, and draw blood according to the measure of its virtue, and then put the patient between your hands and turn the ear upwards, and make a small split in the root of the ear to the fat where it depends; and let the split be like a moon, until you come to the stone, then grind it according to your power, and suck it into your mouth; and cure him until he is well.
Et se c’est grains qui est ens et il enfle, si aministre extraction; et si’il ne puet issir, si amenistre I spatumile tenve subtil selonc ceste forme:	If it is a grain that is stuck and it swells, then administer extraction; and if it cannot come out, then administer the slimy spitumation according to this form:
et amenistre incision de celui grain.	and make the incision of that seed.
Mais ne faire mie ceu quant tu penses que li grains est moistes por la moistor de l’oreille, tant que tu en aies fait maintes pieces; puis l’estrai as pinceures subtilz et au succier, si com nos avons dit, si que li estractions soit aligie.	But do not make this incision when you think that the grain is moist due to the moisture of the ear, until you have made many pieces; then extract them with great care and precision, as we have said, so that the extractions are orderly.
En l’aigue donques que chiet en l’oreille covient que li malaides use d’esternuement de condisi premiers, et ample l’oreille de viel coton.	Therefore, when a person has a headache, it is appropriate that the patient use the first treatment of cold water, and wide open the ear with old cotton.
Et soit gisans sus celle oreille meisme ou li aigue est.	And be careful about that ear where the water is.
s’elle saut fuer per ceu, c’est boin.	if it does not drain well, it is good.
se ceu non, si prent maintes pieres selonc li longesce de ton doit tenves et legieres, et les eschaufe un poc au feu; et em mette li malaides une ou pertus de son oreille, et saille sus i. de ses piez d’autre part, et fiere d’une autre piere sus la piere qui est en l’oreille; et ne cesse de faire ceu de piere em piere tant que li aigue isse toute fuer, et ensi saut elle toute fuer; et se tu vues, si prent I jonc, et boute l’un des chiés en l’oreille, et l’autre chief emprent de feu tant que li plus dou jonc soit ars; puis refai autreteil d’autres jons tant que li aigue isse toute, si com nos avons dit en la piere.	if it does not drain well, take several small pieces of wood from his hand one after the other and burn them slightly on the fire; and put one of them in his ear, and push up another piece of wood from the ear, and do not stop making these pieces of wood until the water is completely drained, and in this way it will be completely drained; and if you see that, take a small piece of wood, and bottle one of the ears, and burn the other one slightly until half of the piece of wood is burned; then remake another piece of wood from the other ear until all the water is gone, as we said before.
En l’estraction de la beste, s’elle est de petit cors, si com puce et semblans chose, cure la si com nos avons dit en la division; mais s’elle est de grant cors c’on la puisse sentir, si amenistre extraction de pinceures; et c’est li chose plus legiere a oster qui soit en l’oreille.	In the extraction of the beast, if it is a small horn, such as a flea or similar thing, treat it as we have said in the division; but if it is a large horn that one can feel, then extract it with tweezers; and this is the lighter thing to remove that is in the ear.
En l’estraction des vers enjanrez as oreilles, quant tu lou cures si com nos avons dit en la division et ou traitier des distillations, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu regardes l’oreille au soleil: s’il i apert nulz vers, si les trai as pinceures subtilz, et s’il n’aperent, si prent la cainne de coi ci est li forme:	In the extraction of worms from the ears, when you treat them as we have said in the division and in the treatment of distillations, and the cure does not benefit, then you should look at the ear in the sun: if there are no worms, then extract them with fine tweezers, and if there are none, take hold of the hair by which it is shaped.
Et soit estroite desoz et large desus.	It should be tight below and wide above.
Et boute lou plus subtil chief en l’oreille selonc la quantiteit de la soffrance dou malaide, puis succe forment a tot la caine; fai ceu sovent tant que tuit li ver issent.	And fill the small channel in the ear with a soft substance according to the amount of pain suffered by the patient, and then suck it out completely; do this often until all the worms come out.
Et s’il n’obeissent a issir, si estoupe entor la cainne de coton si com j’ai dit en la piere; et s’il ne saillent fuer si com nos avons dit, si aministre distillations que li ancien ont esprovees en l’ocision des vers, et tu les troveras ou traitier des distillations; et si distille tes oiles et tes medicines en l’oreille a tout cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme si com tu vois:	And if they don't obey by stretching out the cotton string as I said on the stone; and if it doesn't flow out strongly as we have said, administer distillations that the elders have experienced in the lancing of worms, and you will find them or treating with distillations; and if you distil your oils and medicines into all this instrument, from which this shape comes as you see:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain estrois desoz a I petis pertuis, et desus overs por distiller; et por presser dedens la distillation a I estrument d’arain bien fait por ceu, et se tu vues pren I raseur et envoloupe entor la pointe avenanment coton; puis i giete ton oile ou ton jus, et ceu que tu vues de tes medicines en la cainne, et li caine soit en l’oreille; puis boute dedens lou raseur a tout lou coton, et presse ta main tempreement tant que li oile soit distilleit ou chevement de l’oreille; et lou sente li malaides dedens, et soit li distillations I poc eschaufee au feu ainsois c’on la distille en l’oreille; et garde qu’elle ne soit trop froide, car li medicine ne seroit mie si bone.	And if there is silver or gold, open up the small holes, and above them to distil; and to press inside the distillation into the golden instrument that has been well made for this, and when you see him take a razor and wrap it around the tip with cotton; then pour your oil or juice, and whatever you see of your medicines in the string, and let the string be in the ear; then bottle up the razor into all the cotton, and press your hand gently until the oil is distilled or the ear is chewed; and have the patient smell it inside, and let the distillations be slightly heated on the fire as they are distilled in the ear; and watch that they are not too cold, for the medicine would not be so good.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	of the ear lobes
Aucun enfant naissent qui n’ont nul pertus ens oreilles; et ceste meisme chose avient as homes par estoupement de plaie, ou de char nee dedens l’oreille, et cist estoupemens vient aucune fois em parfont en l’oreille, si c’on ne lou puet veoir; et aucune fois avient I poc defuer lou pertus, et lou voit om bien.	No child is born who does not have some imperfection in their ears; and this same thing happens to men because of an ear injury or a cart wheel inside the ear, and this ear injury often comes completely into the ear, so that it cannot be seen; and there is no such thing as a small defect, and he can see very well.
Celle donques que vient em parfont, si c’on ne la puet veoir, est de grief sanation em plusors dispositions, et en cele c’on voit covient que tu mettes l’oreille dou malaide au soleil; et regarde dedens: se tu vois l’opilation apparent, si la oevre a tot cest spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	So that it comes completely into the ear, so that it cannot be seen, is a great treatment in many conditions, and in this you must put the patient's ear to the sun; and look inside: if you see the operation apparent, if the work has completely removed this sputum from which this form comes:
Et soit agus et trenchans devant et derrier tout plain, si qu’il ne blece l’oreille; se li opilation est de char nee ou cors de l’oreille, si la tien as pinceures subtilz, et la cope legierement, tant que celle chars soit toute ostee.	And be it on the front and back completely plain, so that it does not scar the ear; if the operation is a cart wheel or a corral inside the ear, if it holds the subtle stains, and gently scrape it until the cart wheel is all bony.
Et se li opilations est em parfont en l’oreille, si pren I raseur subtil legier et l’eschaufe un petit au feu, puis li met ou cors de l’oreille.	And if the wart is in perfect shape in the ear, then take a fine and light razor and heat it slightly on fire, then place the ring of the ear.
Se tu sens l’opilation dont li malaides sent grieteit a l’oïr, perce legierement, et garde que tu ne grever les ners de l’oreille; puis met en l’oreille une tente selonc la largesce dou pertus, et la moille en l’oignement egyptien.	And if you feel the wart in the ear, pierce lightly and do not harm the nerves of the ear; then put a thread according to its width, and moisten it with Egyptian ointment.
Fai ceu aucun jor tant que li plaie soit soudee, ou tu pren une tente et la moille en aigue rose, et poudre sus vitriole broiet; et se tu vois enflee l’oreille, si couvient que tu traies la tente et remue une autre tente moillie en cerote qui soit fait d’oile roset et de cire, tant que li enfleure soit ostee; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Do not make it a daily habit until the wound is healed, or you take a thread and moisten it with rosewater, and powder with vitriolic broth; and if you see the ear oozing, let it drain by covering it with another thread moistened with cera-rose oil that has been made from rosewater and wax, until the discharge stops; then treat it until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si plonge une esponge et drapelz en aigue froide, et le met sus l’oreille, et use d’autres cures qui oste lou decorrement de sanc qui sont ou traitier des destillations.	And if the pain comes on, dip a sponge and cloth in cold water, and put it on the ear, and use other remedies that stop the pain of the ear which are or treat the distillation.
de la char des papieres	of the wood of the papers
Cist althelul que vienent em papieres des eulz quant ils sont moiste et sont sec, si covient que tu les estendes de tenailles et de pinceures, et le cope d’un spatumile de ses racines; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet.	Cut the roots of these papers when they are moist and then dry, so that you extend them with pliers and tweezers, and dip them in vinegar. Then put it on the spot with vitriol bromide.
