de l’issue de l’oil	de the issue of the oil
Quant li eulz apert fuer dou tout en tout, et il ne vient point de destorbier au nef, ne amenuisement, si covient que tu lies lou malaide; puis le saine, puis li met ventouses ou haterel sens ferir por succier, puis met sus l’oil I liien fait d’acaice et de aloe et d’encens et de sarcocolle, et puis estrain l’oil, et l’emplaustre sus de bendes et de drapelz; et li maniere des drapelz si est que tu preignes drapelz assez molz, et double chescun en IIII, et puis met l’un sus l’autre selonc la quantiteit que li eulz en ait mestier; puis l’estrain par desus d’un bendeil dur forment, et rencomence les ventouses por succier sens ferir; puis oste les ventouses et laisse l’oil estraint jor et nuit, et se li liiens amolist, si covient que tu l’estraignes mout; puis oste lou liien aprés le jor et la nut, et se tu vois l’oil repairier, c’est boin; se ce non; si rencomence l’emplaustre et les drapelz et lou liien et les ventouses tant qu’il soit sanez.	de the issue of the oil
dou derrompement de toile uvee	and then tie a bandage around it, and then wrap it in soft cloth; and then put the oil on it, made from resin, myrrh, and incense, and then strain the oil, and then apply it with bandages and cloths; and the way to make the bandages is that you twist enough soft cloth, and double each one into four; and then put one on top of the other according to the amount of cloth needed; and then strain the oil through a hard cloth, and then start using the suction cups again without hurting; then remove the suction cups and leave the oil strained for a day and night, and if it thickens, you should strain it more; then remove the bandage after the day and the night, and if you see that the oil has healed, it is good; if not, then start applying the resin and cloth and bandages and suction cups until it heals.
Quant disruptions vient en la toile uvee, puis apert, et vient fuer des papieres si com I grain de resins, et est espoantauble a veoir; adonques se tu la vues coper, li ovraiges est telz que tu boutes une aguille en la racine des la partie desoz jusc’a celi desus, puis boute une autre aguille ou il ait I fil double des la partie dou larmier; et la fai percier, et laisse la premiere aguille selonc la disposition; puis cope lou leu dou fil double et lie une partie de l’uve entor, et l’estraint bien, puis estrai l’aguille et met sus l’oil lainne moillie en abun d’uef; et le laisse tant que li filz chiece avec l’uve, puis cure l’oil de choses confortans tant que li plaie soit sanee; et aucune fois li plaie est restrainte par l’uve chescune part d’un cercle de drap, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	When disruptions come to the woven veil, then cut, and comes up from the paper as if a grain of resin, and is expected to be seen; so if you cover it with a view, the weavings are such that you push a needle into the root of the part of the sown until over there, then push another needle where there is double thread from the part of the armier; and let it pierce, and leave the first needle according to the arrangement; then cover the place of the double thread and tie one part of the uve around, and tighten it well, then extract the needle and put on the other oil wet in honey; and leave it until the thread bumps with the uve, then treat the oil for comforting things until the wound is healed; and never restrict the wound by a piece of cloth each part of a circle as long as it is healed.
Et se li eulz done grant apparance, si le perce au spatumile subtil qui viegne em parfont de l’oil, et corre la moistor albuginé et dessende li eulz, et entre ens tantost; puis l’estrai tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the hairs have a good appearance, then pierce them with a fine needle that comes from oil in perfection, and run the moisture albinized and dry the hairs, and enter so quickly; then extract it until it is healthy.
de la bowe de l’oil	of the bow of oil
Ceste maladie qui est apelee «alcunnati» nen est fuers que bowe qui est assemblee en l’oil, semblant a aigue dessendant, et ce n’est mie aigue; et li maniere de l’apparance de l’ovraige si est que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege appareilliet et droit, puis prent le chief entre tes mains de II pars, et lou muef tant que tu voies la bowe venir au desus a tes eulz; puis soit ens fichie, et ne dessende et soit descombree li lumiere, et voie li malaides les choses si com il soloit; et s’elle ne dessent desoz, saiches que c’est aigue, et se li dessendemens de la bowe n’est appareilliez si com nos avons dit.	This disease, which is called "alcunnati," is nothing but a bow that is assembled in oil, resembling water descending, and not being water; and the manner of the appearance of dislocation so that you sit the patient on II seats apparelled and upright, then take the chief between your hands from both sides, and move it as you see the bow come up to your hairs; then pull it off firmly, and do not descende and be broken the light, and see the patient's things so as it should; and if it does not descend, know that it is water, and the descending of the bow is not apparelled as we have said.
si fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, puis prent le spatumile subtil et fent sus la toile cornee I poc par la continuation de la conjunctive avec la toile cornee et la corone, tant que li bowe isse; et quant elle ert issue, si distille en l’oil aigue chaude mellee a miel, ou aigue ou fenugreic est boillis et miel, puis soit curee d’autre cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	If you put the patient between your hands, then take the subtle spatula and make an incision in the corneal layer along with the membrane and crown, until the bowels come out; and when they come out, pour into the hot oily honey or fenugreek soup, and cure from another cure as long as it is well.
des aigues de l’oil	of the oil
Nos avons jai les semblances des aigues en la division, et ceu qu’il covient por percier; si en oevre selonc la santeit.	have the appearance of needles in division, and what is appropriate to pierce; if it is done according to health.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains croisiet, fuers de la lumiere por le soleil, et li lie l’oil sain et estreint mout fort; puis met la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre se li eulz est senestres, ou a ta main destre se li eulz est destres; puis prent en ta main destre, se li eulz est senestres, l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda», ou a ta main senestre, se li eulz est destre; puis met la pointe de l’estrument delez la corone par la groissece d’un rait en celle blenchor de l’oil a la partie dou menor larmier, puis boute l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda» vertuousement, et trestorne ta main tant qu’il perce en la blenchor de l’oil, et sente que almagda viegne a la chose vuide; et covient que li mesure de la voie almagda soit au parfont de la mesure des l’espaice qui est des la prunele jusc’a la fin de la noirour; et c’est li corone de l’oil; si verras l’os en celle papiere por la clarteit de la toile cornee, et pues met l’estrument jusc’a leu ou li aigue est, puis l’espresse desoz une voie aprés autre.	It is necessary that you put the patient between your hands, away from the light of the sun, and press the oil well; then take the paper of the oil with your left hand if the eyes are on the left, or with your right hand if the eyes are on the right; then take in your right hand, if the eyes are on the left, the instrument which is called "almagda", or in your left hand if the eyes are on the right; then put the point of the instrument on the crown by its thickness in that clear part of the oil up to the smaller limbus, and pour the instrument which is called "almagda" well, and turn your hand around until it pierces into the clear part of the oil, and see that almagda comes to the hollow thing; and it is necessary that the measure of the way of almagda be in perfect measure with the space which is from the plum-pulp up to the end of the blackness; and this is the crown of the oil; then you will see the bone in that paper by the clarity of the corneal layer, and then put the instrument there where the aigue is.
se li aigue dessent maintenant, si voit li malaides devant lui et l’estrument en son oil.	If he is lying down now, then see the patient before him and the instrument in his oil.
Aprés repose I petit, et se li aigue remonte la seconde voie, met la fuer avec l’estrument, et quant elle est ens fichie et ele ne monte, si estrai almagda legierement en tornoiant ta main poc et poc; et puis remette en aigue un poc de seil gemme, et leive de ceu l’oil dedens.	After rest for a short while, and having placed the instrument in his oil, and when it is firmly lodged and does not move up, then gently extract the almagre by turning your hand little by little; and then put back into the oil a little bit of gold, and remove it from there.
Puis met par defuer l’oil estoupes ou lainne moillie en oile roset et en abun d’uef, et lie avec l’oil sain.	Then put by hand the oil that is left or another wet thing in oil with a lot of turpentine, and bind it with the healthy oil.
Nos, et cil qui sont de nostre tens, mettons sus comin broiet avec abun d’uef.	Now, and those who are of our group, let us place on common ground with a lot of turpentine.
Et se almagda n’i puet entrer en l’oil par sa duresce, car il i a de teilz homes qui ont trop durs les eulz, si covient que tu preignes l’estrument qui est apelez «alberit», de coi ci est li forme:	And if the almagre cannot enter into the oil because of its hardness, for there are many men who have very hard hairs, then you must squeeze the instrument that is called "alberit", from which this form comes:
Et perce donques la conjunctive soulement, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, mais fai I leu subtil, puis i boute almagda, si com nos avons dit; et au complissement de l’uevre appareille au malaide I dorteur avenant, en coi il dorme sus son dos en I leu tenebrous; et soit deveez de toz movemens, et preigne legieres viandes, et ne mueve son chief ne a destre ne a senestre, et soit liiez selonc sa disposition jusc’a tier jor; puis le deslie en cele maison meisme tenebrouse, et esprueve sa veue, et lou fai veoir aucunes choses, et puis li remet lou lien jusc’a septime jor; et ne covient mie que tu faices ceu en l’oure de la cure ou aprés l’incision maintenant, mais il covient que tu aliges ceu, por ceu que li aigue monte hastanment.	Et perce donques la conjunctive soulement, et n'aler mie trop em parfont, mais fai I leu subtil, puis i boute almagda, si com nos avons dit; et au complissement de l'uevre apareille au malaide I dorteur avenant, en coi il dorme sus son dos en I leu tenebrous; et soit deveez de toz movemens, et preigne legieres viandes, et ne mueve son chief ne a destre ne a senestre, et soit liiez selonc sa disposition jusc'a tier jor; puis le deslie en cele maison meisme tenebrouse, et esprouve sa veue, et lou fai veoir aucunes choses, et puis li remet lou lien jusc'a septime jor; et ne covient mie que tu faisses ceu en l'oure de la cure ou aprés l'incision maintenant, mais il covient que tu aliges ceu, por ceu que li aigue monte hastanment.
se apostemes chaus vient, que tu desliies l’oil devant le septime jor, et l’adrece de ceu qui assouaige aposteme; et quant il est apaisiez, si deslie la veue et met sus sa faice I orilliet por covrir aucun jor, et soit adés en celle maison tenebrouse.	If an abscess breaks out before the seventh day, then let the oil be applied from the seventh day onwards by one who soothes an abscess; and when it has calmed down, then remove the poultice and place a patch on its face to cover it for that day, and remain in that dark house.
Et puis isse de la maison poc et poc, et se convertisse en ses cas; et saiches que nulz deciples ne se doit entremettre en cest cas.	And then little by little leave the house and become accustomed to it; and know that no doctor should interfere in this case.
Et uns vint a nos qui estoit de la Yrach, qui nos dist que en som pais faisoit om almagda perciet, a coi on succe l’aigue, mais toutevoie je n’en vis onques nul en nostre terre, ne je ne lou lis onques en livres des anciens; et par aventure c’est une novele chose.	And one came to us who was from the Land of Egypt, who told us that in their country a certain water is made to boil, which sucks up the liquid, but I have never seen such a thing in our land, nor do I find it in any of the books of the ancients; and perhaps it is a new thing.
Et ce sont les semblances des formes de almagda, por ceu que cil qui ne les conoit les voie; et soient d’arain proprement:	These are the appearances of the shapes of almagda, so that he who does not know them sees them as if they were made of stone.
Et soient li chief d’aus de ceste meisme subtiliteit, et li derriene en III angles ague.	And let the head of this mixture of subtility, and the behind three angles acute.
de la char sor le neis	of the horse's head on the neck
Aucune fois naissent ou neis chars ajostees diverses, de coi il i a aucunes qui semblent scorpions a mout de piez; et si i a de telz ou il ait char enchancree de fuxe color, et si a char souef de bone color.	There are times when the horse's head or neck is broken in various ways, so that it seems like scorpions from the foot of the foot; and if there are any such or there is a broken horse with a good color, and if there is a black horse.
En celle donques de ces chars qui est souef, et ne mie enchancree, covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains encontre lou soleil; et oevre ses narines, et giete l’oncine a celles chars, et les trai fuers; pues cope ceu que tu em pues sostenir au spatumile subtil agut d’une part, tant que tu saiches que celle char est toute ostee.	In the case of those horses that are broken but not entangled, it is necessary that you sit the patient between your hands toward the sun; and open his nostrils, and insert the hook into those horses, and tighten them firmly; for one can hold on to the delicate bone with the sharp hook from one side, as long as you know that this horse is all boned.
Et s’il en remaint aucune chose c’on ne puisse coper, si l’ovrez a tout I des estrumens subtil legierement, si qu’il n’i demoure rien; et se sans te sormonte, ou aposteme chaus, si lou secort si com il covient; et se c’est apostemes malignes, si te haste et lou cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez et soient ostees toutes les chars, puis giete ou neis aisil et aigue ou vin.	And if there is nothing left that cannot be covered, if you open it all with the sharp and light instruments, so that nothing remains; and if he rises up without any pain or ache, or if there are any malicious abscesses, then hasten and cauterize them so that they are all closed and boned, and then cut off or extract them easily and quickly or pierce them.
Se li neis oevre, et moistors en vient jusc’a palais, saiches qu’il est sanez; et se moistors ne perce si com il covient, saiches qu’il i a char nee en l’os desus, a coi li estrumens ne vient mie por taillier: adonques covient il que tu i boutes I fil de lin un poc gros, et soit noez de mains nous, et ait entre chescun nout d’espaice I doit ou moins; et mette li malaides lou chiés dou fil en son neif a som pooir, et traie en odorant tant qu’il viegne par lou neif dedens la bouche; et maintes fois font ensi li enfant as escoles, et c’est legiere chose a celui qui le vuet faire; puis tien le chief qui vient par lou neif a une main, et l’autre chief qui vient par la bouche a l’autre main, et saiche l’un aprés l’autre en soiant as nous qui sont ou fil.	If there is a headache, and moisture comes up to the palate, know that he is okay; and if the moisture penetrates as it should, know that there is no toothache in his bone, since the instrument does not cut: then you must put a piece of linen thread a little thick, and tie it tight with your hands, and leave some space between each knot or more or less; and put the child's hand on the thread at his power, and pull in smelling until it comes through his nose into his mouth; and many times do this to the child when he is at school, and it is a light thing for him who does it; then hold the head that comes through his nose with one hand, and the other head that comes from the mouth with the other hand, and feel one after the other as we are doing with the thread.
Fai ceu tant que tu saiches que li nout ont corrompue celle char, puis trai lou filz, essue le sanc, et moille lou fil en oignement egiptien, et le remet derechief au neis si com devant; fai ceu III jors ou plus, tant que li oignemens corrode tout ceu qui est demorez de char; et puis met ou neis une caine de plonc aucuns jors tant qu’il soit sanez, et s’il a mestier de medicines sechans, si en use; et c’est li forme de l’estrument por purgier lou chief, a coi on distille les oiles et les medicines ou neis:	Make it so that as long as you know the new wine has corrupted the barrel, then treat the child, wash the blood, and moisten the child with Egyptian ointment, and put it back in the neck right away as before; make it so that III days or more, as long as the ointments corrode whoever is delayed from the barrel; and then put a plug of plaster in the neck for some days until he is well, and if there is need for dry medicines, use them; and this is the form of the instrument for purging the head, where they distill oils and medicines in the neck:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, semblant a une lampe overte, si com une cainne, et li conduis ausi; et se tu vues, si fai une cainne close, et soit li estrumens plains por espurgier lou chief; et ait I mainche au chief por lou tenir quant on chaufe l’oile ou aucune liquor.	And be of silver or gold, resembling an open lamp, like a plug, and conduct it so; and if you see, make a closed plug, and be the instrument flat for purging the head; and I have many in the head to hold it when they heat oil or any liquid.
de la char sor le neis	the horse's back over the neck
Maintes fois naist au chief dou neis une maladie qui est apelee «telul», et croist et devient grans adés, tant qu’il est vis chose au regarder; et por ceu covient que tu lou copes au comencement, et l’oste tout fuer, puis met sor leu lou cautere ou la medicine ardant; et s’on le tarde a coper tant qu’il soit grans, si pren warde s’il est durs, de fuxe color, de povre sens: si ne lou touchier mie de fer car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, car quant on le cope aucune fois, si en vient grant malice au malaide; et se li apostemes est de soef touchement, non mie de fuxe color, et tu vois c’on le puisse tout coper, si vuide le malaide et lou cope sens paor, et cure le leu de choses sechans et restraignans.	Several times the horse's back caused a disease called "telul", and it grew and became very large, so that one can see it in the eye; and for this it is necessary to cut the head at the beginning, and then burn the bone completely, and then put fire on it; and if it is delayed to cut it until it becomes very large, then take care not to touch it with iron because it is a scorbutic wound; for when one cuts it, great evil comes to the patient; and the wound is of light touch, not of red color, and you can see that you can completely cut it, if you empty the patient and cut it without fear, and heal the head with dry and restraining things.
quant li neis est copez et cosus	When the neck is cut and seared
Saiches que quant solutions de continuation vient en une de ces cartillagines ovraiges, i profite poc, fuer que en aucuns homes.	It is known that when the soluions of the continuance come into one of these cartilage sovereignties, it profited little, but that in some men.
Il covient donques cant ceu avient a aucun, si regarde se li plaie est fresche a tout son sanc; et adonques ajoste les II levres a une costure, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se les levres sont ja desevrees d’une part et d’autre, si covient que tu escorches toutes les parties de lor keur tant qu’elles sainent, puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et l’estraint, et poudre sus poudre de sanc de dragon, et encens broiet; et met sus les poudres une piece d’emplaustre de fort ou d’autre emplaustre soudant, et le laisse tant qu’il chiece par lui, puis le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	It is necessary therefore to consider if there is any cause; so regard the wound is fresh in all its strength; and then join the two lips together at one seam, then heal them as long as they are healthy; and if the lips are torn on both sides, then it is necessary that you peel off all their skin as long as they heal, then join the two lips together at one seam, and bind it, and powder with dragon's blood powder, and incense broached; and put on the powders a piece of plaster of ferment or any other plaster then, and leave it to make it come out by itself, then cure with ointment as long as it is healthy.
Li maniere de la costure si est que tu assembles la solution: ou par aguilles, si com nos avons dit en la costure dou ventre; ou par fil, si com je le t’ai fait savoir.	The way to sew up an incision: so you gather the solution: either with needles, as we have said in the incision of the belly; or with thread, as I have told you.
des apostemes des levres	of the lips
A mains homes avient dedens les levres aposteme dur, semblans a grains de veces, et menor et plus grant; adonques couvient que tu tornes les levres, et fendes sus chescun nout, et le prent as pinceures et le cope en chescune partie; puis emple lou leu aprés l’incision de vitriole broiet, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; et puis lou leive d’aisil, et cure lou leu de choses seches tant qu’il soit sanez.	of the lips: at home, make a hole in the middle of the lip, resembling grains of sand, smaller and bigger; then, you must turn the lips, cut each one with a knife, and wrap them in cloth; then employ the vitriolic paste after scraping away the scabs; and then let it be, and cure the wound with dry things until it is healed.
de la char des gencives	of the teeth
Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent «albulus»; si covient que tu la sostienes as tenailles, et la cope a sa racine, et laisse corre la bowe ou le sanc; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet, ou autres poudres restraignans et desiccatives; et se celle char revient aprés l’incision, et maintes fois avient, si la cope la seconde fois, et la cauterize: si ne revient mie aprés le cautere; et ce sont les formes des estrumens por coper.	often times grows hair on the gums, which the old call "albulus"; if it is necessary to hold them with pliers, and cut off the root of the tooth, and let the blood flow; then apply vitriolic paste, or other powder that binds and dries; and if this hair comes back after the incision, and often times comes back, if they are covered again, and cauterized: if they do not come back after cauterization, and these are the shapes of the tools to cover them.
des sordens	of sorrows
Aucunes fois sont assemblees au chief des dens, dedens la bouche entre les gencives, escorces qui sont laides et aspres; et aucune fois sont li dent noir et citrin et vers, tant que li corruption vient a la gencive, et sont li dent puant; si covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, et ses chiés soit en ton saint, et reis les dens ou les escorces aperent, tant qu’il n’i demore rien; et ensi fai de la noiror et de la verdor, et de la jaunice et des autres taiches, tant qu’elles soient mondees; et s’on oste ceu que i est a la premiere rasion, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence a rere le secont jor et lou tier, tant que tu aies tout reis; et saiches que li dent ont mestier de diverses formes d’estrumens por reire, selonc ceu que li oevre lou demoustre, por ceu que li raseur dont on reit defuer les dens ont autres formes que cil dont on reit entre les dens; et cestes formes et autres soient avec toi appareillies.	of sorrows
Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire; car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	It is necessary when you cure the tooth of its pain that you wait to extract it as long as you can, for this is not good to do; because it is a very high substance until one has no excuse to extract it.
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant.	And then when the patient is constricted by the traktement, it is necessary that you are careful with the toothache.
Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu’elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent; et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l’avons ja veut faire a ces sainors; et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars; puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant qu’il soit bien eslochiés, puis i afferme bien les tenailles; et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu’il ne se mueve.	Often the pain leaves the patient, and he should be sure that it is a healthy tooth, and he has the right tooth pulled; but nevertheless the pain does not go away for this reason, until you have carefully scraped under the tooth with a sharp instrument on all sides; then he moves it slightly to the left or right, little by little, until it is well loosened, then he tightens the pliers well; and the head of the tooth in your good mouth, between your teeth, and hold it well so that it does not move.
Aprés estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et s’il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier.	After removing the tooth properly without breaking it, and if it does not come out, then take one of these instruments and knock it in slightly from each side, and move it a little; do this again until it comes out easily.
Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l’emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont; et si l’estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l’estraindre; et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	And if the jaw is tightened and swollen, fill it with cloth where the pain is; and if it is held firmly with pliers, so that it does not break when it is pulled, and carefully clean around the gum to loosen the tooth.
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere.	And do you well in mind that you do not break it, and remain a part of it, and return to the patient by the malice of the root greater pains of the first.
Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit; mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut; et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet; et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	And be careful that you do not do so as the ignorant surgeon does, who, by his haste and audacity, breaks the carriage sometimes, and does not administer any of those which we have spoken of; but brings it about sometimes by the quelling of that great disease for the roots from which they come out, or by the carriage which they break, as we have often wanted; and when the jaw is pulled, wash the place with wine or ale and silk; and let them run away without pain coming, so often comes, if you employ the place of vitriol; and if this does not work, cauterize it.
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent; et ce sont les formes:	The shapes of the instruments, for which it is necessary that the teeth do not touch each other, are long in length and thick in diameter, so that they do not double when you pull the tooth; and these are the forms:
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	And let them be thick limbs so that they do not bend when pulling, and let them be well made of iron, and let them have teeth to hold the tooth in place.
de la racine des dens	of the root of the teeth
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre I jor ou ij.,	When the root moves when pulling, it is necessary that you put cotton wet with oil on the place where you pull or rub.
tant que li leus soit amolis, pues i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne; et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	As long as the roots are smooth, for then the pliers that are called 'algefri' [smooth-toothed] seem to be a saw; and let them be made inside like a grindstone, and this is the shape:
Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l’estrument qui est apelez «althali», c’est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:	And if the roots do not want to come out with all these pliers, it is necessary that you uncover the whole thing around the root, and put the instrument that is called 'alhalith' [palsy-tooth], that is a saw; and this is the shape:
Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c’est boin; se ceu non, si t’aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:	And be it small or large so that he does not break, and his root jumps because of this, it is good; if not, if you help with all the instruments, from which the forms come afterwards:
Et si s’aide on de cest estrument qui ait II rains, de coi ci est li forme:	And if one helps himself with this instrument that has two heads, from which this is the form:
et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	and other iron tools that are in front in the rasion of teeth, and this instrument which seems a pair of large pliers, from which this is the form:
Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont; et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez; et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	and this instrument is out of the way that it cannot break, and know that many tools of teeth are; and also other instruments, which are not accounted for; and the wise masters carefully examine their own instruments, according to what their works and the illness show them, because there are many diseases where the old do not teach about instruments; and if it does not break the chariot or other bones on which it rests, if he seeks the right tools, which I have told you, and helps with gestures, from which this is the form:
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	And let it be large and well-fixed to hold the bone, so that it does not escape but can be held and removed; then return it to the place of medicine appropriate for this, and if there is putrefaction in the bone, and it is small, then use all this instrument:
Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer: adonques lou raie; et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a I petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	When the teeth do not appear to be in line with the natural shape of the jaw, and the form is ugly, especially in young women, you must know that the root is not in its right place, and it cannot be sewn or filed; then cut it off; and if it is attached to the tooth, take this instrument whose shape is like a small pick, and which is made of iron:
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	And take the cap and hold it firmly with your hands because of the hardness of the tooth, and so that you do not move the others, and if it seems that it can be filed, then use a file of this kind:
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles; et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece; puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	and is also like the lime with which we make needles; and in a lime bite and bite gently with the hand every day so that it does not move until it bites; then, at the end, to any razor, and its edge is too rough and it bleeds the tongue, then you have to sharpen the尖锐さまで so that it doesn't bleed the tongue or destroy speech.
quant li dent lochent	when the teeth come loose
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut; si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques; et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens; et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les II dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a I ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part; puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point; et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper.	when the teeth come loose from each other, whether by striking or by chewing, and the patient cannot press on anything without vomiting, and you have treated them with medicines that constrict, and it doesn't work; then you should restrain them with a gold thread, because silver threads turn green and rot, but gold threads never move; and make the thread neither too thin nor too thick, according to the amount of space between the teeth; and if you notice any gaps, take a thread and double it between two healthy teeth, then place the bridge between the teeth, whether there is one or more, until you tighten it securely up to the healthy tooth on the other side; then start again at the covering end, tightening gently and securely so that it doesn't move; and hold the ligature to the root of the tooth so that it can't escape.
Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue; et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil; si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des II dens sains, et des II meus, si com tu vois:	Then cut the heads of the threads with a pliers, and assemble them, and run them between the healthy tooth, and put them so that they do not scratch the tongue; and then leave them so tight as it can stay, and if they loosen, or the thread breaks, fasten it with another thread; if it stayed, and served so for all its time, and this is the form of the teeth and the figure of the insertion of the II healthy teeth, and the II bad ones, as you see:
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit; et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	Then, if the tooth is loose, put it back in its place, little by little, as we have said; and do not meddle with those who are not skilled or tolerant, and never make the shape of a tooth from ivory; and put it back in its place where it is defective, and fasten it as we have said, and let it stay and serve for a long time.
de coper lou liien de la lengue	of copper the tongue of the tongue
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi; ou par accident de plaie soudee; et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue; puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement; et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz; et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin; et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder.	Once there was a tongue that came out of its socket, whether by nature or by accident due to a wound; and the ovations are such that you open the mouth of the sick person, and put his head in your lap, and loosen the language; then cut the large nerve with an awl, as long as the tongue is dislocated from its place, and if there is pain or no pain, and it is due to a sudden wound, then grab the awl and cut the large nerve; and be careful that the incision is not too perfect, so that the artery that is behind; and when you have done this, if you lift up hot water and cold water, and put it on the tongue for a tent of linen; and scrub the sick person every night, so that the lees cannot close.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet; et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	And if the pain comes, then put vinegar on it; and if he doesn't go away, then cauterize with slow fire, which is good for him; then heal him with other treatments until he is well.
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre; et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre; et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer; puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you see a red or black or hard color there, so that the patient doesn't feel it, then don't touch it, because it is leprosy; and if it declines towards blenchor, and there is moisture, then put the oncine on it, and make it with a thin scythe, and deliver it from one side and the other; and if he does not go away to your help, then put vinegar on it as long as it is stained, and then return to your help until you pull all of it; then raise his head from there and from here, and heal him with other treatments until he is well.
des apostemes de la gorge	of the throat
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les II amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde: se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer.	No time comes from within the throat called "godath", and they are properly called "II amandres", and when you cure them, as we said in the division, and they are not healed, if take care: that is a hard-to-heal, small-sized, and pale warts, do not touch them with iron.
Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc; mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi; et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez.	If it is red and the root is large, do not touch it with iron either for fear of blood loss; but let it be until it is dead, and then you will remove it, or it would break by itself; and if it is a pale color, and the root is thin, then prepare the instrument to cover it, but first look at whether the abscess is hot and calm.
Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme; et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	Then have the patient sit in the sun, and his joints be in good position, and he opens the mouth and puts his fingers between his teeth, and presses the tongue towards all of the instrument, so this is the form; and also be silver or gold as fine as our knives:
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues; et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces; et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	And you press the tongue to all this instrument, and you see the abscess, if take the scythe and put it in the ambrosia, and move it strongly at the top more than you can; and do not move anything from the threads with it, then the cap to the instrument, of which is the form, that seems a force; and nevertheless the heads are curved, and one place another, and are very useful, and is made of iron in or of anvils:
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you do not have this instrument present, if you take the cope as pliers, of which is the form:
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom; et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les II amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les II amandres igament.	And be sharpened on one side and not on the other; and when you have caped one of the ambrosias, if you cap the other according to the same manner, and after the incision gargarize the patient with hot water, and cold and easily, and let it be stayed until the blood has stopped, then gargarize the patient with wine or cooked pomegranates, or bay leaves, and similar things, until the wound is healed; then cure it as long as it is healthy; and never let others apoplexy in the throat except the two ambrosias, if they are capped like the two ambrosias.
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir I aposteme de petit sens; et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi I jor ou II.	And I medicated a woman with an abscess that was lodged in her throat, namely a small abscess; and I had it very tightly closed all the way up, so that the woman could not breathe through the passageway that was stopped up, nor could she eat or drink, and she would have died if she had delayed any longer than one day or two.
Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis II rains par les II pertuis dou neis.	And the abscess was so high up that it had been opened two times through the two openings where it was coming out.
Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un I oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe; puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue; aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc; et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens; et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros; adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge: ensi demora sens croistre; et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	So I quickly did so, and inserted an onion into one of them, then drew it out, and in drawing it out a little bit of blood came out; then I inserted the onion into the abscess again, and poured some of it out, and there was no more blood coming out; but at that moment the passageway in the woman's throat became blocked up, and she began to drink water and then wine, and did not stop cutting this abscess for a long time; and the abscess recrossed itself, and filled up the space that I had emptied, until it was very large; then I sewed it up and cauterized it inside her throat: so she stayed still without growing any worse; and I left those parts, and only God knows what happened to them afterwards.
de l’uve	of the eye
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»; et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve».	When the fever rises from the eye, and it is gone and far away, then it is called "perpendicular"; and if it is big and round, then it is called "eye".
Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes; et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe; et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li.	When it is healed as we have said in the division, and the healing does not benefit, and you see that the cheek abscess is eased and thin, then you should cut it; and if it is round and united and not far away; and it is bloody or reddish or black, then you should avoid the incision.
Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide.	For there is great danger with the disease.
Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant; puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a I des II estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des II amandres.	It is necessary, therefore, when you see it, according to the manner that I have said, of its blenchor and remoteness, that you cause the patient to sit in front of the sun, and press his tongue onto the instrument which we have mentioned above; then cut with the sharp edge at the corner of the eye, and chop it off, and cut with two instruments as I have said in the incision of the two mandibles.
Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil; car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle; et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des II amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And it is necessary that you do not cover more than the surplus that is beyond the natural term; because if you cover more, it will grieve the voice and the word; and after the incision, use what we have said in the incision of the two mandibles, and cure as long as it is healthy.
Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor.	And if the patient has fear of covering, then you should use fire to cauterize the pain.
Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague.	And the way of fire cautery is sharp water.
Et est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, et puis li presse la lengue a l’estrument que nos avons dit ou chapistre de cautere, et confis avec aigue vive chaus, si qu’elle ne soit mie trop espesse ne trop clere; et en emple le chevement de cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme:	And the patient should put his head in your lap, and then press the tongue to the instrument that we have said or fire cautery, and confound with sharp water so that it is not too thick or too clear; and by this employment of this tool, from which this form comes:
Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve; et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece; puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie; et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve; et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés IIII jors ou V Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l’essue entor l’uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine; et soit arosez d’aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu’il soit sanez.	And place a hairstyle where one puts the medicine, as with a spoon, and put the instrument that we have said or fire cautery on all the medicine on the vein; and let the patient lie on his side, so that saliva and muscle juice run from his mouth into the medicine, so that it does not go down the throat and burn him; then hold your hand over all the medicine and press it on the vein for half an hour, until you see it darken and the medicine bits be calm; and if you need to renew the fire cautery, do so, and after the cautery rinse inside with cold water, and gargle as long as it is healthy.
Ceste cure est plus save de l’incision, ne que li cautere; s’elle est curee de fumigation selonc ceste maniere, pren calament et ysope et origanum et rue et camomille et avronne et semblans herbes, et les assemble toutes ou aucunes d’eles en I pot, et i met aisil, et fai bullir; et li potz soit bien gluez de fort terre, et enmi le pot ait I estrument cheveit selonc ceste maniere:	This cure is more effective for incision than cauterization; if it is cured by fumigation according to this method, take calamus and hyssop and oregano and rue and chamomile and avronne and similar herbs, and gather them all or any of them in a pot, and pour it easily and boil it; and the pot should be very clenched with strong earth, and put the instrument that is chained according to this method:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l’uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie; aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l’avenement de l’aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent; et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d’aposteme chaut.	And it is of silver or gold, and let one of the shoulder heads be inserted into the mouth of the patient until the vapor rises to the vein through the tube until the vein is dead; then start over again, often until the vein dries up, and take care not to do this at the beginning of the arrival of the abscess, because many things have happened; and do not do it unless it is at the decline of the abscess.
Et se cist estrument n’est presens, si pren une caine et met dedens lou chief une craiffe d’uef, si que li bouche au malaide n’ait mie trop chaut; car li craiffe d’uef ne lait mie la vapor grever la bouche, et c’est bone cure ensamble salut.	And if this instrument is not present, then take a knife and put it in the patient's mouth a piece of fur, so that the mouth does not get too hot; for the piece of fur does not make the vapour of the wound go into the mouth, and this is a good treatment together with healing.
Maintes fois s’aert a la gorge os ou espinee de poisson, ou aucune chose; si covient donc que tu traies ceu que tu pues veoir, et li presse la lengue au soleil a tout l’estrument, si que tu voies mues la chose; et ceu que ne t’apert mie et est reponus en la gorge, covient que tu faices vomir le malaide ainsois que li viande soit cuite en l’estomac; par aventure si istra li chose aerse par le vomissement; ou li malaides englutisse une piece d’esponge, ou une piece de navel, ou une racine de laitue, ou I morceil de pain sec; et lie a l’esponge I fil, et puis la transglutisse; et quant elle venra au leu, si s’aerdra, et puis trairas fuer; et s’elle ne vient fuer de ceu que nos avons dit, si pren I estrument de plonc selonc ceste forme:	Many times a piece of bone or fish bone, or nothing comes out; so it is necessary that you pull out what you can see, and press the tongue to the sun with all the instrument, so that you can feel the thing; and if what does not open up for you and is put back into the throat, it is necessary that you induce vomiting in this way so that the food is cooked in the stomach; perhaps it will come out with the vomit; or the patient swallows a sponge piece, or a navel piece, or a lettuce root, or a dry bread mooceel; and you put a string on it, and then you swallow it; and when it comes to the place, if it hardens, then pull hard; and if it does not come out with what we have said, then take the instrument of plunger according to this form:
