dou retenement de l’urine	Retaining of urine
Li retenue de l’urine si est d’opilation de piere, ou de sanc congeleit, ou de bowe, ou de char nee, ou de semblans choses, que nos avons dit en la division; et se li urine n’est desliie , et tu vois estre la retenue por la piere qui est jai ou col de la vessie, si covient que li malaides soit corbés sus ses genoulz; et li soient mis li piez sor le dos, et estende son ventre de la partie desus lou dos, et restraigne li malaides s’alainne tant com il puet; et adonques est constrains li colz de la vessie a l’expression de la piere au desus, por coi li urine est desliie e; et s’elle ne vient, si com nos avons dit, et li malaides sent grant dolor, si covient que tu i aministres extraction a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «siringue», de coi ci est li forme: et soit d’argent subtilz legiere chevee, si com li penne d’un oiseil; et soit li caine d’une palme de lonc et demie, et soit subtilz au chief.	Retaining of urine is caused by a stone in the kidney, or frozen blood, or bowel obstruction, or colic, or similar things that we have mentioned in the division; and if the urine does not pass, and you see that it is retained because of a stone at the base of the spine or the neck of the bladder, then it is necessary that the patient be laid on his back; and let him place the tip on his back, and extend his abdomen from above his back, and restrain the patient so that he remains in this position as long as he can; and then force the neck of the bladder toward the extraction of the stone from above, so that the urine passes; and if it does not pass, as we have said, and the patient feels great pain, then you should use an instrument called a "syringe", which is shaped like this: and let it be made of fine silver, as light as the feathers of a swallow; and let the tube be about a palm long and half as wide, and let it be fine at the end.
Et li maniere de l’issue de l’urine si est que tu pren I fil double, et lie au chief I poc de laine ou de couton, et boute le chief dou fil dedens la siringue; et cope la superfluiteit de la lainne et le boute jusc’au chief de la siringue, puis oint la siringue d’oile ou de burre et d’aubin d’uef, et fai seoir le malaide sus I siege, et li arose la vessie et la verge d’oile moiste et d’oile d’olive et d’aigue tede; puis met legierement la siringue en la verge, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la verge, puis double la verge desus devers la boude; puis boute la siringue avant jusc’a la vessie, et la sente li malaides venir jusc’a la chose vuide, et ceu n’est mie fait selonc cest ordre fuer que por ceu que li conduis ou elle vait est tors; puis estent le fil a tout la laine poc et poc, et li urine en suit la laine, puis l’estrai fuer, et fai corre l’urine; et rencomence la siringue tant que li vessie soit vuidie, et soit aligiez li malaides.	Et the way of issuing the urine is that you take I double thread, and bind at the head I piece of wool or cotton, and bottle the head with thread inside the syringe; and wrap the surplus of the wool and the bottle up to the head of the syringe, then oil the syringe with oil or butter and auburn of egg, and make sit the patient on a seat, and raise the bladder and the penis with wet oil and olive oil and spring water; then put lightly the syringe in the penis until it comes to the root of the penis, then double the penis over towards the bouge; then bottle the syringe before jusc' to the bladder, and let the patient come jusc' to the empty thing, and this is not done according to this order but that which you lead or she went is twisted; then the thread is all bound and bound, and the urine follows the wool, then it is taken away, and the urine runs; and recommence the syringe as long as the bladder is empty and the patient is comforted.
des maladies de la vessie	of the diseases of the bladder
Quant escorcheures ou sanc vient en la vessie, ou porriture i est assemblee, et tu i vues distiller aigues et medicines, si fai a tout l’estrument qui est apellé «clepsedre», et c’est li forme:	When the blisters or the sore comes in the bladder, or it is assembled, and you see to distill water and medicine, if done to all the instrument which is called "clepsydra", and it is the form:
Elle est close, et si a III pertus: II d’une part, et I d’autre, si com tu vois; et li leus chevez par coi li medicine cort soit telz qu’il estoupe bien la verge sens adition, si c’on em puisse traire la moistor, et bouter quant mestier est; et quant tu vues giter tes medicines en la vessie, met le chief dou keusteur en la moistor, et trai au traiant qui est ens; si trairas la moistor au kesteur, et puis reboute fort le traiant ens; si entrera li moistors ens, et venra a la vessie maintenant, si que li malaides la sentira; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil dont on clisterize la vessie: si est ci:	It is closed, and if it is III holes: II from one part, and I from the other, as you see; and let the medicine-head through which the medicine drips be such that it well stops the stream without addition, if one may draw the moisture, and pour when necessary; and when you see to move your medicines in the bladder, put the head of the syringe in the moisture, and pour while stirring what is inside; if you pour the moisture into the head, and then rebounce the head with force, so it will enter the moisture and come to the bladder now, so that the patient will feel it; and this is the form of the subtle catheter with which one catheterizes the bladder: that is here:
Et est d’argent ou d’archaut, et est li chiés plus haut; et desoz a I sein ou li liiens chiet; puis pren une vessie de mouton et i met la moistor dont tu vues clisterizer la vessie, puis la lie entre les II seins forment d’un boin fil double, et chaufe I poc celle moistor sus le feu; puis boute le chief dou clistere en la verge, puis estrain ta main sus la vessie a tout la moistor avenanment, tant que li malaides sente que celle moistor est jai venue a la vessie; et se tu n’as la vessie, si pren une piece de parchemin, et en fai I cercle, et le perce rondement entor; puis boute I fil fort en ces pertus, puis assemble le cercle si com on assemble I dal, et met dedens ceu que tu vues d’oile et de moistor et d’aigue, et le lie en l’estrument; et fai si com tu as fait de la vessie, de presser a ta main tant que li moistor veigne a la vessie.	And it is of silver or brass, and this is the shoulder-blade higher up; and desos in the heart or the ligaments; then take a sheep's bladder and put the moisture that you saw to clean out the bladder, then tie between the two breasts formed of good double thread, and heat I piece of moisture over the fire; then pour the head of the cleaned bladder into the staff, and strain your hand on the bladder all the moisture coming up, so that the patient feels that the moisture has come to the bladder; and if you don't have a bladder, take a piece of parchment paper, and make it a circle, and pierce it roundly around; then bottle a strong thread in these holes, then put the circle together as you would a patch, and put what you see of oil and moisture and water inside, and tie it to the instrument; and do so as you did with the bladder, pressing your hand until the moisture comes out to the bladder.
de la piere	of stone
Nos avons jai dit en la division les manieres de piere, et l’estraction ensamble medicines; et ai dit la difference entre la piere enjanree as rains, et toz les signes, et en queil piere on doit ovrer de taille; et en la vessie, et en la verge; et je le vos dirai apertement et briément.	We have already spoken about the types of stone and their extraction in general; I said before that there is a difference between stones that come out whole and those that are broken into pieces; and about the size of stones, and about the bladder and penis; and now I will say it clearly and concisely.
Je dis que li piere qui est enjanree en la vessie si avient plus sovent as enfans, et c’est signe que li aigue saut de la vessie semblans a aigue en sa subtiliteit; et i apert harene, et graite li malaides sa verge, et li pent maintes fois, et puis enroidist; et a mout de ces saut li fondemens; et est legiere li sanation des enfans jusqu’il ont IIII ans, et est mout grief en viellars, et est as jones moiene, a ces qui sont entre jonesce et viellece; et est li cure plus legiere de ces qui ont la piere grans, que de ces qui l’ont petite.	I say that the stone which is stuck in the bladder often occurs more frequently in children, and it is a sign that the water jumps from the bladder into subtlety; and I open it, and massage the patient's penis, and rub it many times, and then smoothen it out; and its roots fall away; and the recovery is lighter for children up to four years old, and there is much grief in older people, and between middle age and old age; and the cure is lighter for those who have large stones than for those who have small ones.
Et quant nos venons a la cure, si couvient premier mundifier le malaide per clistere, por traire tout le fiens qui est as intestines.	And when we come to the treatment, if it is necessary first to purify the patient with enema, in order to remove all the matter that is in the intestines.
Car il encombre aucune fois a querir la piere.	For it does not happen often that he wants to cut into stones.
Puis prenez le malaide par les piez, et lou deboutez et movez au desoz, si que li piere dessende au parfont de la vessie, et saille aucune fois dou leu haut; puis le fai seoir entre tes mains appareilliet, et ses mains soient desoz ses cuisses, si que li vessie soit toute declinans aval; puis la quier et la touche dedens; se tu sens la piere en l’espaice, si te haste maintenant de taillier sus la piere.	Then take the patient by the legs and move them up to dislocate, so that the stone falls completely into the bladder, and does not remain in one place; then make him sit with his hands between his knees, and his legs dislocated, so that the bladder is all turned downward; then feel for it and touch it inside; if you feel the stone in space, hurry to cut it on top of the stone.
Et s’elle ne chiet au touchier dou tout, si moille ton doi indice d’oile de la main senestre, se li malaides est enfes, ou ton doi moien, se li malaides est jovencelz acomplis; et le boute en son fondement, et quier la piere, et quant tu la sens a ton doi, si l’amoine au col de la vessie; puis presse sus a ton doi, et la boute au defuer lai ou tu vues taillier.	If it does not fall when you touch it all over, then moisten your index finger with oil from your left hand, if the patient is old and complete, or cut your finger, if the patient is young and incomplete; and press it into its base, and feel for the stone, and when you feel it on your thumb, press it against the neck of the bladder; then press upwards with your thumb, and cut at the place where you feel it.
Et comande au ministre qu’il presse la vessie a sa main, et li comande qu’il estende a sa main destre les coions en haut, et a sa main senestre oste le cuir qui est desoz les coions en la partie ou on fait la taille; puis i boute le spatumile copant, de coi ce est li forme:	And command the minister to press the bladder to his hand, and he commands that he extends to his right hand the testicles up, and on his left hand he rubs the skin that is dislocated behind the testicles in the part where one makes the waist; then he pours the sputum out, so that this is the form:
Et fent entre ceu qui est entre les coions et le fondement, ne mie em mileu mais au costeit de la naige senestre; et soit drois sus la piere, et tes dois soit adés ou fondement, et soit li taille dou traver si qu’ele soit large par defuer, et dedens estroite, selonc la quantiteit de la piere, ne mie trop grans; par aventure la presse si li dois qui est ou fondement, qu’elle saut fuer sens travail; et saiches qu’il i a teil piere ou il a angles, et marges: si est griés a issir; et si a teil qui est souez, semblans a une glant, et reonde, dont li issue est legiere.	And open between what is between the testicles and the fundament, not in the middle but on the edge of the left side; and let it be right on the stone, and your two be close to the fundament, and let the cut be through the navel so that it is wide at the bottom, and narrow inside, according to the quantity of the stone, not too big; perhaps press it so that the one which is between the fundament, comes out without work; and know that there is a part of stone or angles, and edges: let it be like a piece of metal, and round, whose issue is light.
A celi donques ou il a angles et marge, fai la taille plus grant; et s’elle ne saut, si covient que tu estraignes sus as tenailles qui sont ausi com une lime au chief, por mues estraindre la piere si qu’elle n’eschaipe; ou tu boute desoz li I estrument subtil corbé au chief; et se tu ne la pues engignier ensi, si eslarge I poc lou pertus, et se li sans decort, si l’estrainche de vitriole; et s’il i a plus d’une piere, si boute premier la plus grant au col de la vessie, puis cope sus, puis le trai fuer, et les petites aprés s’il en i a plusors.	A cell where there are angles and corners, make the hole bigger; and if it does not come out, then you pull it with pliers that are like a file at the top, so that it does not escape; or you pour out the fine oil on the head; and if you cannot catch it in this way, then it is a little broken, and if it is peeled off, then you put vitriol on it; and if there is more than one stone, then first pull out the biggest one at the neck of the bladder, then cut above, then forge it hard, and the smaller ones after, if there are more.
Et s’elle est mout grans, si la covient soier, et faire plus grant plaie.	And if it is very big, then it is necessary to make a bigger wound.
Car II choses avienent au malaide: ou il muert, ou li urine vient adés par lai que li leus ne puet souder; mais toutevoie t’efforce dou traire, ou dou debrisier as tenailles, tant que tu la traies par pieces; et quant tu as acomplit ton oevre, si emple la plaie d’encens et d’aloe et de sanc de dragon, et l’estraint, et met par sus I drapeil moilliet en oile et en vin, ou en oile et en aigue rose et aigue froide, por apaisier l’aposteme chaut; puis resovine le malaide sus son col, et ne desliier lou lien jusc’au tier jor.	For two things happen to the patient: either he dies, or his urine comes out by itself because the limb cannot close; but you must keep trying to pull it out, or to cut it into pieces with pliers, until you have finished; and when you have finished your work, then apply hot balm and aloe and dragon's blood, and bind it up, and put a wet cloth covered in oil and wine, or oil and rose water and cold water, to soothe the abscess; then cut off the patient's hair from his neck, and do not untie the bandage until three days have passed.
Et quant tu le desliies, si arose mout bien lou leu d’oile et d’aigue, puis le cure d’oignement dyafinicon et d’oignement basilicon, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you remove it, so that it rises well in its place of oil and water, then cure with the ointment of garlic and the ointment of basil until it is healthy.
Et se apostemes chaus vient en la plaie et corrosions, et congelemens de sanc en la vessie, et soit par ceu retenue li urine, qui est conue en teil maniere que sans saut avec l’urine: boutes donques ton doi en la plaie, et estrai celui sanc, car s’il i remaint, si corront la vessie, et la porrit; puis leve la plaie d’aigue et d’aisil et de seil, et li aide en toutes les manieres que tu seis, tant qu’il soit sanez; et covient que toutes les oures que tu le cures, que tu li lie les II cuisses, et assemble les medicines sus le leu.	And if abscesses come to the wound and corrode, and congealed blood in the bladder, and is held back by urine, which comes out in a certain way that does not jump with the urine: then you must put a plug in the wound, and extract the blood, for if it remains, it will corrupt the bladder, and clean it; and raise the wound with water and mint and tar, and help it in all ways that you can until it is healthy; and it is good that you tie its two legs, and put the medicines on the place.
Et se li piere est petite, et ele est ou conduit de la verge, et fichie ens, et li urine ne puet issir; si le cure de ceu que je dis ainsois, que tu lou tailles maintes fois, est on escusez de la taille per ceste cure.	And if the stone is small, and it lies in the bladder, and stuck in, and the urine cannot come out; then heal it with this treatment that I have just described, and cut it many times, so that you excuse the cutting because of this cure.
Je ai ja ce proveit ensi.	I have proved this myself.
Pren I foret de fer selonc ceste forme et soit a III angles fichiees en I tison:	I will forge it according to this form, and be three-angled, riveted with an iron nail:
puis pren I fil et lou lie entor la verge desoz la piere, si qu’ele ne puist venir arrier en la vessie; puis boute le foret en la verge legierement, tant qu’il viegne a la piere; et torne le foret a ta main en la piere poc et poc, tant que tu puisses percier la piere d’autre part; si venra tantost li urine, puis presse ta main sus ceu qui est demorez de la piere qui est dedens la verge.	Then take a file and smooth the edge of the iron nail, so that it cannot move back into the stone; then tap the nail lightly into the edge of the stone, so that it does not come out again; and turn the nail to your hand little by little, until you can pierce the stone from the other side; then soon after the urine will flow, and then press your hand on what is held back in the stone, which is in the iron.
Si est tantost brisie, et saut fuer avec l’urine, et est garis li malaides; et se tu ne pues ce faire por aucune chose qui le deffent, si lie I fil desoz la piere et I autre desus, puis fent la verge endroit la piere entre les II liiens, puis l’estrai fuer, et deslie lou liien, et mundifie lou sanc congeleit qui est en la plaie; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If it is soon broken and jumps with urine and the patient gets well; and if you cannot do this for any reason that hurts it, then I will file the stone and another above it, and then pull out the iron between the two threads, and extract it strongly, and release one of the threads, and cleanse the frozen blood in the wound; and heal it until it is healed.
de la piere des femmes	of the women's stones
Poc avient que piere soit enjanree en femmes, et s’il avient aucune fois, si est li cure grief, et est deffendut por III choses: l’une est que per aventure li femme est vierge; et li seconde est c’on ne puet trover femme bien saichant qui se descuevre as mires, meismement quant elle est caste.	May it happen that a stone is passed away in women, and if it has not happened at any time, this is a painful cure, and is protected by three things: one is that per adventure the woman is a virgin; and the second is that we cannot find a woman who knows well to dislodge herself from the mirages, even though she is married.
Et li tierce maniere si est que par aventure on ne puet trover femme bien saichant en cest art de mains; et li quarte maniere si est que li piere de la femme si est plus em parfont que li piere de l’ome, por coi il i couvient faire plus parfonde taille, et grant paour i a. Et se necessitez semont a ceu, si covient que tu preignes une mieresse bien sachant, et a poines la trueve on, et se tu n’en trueves, point si quier I caste mire subtil; et li presente une baile bien saige en la vie des femmes, ou une femme qui saiche une partie de l’art, et li comande qu’ele faice ceu que tu li comandes de l’inquisicion de la piere; et regarde mout bien se li femme est vierge: adonques li covient bouter son doit ou fondement et querir la piere; et s’ele la trueve, si la constraigne desoz son doit, et li recomande qu’elle boute son doit ou con la malaide, et quiere et presse sa main senestre sus la vessie forment.	And the third way is that if per adventure we cannot find a woman who knows well in this art of hands; and the fourth way is that the stone of the woman is more perfectly formed than that of the man, so that it is necessary to make a more profound incision, and there is great fear. And if it is necessary to go to another, then you should seek a midwife who knows well, and at few, and if you do not find her, do not look for her any further; I know a woman who knows part of the art, and order her to do that which you command in the inquiry of the stone; and see very well whether she is a virgin: then it is necessary for her to put her right hand or foundation and seek the stone; and if she finds it, then she obliges her by oath to put her right hand on the fundament and wants and presses her left hand on the bladder.
S’elle la trueve, si covient qu’elle la mueve de greit en greit des l’entree de la vessie jusque desoz, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la cuisse; puis cope sus la piere en la racine de la cuisse encontre le mileu dou con, lai ou il est mues apparilliet, et sent la piere en celle partie; et ne mueve son doi desus la piere ou desoz, et soit li taille au premier petite; puis boute lou rait en la taille, se tu sens la piere si acroi la plaie tant que li piere puisse issir fuer, et saiches que maintes manieres de pieres sont: c’est a savoir, petites et grans et aspres et souez, longes et reondes, et qui ont rains.	If she pees, then it is necessary that she move from the bladder's entrance to the anus little by little until she reaches the root of the thigh; then cover on the stone in the root of the thigh against the middle where the muscle is attached, and feel the stone in that part; and do not move your two legs above the stone or below it, and cut at the first small; then blow on the wound, if you feel the stone very much in the wound as long as the stone can come out further, and know that there are many ways of stones: this is to say, small and large, sharp and rough, long and round, and which have rain.
si saiches les semblances por savoir l’issue.	If you know the signs, then know the outcome.
Et se li sans te vaint, si met au leu vitriole broiet, et li tien une houre tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer, et aies des estrumens que je t’ai dit en l’estraction de la piere as homes por toi aidier en ton oevre; et se li sans te vaint, et c’est de l’artere qui est copee, si met la poudre sus le leu et l’estrain de tentes et de bendelz, et ne rencomencier plus ceu, et laisse la piere et ne la traire mie, que par aventure morroit li malaide; puis cure la plaie.	If it doesn't go away, put the vitriolic broie on it and hold it for an hour until the sore is made worse; then return to your work, as long as the stone is gone, and have the tools that I told you about in extracting the stone from men to help you with your work; and if it doesn't go away, and it's the artery that has been cut, put the powder on the place and drain the blood and urine, and don't repeat this, and leave the stone behind, and don't extract it, lest the patient die; then heal the wound.
Et quant li chalor dou sanc est apaisie, et li leus porrist, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer.	And when the heat of the fire is gone from the wound, and the flesh begins to close, if you return to your work, let the stone be far away.
de hernie carnouse	of hernia
Ramice aquouse n’est autre chose que assemblee de moistor ou blanc syfac, qui est desoz lou keur des coions, que contient l’uef; et est apelez «syfac», et aucune fois est proprement en la toile de l’uef, si c’on cuide que ce soit I autre oef; et c’est li cuir dou coion entre lou blanc syfac que nos avons dit; et ceu n’avient se poc non.	is nothing other than a gathering of moisture or white soap that is found in the shell of the egg, which covers the testicles; and it is called "syfac," and there is none properly in the shell of the egg, if one thinks that it is another egg; and this skin of the ball between the white soap is what we have said; and such a thing does not happen.
Et li generation de cest ramice si est de foibleteit que vient as coions, et est espandue celle matiere.	And the generation of this hernia is so feeble that it comes to the testicles, and this matter is spread out.
Et aucune fois si vient de percussion sus les coions, et ceste moistor si a maintes colors: ou c’est color declinans a jaunice, ou c’est sans rouge, ou noir, ou aquous blans, et ce avient plus; et ce sont li signe de conoistre ceste assemblee, car s’elle est ou blanc syfac que nos avons dit, si est li apostemes reons, I poc lonc si com li figure d’un oef, et n’apert mie li coions, car il a moistor tout entor.	And it does not come from impact on the testicles, and this moisture has many colors: or it is color that declines to yellow, or it is without red, or black, or watery white, and such things happen more often; and these are the signs of this gathering, for if it is white soap as we have said, then the spermatic cord is stiff, a long figure like an egg, and does not close the testicles because there is moisture all around.
Et s’il a moistor en la propre toile, si est li apostemes reons avec une partie de l’uef, et por ceu pense on que c’est uns autres oef; et se li moistor est entre le cuir des coions et le blanc syfac, si le sent om bien; donques quant tu vues savoir la color de la moistor, si esprueve a tout l’intromissoire quarreit, de coi li forme est ci devant.	And if there is moisture in the proper towel, if the abscesses have pus with part of the egg, and for this reason one thinks that it is another egg; and if the moisture is between the skin of the testicles and the white fluid, then he feels bad. So when you want to know the color of the moisture, try all the inside quarter, because its form is in front.
Selonc ceu donques qui vient aprés l’intromissoire, juge de ceu qui est dedens.	According to what comes after the inside, judge what is inside.
Et quant nos la curons par fer, si covient que li malaides soit sainiez selonc som pooir et la repletion de son cors; puis le sovine sus son dos, sus une chose un poc haute, et met desoz lui mout de drapelz; puis sié sus sa senestre, et comande au ministre qu’il sié a destre, et estende la verge a l’un des II costelz dou keur des coions; puis pren le spatumile leit, et cope le cuir des coions parmi leu dou lonc jusque delez lou poignil, et soit ta fendure toute droite en devisant le cuir des coions jusc’a syfac blanc, et l’escorche subtilment selonc tom pooir; puis perce lou syfac plain d’aigue a I large pertus, et estrai toute l’aigue, et puis met tes oncines, et estent lou syfac amont; et ne touchier le keur des coions, mais que le syfac soulement; cope tout ou par pieces meismement le costeit de lui subtil, que se tu ne le copes bien saigement, si revenra li aigue; et se l’uef saut fuer a ton oevre, si le ramoinne en son leu quant tu avras acomplit l’uevre dou syfac; puis assemble les II leivres dou keur des coions a une costure, puis le cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when we treat it with fire, if it is necessary that the patient be healed according to his power and the repletion of his body; then he sits on his back, on something a little high, and covers himself with sheets; then sits on his left side, and commands the minister to sit on his right, and extends the rod to one of the two ribs from between the testicles; then take the lead spittle, and cut the skin of the testicles among them until you come to the long finger, and let it fall naturally; and be your cut all straight in cutting the skin of the testicles jusc'a white fluid, and the scalpel gently according to the power; then pierce the white fluid plain with water at a large opening, and drain out all the water, and then put your fingers, and raise the white fluid upstream; and do not touch the testicles, but only the white fluid; cut it in pieces separately the cost of him subtlety, that if you do not cut it well, the water will return; and if the egg had jumped to your work, if you take it back to its place when you have completed the work of the white fluid; then join the two testicles with a stitch, then cure it as you would other wounds, until he is healed.
Et se tu trueves l’uef corromput d’autre maladie, si covient que tu lies les vasselz que sont suspensoire, en doutant le decorrement de sanc; puis cope le coion a tout le suspensoire, et estrai l’uef, et le cure si com nos avons dit.	And if you find the egg corrupted by another disease, it is necessary that you lay the eggs that are suspended, in doubt of corruption of blood; then take the egg and extract it, and treat it as we have said.
Et se aigue est assemblee en II parties ensamble, saiches que ce sont II ramices; si cope l’autre partie si com tu as fait la premiere igalment, puis essue lou sanc, et met en la plaie lainne moillie en oile roset; et met defuer autre laine moillie en vin et en oile, et met sus les II coions, et met desus drapelz doublés, et le lie sus a tout le liien qui est selonc ceste forme:	And if the egg is assembled in two parts together, knowing that these are two branches; then take the other part as you did with the first one evenly, then rinse the blood, and put into the wound another wet one in oil rosin; and put away another wet one in wine and oil, and put on the two eggs, and put double sheets over them, and tie it up all together according to this form:
Puis pren II drapelz, et les emple de laine charpie selonc ceste semblance et soient assemblez par cousture en la gorle des braies, et li uns des chiés preigne sus le fondement jusc’au dos, et li autres a la partie dou poignil; et li autre dui chief sus les II angres, et soit toute assemblee li restreinture en la boucle dou braier; et aucune fois est medicinee ceste ramice de cautere en leu de taille de fer, et est que tu preignes I cautere cultellaire subtil, et cope le cuir des coions, et soit eschaufez si com nos avons dit, si que li syfac blanc que contient l’aigue est descovers; si pren lou cautere selonc ceste forme, et perce celui syfac as oncines, et l’escorche a cest subtil cautere chaut:	And take two sheets, and fill them with cotton wool according to this form and are assembled by sewing in the throat of the shirt, and one of the shoulders preys on the foundation up to the back, and the other to the part of the shoulder; and the other two chiefs on the two arms, and is all assembled the restraint in the loop of the shirt; and no time is medicated this ramice of cautery in the place of a iron bar, and it is that you preys the cautery cuttle-skin, and take the skin of the eggs, and be heated as we have said, so that the white syfac that contains the egg is uncovered; then take the cautery according to this form, and pierce that white syfac, and burn it with the small cautery:
Et lou cope en toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que tu esraiches tout; et garde que li feus ne touche l’uef; et saiches que ceste oevre est plus salve; et mues gardans de decorrement de sanc, et muedres que li ovraiges de taille; et se nulle chose te fait contraire, ou aposteme chaus ou decorremens de sanc ou autre chose, si cure ce qui te fait contraire, selonc ceu qui est devant dit.	And rub the wound in all ways that you can, as long as you clean it all out; and be careful that the fire does not touch the egg; and know that this work is safer; and keep your mind clear from bloodletting, and more cautious than the incision of an abscess; and if anything makes you opposite, or an abscess or a bloodletting or another thing, then cure what makes you opposite, according to what has been said before.
Et se li malaides est paourous, et ne vuet atendre cest ovraige por son horribleteit, si amenistre perforation, si com je te di, et est que quant tu es bien certains par les significations que nos avons dit que ramice aquouse est lai, si fai seoir le malaide sus I siege leveit; pues perce l’aposteme an la partie desoz a tout le spatumile large, et met la perforation dou lonc dou cors; et soit larges li pertus, si que toute li aigue corre fuer; puis met coton sus le leu, et le lie, et laisse por corre le remenant de l’aigue, puis le cure tant que li plaie soit sanee; et se li blainche toile ne laisse issir l’aigue en la bouche de la plaie, si covient que tu i boutes une penne ou l’estrument dont on trait l’aigue des ydropiques, de coi li forme est ci devant; et eslarge I poc la plaie, et saiches que li aigue revient, et est assemblee aprés VI mois ou enqui entor, et quant elle est assemblee si com devant, et ensi passera li malaides ses jors.	And if the patient is afraid and will not wait for this treatment because of its horror, then make a perforation as I said before, and it is that when you are sure with the signs that we have said that the water is there, then put the patient on one side up; because pierce the abscess in the part of the bone to all the large skull, and place the perforation long of the neck; and make the hole wide so that all the water runs out; then put cotton on the spot, and tie it, and leave it to run the remaining water, then cure it as long as the wound heals; and if the white cloth does not let the water come out into the mouth of the wound, then you must put a feather or the instrument that collects the water from the drops, so that the shape is as I have said before; and open the wound slightly, and know that the water returns, and is gathered after VI months or more, and when it is gathered as before, and so the patient will pass his days.
de l’aposteme des coions	of the testicles
Saiches que en la section de ceste ramice a paor em plusors dispositions, por coi il me semble que mues vaut c’on la laisse; et je vos dirai l’ovraige et les semblances de l’aposteme.	I understand that in this part of the text there are many interpretations, so it seems better to leave it; and I will tell you about the technique and the appearances of the testicles.
Je dis donques que maint aposteme vienent ou cors, et meismement as coions; et c’est par mout de cas.	I therefore say that many abscesses come from the scrotum, and most often from the testicles; and this is usually the case.
C’est a savoir par superfluiteit aigre et ague, qui est espandue as coions, ou de percussion; et est li color de l’aposteme selonc la color dou cors; et ne trueve point de dolor, et est aposteme grief; et par aventure est uns apostemes griés paourous et pierous, et de fuxe color, et aucune fois vient de nout d’artere, ou d’enfleure de voine.	This is to be understood: either by the excessive acidity and ague that spreads to the scrotum or by percussion; and the color of the abscess corresponds to the color of the skin; it does not cause pain and is painful; and sometimes there is a dark-colored, painful, piercing abscess, and never comes from an artery, or swelling of a vein.
Quant c’est par nout d’artere, si est conus par la disposition d’aposteme chaut, quant tu la presses a tes dois; et ne covient mie que tu i touches.	When it is from an artery, if you warm the area with hot water, when you press it with your hand; and it is better that you do not touch it.
Cil qui est fais d’enfleure de voine est conus par sa disposition a l’expression dou touchement des dois, et puet om bien faire la taille sus ceste semblance, et sus les autres chars; et est que tu cope lou keur des coions, puis estent l’uef en haut, et le trai fuer dou blanc syfac, et delivre lou suspensoire de toutes pars de l’uef.	Cil qui est fais d'enfleure de voine est conus par sa disposition à l'expression du toucher des deux, et puet on bien faire la taille sur ceste semblance, et sur les autres chars; et est que tu cope lou keur des coions, puis estent l'uef en haut, et le trai fuer du blanc syfac, et delivre lou suspensoire de toutes pars de l'uef.
Se li uef est ja sodez avec ces chars nees, si covient donques que tu traies l’uef, et lou cope; et s’il est aers au syfac, ou en ceu qui est dedens les vasselz, si covient que tu delivre toute celle tenve, et la cope reondement.	The dislocation of the shoulder is caused by moisture causing it to move out of its normal position, which results in malpositioning of the limb and severe pain and injury for the patient. To treat this, you should first reset the dislocated head of the shoulder, then carefully move it back into place while avoiding any sudden or abrupt movements. If the dislocation has caused damage to the surrounding tissues, you should gently stretch and massage these areas to release any tension and promote healing.
Et se li naissance de la char est ou leu derrier, si covient que tu la copes toute, et estrai l’uef, si com nous avons dit.	If the dislocation has caused damage to the surrounding tissues, you should gently stretch and massage these areas to release any tension and promote healing. Additionally, if the dislocated shoulder is located behind the affected area, it is important to carefully cope and extract it as we have outlined previously.
Et quant tes ovraiges est acomplis, si emple la plaie de laine moillie en oile roset et en vin, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when your wounds are healed, if you employ wool dampened with oil and wine, then the surgeon should apply other remedies until they are well.
de l’aposteme des coions	of the abscess of the testicles
Cis est uns apostemes envoloupez d’un envoloupement semblant a I borjon, avec le mollifiement des coions, et se muet li malaides griement quant il vait; et li cure de ceste maladie si est bien pres ausi paourouse com ceste ci devant, et toutevoie nos vos dirons l’ovraige de li, selonc ceu que li ancien firent.	This is one aposteme wrapped in a wrapping resembling an inchworm, with the softening of the testicles, and the patient groans much when he goes; and the surgeon of this disease should be so fearsome as this before, and we will tell you the work of it, according to what the old one did.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege aleveit, puis li boute le suspensoire des coions aval a tes dois, a tout le vasseil qui sont prochien a la verge, et les teigne li maistres, et les estende forment; puis cope au spatumile trenchant large dou traver endroit les vasselz, tant qu’il soient descovert, et puis escorche de chescune part, si com nos avons dit en l’estraction des arteres qui sont en temples; puis i fiche une aguille ou il ait I fil double, et le lie au premier leu ou li vis est venue, et le lie derechief a l’autre chief; puis les cope em mileu droitement, selonc la longesce dou cors, et en trai les moistors corrumpues; puis cure la plaie si com les autres ou on enjanre bowe, si que aucun vassel chiecent que norrissent l’un des coions; car par ceu n’i vient point de mal, et se a toz les vasselz vient vis, si covient traire les coions a tout les vasselz; si que li oes ne perde son norrissement por l’incision des vasselz, et sechent et ne se puient aidier.	It is necessary that you sit the patient on an easel, and then pour the softener of the testicles down his throat at both sides, to all the vessels which are near the penis, and wet them with the master, and spread them out flat; then cut with a sharp scythe across the vessels, as far as they are uncovered, and then peel off each part, as we have said in the extraction of the arteries that are in temples; then he sticks an awl or there is a double thread, and ties it to the first place where the vein has come, and ties it quickly to the other head; then he draws them up straight, according to the length of the body, and removes the dampness that is corrupted; then cure the wound as you do with others, so that no vessel squirts out because of the incision of the vessels, and they dry up and cannot help themselves.
de la routure dou syfac	about the surgery of the sick
Li avenemens de ceste ramice si est par la section que vient ou syfac, ou l’estension sus le ventre en la partie des angres, por coi li intestine dessendent de celle routure a l’un des coions; et ceste routure est ou dou syfac, ou de l’estension de li, et vienent ces II manieres de mout de causes: ou de percussion, ou de saut, ou de braire, ou de levement de grief faix, et par semblans choses; et li signes quant c’est de l’estension dou syfac, si est qu’il avient poc et poc, en lonc tens, et ne vient mie soudainnement; et est li apostemes igalz jusque vers le parfont, por ceu que li syfac apresse l’intestine.	Regarding the surgery of the sick, if it is due to sectioning, or extension on the belly in the part of the angles, so that the intestines descend from this section on one of the loins; and this section is either from the syphi-cut, or from the extension of it, and these two ways come about from causes: from impact, or jump, or braying, or lifting a heavy burden, and by similar things; and the signs when it is an extension of the syphic cut, are that it comes little by little, for a long time, and does not come suddenly; and the abscesses are even until near the end, so that the syphic [cut] hastens the intestine.
Et li signes est quant c’est de la section dou syfac, qu’elle fait venir a l’encomencement dolor soudaine, et est li apostemes divers apparans, desoz le cuir pres, et c’est por l’issue de l’intestine et le cors au defuer dou syfac.	And the signs are when it is a section of the syphic [cut], that it brings about sudden pain, and the abscesses are different in appearance, and it appears on the skin near by, and this is for the exit of the intestine and the body away from the syphic [cut].
Et aucune fois dessent li cirbes avec l’intestine, et est retenus enqui, et fait grant dolor soffrir au malaide, meismement quant il est pressez.	And never remove the girdle with the intestine, and is held in, and causes great pain to the patient, even when it is pressed.
Et en ces cures de fer a paor, por coi il s’en covient eschuir.	For in these cures of iron for fear, so that it must be avoided.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que tu comande ou malaide qu’il ramoine l’intestine a sa main au dedens en la plaie, s’il i puet rentreir; puis soit sovinez sus son col. entre tes mains, et lieve les cuixes; et pues muef a la main destre dedens lou keur des coions, et estent lou blanc syfac en haut a ta main senestre, et lieve l’uef a tout lou syfac devers la taille; et comande au ministre qu’il estende l’uef en haut, et deslie ceu qui est aers derrier le liement; And in these cures of iron for fear, so that it must be avoided. de hernie carnouse	of hernial hernia

de l’amollissement dou cuir des coions	of softening the leather of the shoes

Many times the leather of the shoes becomes soft in certain men, because the hairs that are inside them are softened, and it is necessary to see; and it is necessary, when you are healing it, to make a incision on his back, and take off the leather that is softened on the natural leather; then join the two lips to one seam, and cover it up, cutting off the excess of the leather that was softened in III seams or IV firmly; then cut between the seams, and heal it as you would other wounds, until it is healthy, and take off the thread.
dou chastrement	doulx chaste
Saiches que chastremens est escomeniez en nostre loi, et por ceu il me plairoit que je n’en parlasse mie en cest livre; et n’est necessaires fuer que por II manieres: dont l’une est que li mires en saiche respondre quant on li demandera, et en saiche la cure; et li autre, por ceu que nos avons sovent mestier de chastrement d’aucunes bestes por nos aidier, si com de bouc et de mouton et de chait et d’autres bestes.	For I know that chastisement is the use of a rod in our law, and because of this I would not like to speak about it in this book; and it is necessary only for two reasons: one is that the horse should answer when asked and be cured in horse language; and the other, because we have often needed to chastise certain animals for our aid, such as rams and sheep and hares and others.
Je dis donques que chastremens est fais selonc II manieres: ou par atraction, ou par fendure.	I say then that chastisement is done in two ways: either by attracting or by splitting.
En celle que nos faisons par attraction, faisons nos seoir la beste en aigue chaude, tant que li coion soient mollifiez et pendant; puis les preing a ta main, tant qu’il soient remis et que tu ne les sentes plus.	In that in which we do it by attraction, let us sit the animal in warm water until its testicles are softened and relaxed; then grab them with your hand, until they are set back and you no longer feel them.
Du chastrement de taille: covient que tu teignes la beste, et li presse le cuir des coions a ta main senestre, puis lie le suspensoire, et cope sus chescun oef a I cop, quant tu les avras bien escorchiez; et i laisse aucun poc dou syfac et lou subtil syfac qui est sor les vasselz; et ceste maniere de chastrement est muedre que cele qui est faite par attraction, por ceu que a l’atraction demoure par aventure aucune chose des coions, par coi li beste desire luxure; puis cure la plaie tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Of the chastisement of size: it is necessary that you take the animal, and press the scrotum to your left hand, then tie the suspension, and draw up each testicle as far as you can; and leave no pimple of the skin and subtle essence which is on the scrotum; and this way of chastisement is milder than that which is done by attraction, because with attraction there may be some remains of the testicles, so that the animal desires lust; then cure the wound until it is healed.
des hermofrodites	of hermaphrodites
Hermofrodie est selonc II manieres as homes: l’une si est que entre les II coions apert ausi com li figure de la nature d’une femme, ou il ait poil, et aucunes fois en cort li urine.	is according to two ways like men: one is that between the two crotches open as much as the figure of nature of a woman, or he has hair, and sometimes in wetting there is urine.

de la tentigene	of the tetanus
Tentigene est une chars ajostee sus la partie natureil, tant qu’elle est trop laide a veoir; et aucunes femmes l’ont ausi grant com une main, et c’est li cure.	is a wriggling worm on the natural part, so that it is too ugly to see; and some women also have it as much like a hand, and this is the cure.

It is fitting that you have the surfeits of the tingling in your hand or the onces, and make it light; and do not go too much into detail, lest there come blood flow, then cure with other remedies until he is well; and to another cart that comes out at the mouth of the mare, and use it, and perhaps jump outside, and is according to the appearance of a cow, and for this they called him the old "cow disease".
Si covient que tu la copes, si com nos avons dit la tentigene, et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	If it is necessary that you cope with it, as we have said in the chapter on tingling, and cure her until she is well.
de erratique	of the errant
Erratique si est quant li nature de la femme n’est mie percie, ou li pertus est petis; et est naturez par naissance, ou accidens par maladie que venue i est; ou c’est par char ajostee, ou dou syfac subtil ou espés, et est fais em parfont en la marris, ou en costez, ou desoz, ou que soit; et deffent le concevoir, et l’enfantement, et par aventure les flors a avoir; et li connoissance de ceu si est par le regart de la baile.	Erratique if it is that the nature of the woman is not yet perceptible, or the perforation is small; and is natured by birth, or happens through disease that has come about; or is by a cart being driven, or by subtle poison or spice, and is made perfect in the mare, or in the coast, or the dung, or whatever it is; and they do not conceive, and the childbirth, and perhaps the flowers to have; and the knowledge of this one is by the regard of the ball.
Se li estoupemens est prochiens apparans, si quier a tes dois ou au rait.	If the back is bent forward, it is close to appearing, whether to the left or to the right.
S’il est dou syfac subtil, et il est prochiens as II leivres, si te haste, et la ront ensi: met tes II dois indices ensamble, et li femme soit sus son dos, espandues ses jambes; puis estent les II leivres forment, tant que li subtilz syfac soit rons, et soit overs li estoupemens; puis pren laine, et la moille en oile, et la met sus le leu, et gise li femme a home chescun jor, si qu’il ne puist souder.	If it is soft and subtle, and it is close to the sides, if you hurry, and then turn over: put your two fingers together, and let the woman be on her back, spreading her legs; then make the two sides form, as long as the subtle fluid is running, and the stoop is gone; then take wool, and moil it in oil, and put it on the spot, and let the woman lie on her back every day, so that he cannot hold it together.
Et se li syfac est dur et espés, si covient que tu lou copes au spatumile semblant a foille de mirte.	And if the subtle stuff is hard and thick, you must take a loofah-like thing that looks like a leaf of sage.
Se li estoupemens est de char nee, si la sospent a l’oncine et la cope; et aies les medicines estainchans sanc, si com acaice, sanc de dragon, encens, ensamble abun d’uef; puis amenistre une caine de plonc large, si que li plaie ne puisse souder; et ensi soit longement, et li amenistre une tente de lin sec; puis soit curez d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the stoop is from a horse, if you suspend it by the neck and cover it; and bring medicines that stop the blood, as in the case of a dragon's wound, incense, all mixed together with ash; then bring a long cane so that the wound cannot heal; and let him be treated thus for a long time, and bring him linseed oil; then he is cured of other diseases until he is well.
Et quant en la marris vient char nee, si la covient coper selonc ceste maniere, se ce n’est apostemes enchancrez.	And when in the wound comes the poultice, if it is done according to this method, then there are no abscesses.
Car a l’aposteme enchancreit qui est en la marris, ne doit on touchier de feir.	For with the wound that is chapped, one must not touch fire.
des emorroides	hemorrhoids
Emorroydes sont overtures de voines dont sans cort acostumeement, et quant les emorroydes sont vielles si devienent thelul; et nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’aus, et les signes, et je dirai ci celles qui resoivent curation.	are openings of veins whose cure without a surgeon's assistance, and when the hemorrhoids are old they become thorny; and we have said in the division the appearances of wounds, and signs, and I will say here those who receive cure.
Je di que les emorroides et li thelul, quant il sont em parfont en la marris, et il n’aperent au sentir, si n’est mie li cure par fer.	I say that hemorrhoids and the thistle, when they are completely formed in the wound, and do not hurt unless one touches them, then it is cured by fire.
Cil qui sont a la bouche de la marris, c’on puet sentir, sont cil c’on puet curer.	Those who are at the mouth of the wound, can be felt, are those that can be cured.
Il covient donques que tu mettes la femme en une maison froide, puis estent l’altelul as tenailles, et le cope en ses racines, puis poudre sus medicines restraignans sanc, si com acaice et sanc de dragon et encens, et semblans choses; puis boute ses piez a la paroit une houre, puis la met en aigue froide; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, si la fai seoir en une decoction de sumac et d’escorce de pomes grenates et de gales et de semblans choses, et puis pren farine d’orge, et la confis avec miel et aisil, et en fai I emplaustre sus son dos.	Therefore you should put the woman in a cold house, then tie her with thorns, and dip it in its roots, then sprinkle on medicines that restrain blood, as well as acacia and dragon's blood and incense, and similar things; then pour her hair onto the wall for an hour, then set it in cold water; and if the pain comes back, put it in a decoction of sumac and bark of pomegranates and gall and similar things, and then take wheat flour, and confound it with honey and easily, and make a poultice with it and put it on her back.
Et se il estainche, c’est boin.	And if it stops, it's good.
Se ceu non, se li fai aerdre ventouses au dos et as mameles sens ferir; puis pren lainne, et la moille en jus de plantain ou en jus d’aglentier avec vin viel, et fai aerdre au leu.	And if it doesn't, if you make a poultice at the back and massage with oil, then take another one, and the juice of plantain or of hawthorn with old wine, and apply to the place.
Et quant li aposteme repose, si cure lou leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et celle qui est apelee «albathir» est rouge, et est semblans a I chief aspre, si le covient coper si com j’ai dit le thelul; et puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the abscess has healed, apply the poultice for as long as it remains healthy; and that which is called 'balath' is red and resembles a sharp chief, so you cover it as I have said above; and then cure it until it is healthy.
des apostemes de la marris	The abscesses of the breast
Maintes manieres d’aposteme vienent en la marris, si com chancre et aposteme pierous et herpes et estiomenes et fistules et emorroides et aposteme chaut, et plusors autres maladies que j’ai dit en la division.	come about in the breast: as cancer and painful abscess, and herpes, and festering sores, and fistulas, and hemorrhoids, and hot abscess, and many other diseases that I have mentioned in the chapter.
Il covient donques que je die en cest traitier l’aposteme chaut qui vient en la marris, qui n’est mie des apostemes que coillent bowe; et se tu vues savoir l’ovraige de fer, si regarde se li apostemes est agus en l’encomencement de sa venue, et plain de chalor et de fievre, et s’il devient rouge se tu le pues veoir.	It is therefore necessary that I die in this tract the chaut which comes to the navel, who is not an aposteme but a bowstring; and if you know how the iron works, look at how the apostemes are sharp when they begin to come out, and full of heat and fever, and if they turn red, you can see them.
Adonques ne te haster mie de percier, mais lou fais meurer tant que li dolor soit apaisie; et puis fai seoir lou malaide sus I siege, et ait II petis sieges ou il se cline, et apoie sus son dos et assemble ses piez as parties defuer la jambe; et soient ses cuixes espandues, et mette ses braz desoz ses genous, et les lie bien d’un boin liien; puis succe li baille devers lou destre costeit, et i amenistre l’estrument dont on oevre la bouche de la marris, de coi ci aprés vient li forme; et covient que quant tu i vues amenistrer cest estrument, que tu fiches le rait premier ens por savoir la parfondeté de la marris, si que ceu qui entre ens de l’estrument n’i viegne plus em parfont qu’il ne doit, et qu’il ne blece la malaide; et se li estrumens est plus grans, si covient covrir la parfondesce de la marris de drapelz, si que li estrumens ne li grieve; et covient qu’il mette le cornet de l’estrument au desus, et qu’il teigne l’estrument.	Therefore, do not hasten to pierce it, but let me die as long as the pain is relieved; and then place the sick person on II small chairs where he leans his legs, and put his feet together, and tie them well with a good knot; and then take the breath towards the right side of the navel, and introduce the instrument with which we work the mouth of the navel, from which comes the form afterwards; and it is necessary that when you introduce this instrument, you stick the pointed end first to determine the depth of the navel, so that what enters into the instrument does not come in more deeply than it should, and does not hurt the sick person; and if the instrument is larger, it is necessary to cover the depth of the navel with cloth, so that the instrument does not hurt it; and it is necessary that he put the tip of the instrument on top, and dip it.
Et quant li apostemes apert, et on lou fent a la main mol, si le covient coper au chief, au spatumile leit; et quant li bowe est vuidie, si covient que tu mettes en la plaie tentes moillies en oile roset, ou en oile vert sec; et met la tente fuer de la plaie au parfont de la marris, et met par defuer sus la marris et sus le poignil lainne nette moillie en aigue ou malves soient cuites; puis le cure aprés II jors d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois leve on la marris et la plaie par clistere d’aigue et de miel, et puis d’aigue ou racines de lis et aristologe longe soient cuites; puis reveigne a l’oignement.	Et when the abscess is opened and one puts the hand to the meat softly, if it is necessary that you cover the head with a woolen cloth; and when the bowels are empty, if it is necessary that you put moist tents in the wound with oil of roses or with dry green oil; then place the tent firmly on the wound at the base of the bone, and on the other side of the bone put dry moist tents with cooked raspberries or with carrots and long herbs; then continue to dress after two days of healing until he is healthy; and do not raise the bandage or the wound by means of a hot poultice of water and honey, and then only of water or cooked roots of lisp and aristeology. Then renew the dressing.
Et se li plaie est reponue en la marris, si covient que tu te gardes de cuire de fer, mais cure la si com nos avons dit en la division.	And if the wound is covered with skin, then you must beware of cooking with iron, but treat it as we have said in the division.
de l’enfantement	of birth
Mestier est premier a la baile qu’elle conoisse la figure de l’enfantement natureil, et li signes si est quant tu vois la femme apresser aval, et desire odorer l’ar: adonques se haste li enfes de fuer issir; adonc saiches que cil enfantemens est selonc la figure natureil, et est li issue soz son chief, et li secondine avec lui; et quant tu vois ces signes, si covient presser legierement son ventre, si que li enfes isse tost; car quant il dessent sus son chief, si ist li secondine avec lui, et est mondee li marris de ses superfluitez par bone mundification; et cist qui vient autrement ne vient mie naturelment.	The art of childbirth: She should know the natural figure of childbirth, and the signs that tell when a woman is rushing down there, and desires to smell the air: then the baby rushes out with a rush; then you will know that these childrens are according to the natural figure, and the issue comes from her head, and the second one with him; and when you see these signs, then you should lightly press her belly, so that the baby comes quickly; for when it goes up on her head, then the second one is with him, and the married man is washed away by his excesses with good purification; and what comes otherwise does not come naturally.
Car il vient aucune fois sus ses piez, et vient fuer li cors ou li chiés, et les mains, ou il vient sus son ventre, ou sovin, et est convertis par aventure sor son col, et par autres figures malvaises; si est mestier a la baile qu’elle soit saige et subtilz en ces choses, et se warse d’error et de decevement, et je vos mostrerai toutes les figures coment on li doit aidier.	For it comes not once upon its feet, but comes upon its chest or shoulder, and its hands, or sometimes upon its belly, or sometimes upon its neck, and turns upside down by accident; so it is a matter of childbirth that she be wise and subtle in these things, and guard against error and delusion, and I will show you all the figures how to help her.
Se li enfes vient sus son chief par issue natureil, et li femme enfante griement, et li vertus de li est foible, si la fai seoir sus une selle, ou les femmes la tienent; et arose sa nature d’oile ou fenugreic soit cuit, et puis boute li baile entre ses dois le petit spatumile dont ci est li forme:	If a man falls upon his head by natural cause, and the woman gives birth with great pain, and the virtue of him is weak, so that if it were put on a seat, or the women hold it; and raise its essence of oil or fenugreek cooked, and then pour the ball between his two little spatumiles whose form here is.
et fende la secondine, et cope a son ungle tant que li moistors qui est ens corre fuers; et preint lou ventre de la femme tant que li enfes dessende, et s’il ne dessent, si covient clisterizer la femme de muscillaige de fenugrec avec oile de sisament; puis la fai preindre et esternuer de condisi, et tien sa bouche et son neis une houre: si istra maintenant l’enfes.	If a second cut is made, and the nail is removed until the moisture is gone; and if the baby does not come out, then it is necessary to massage the woman with fenugreek oil mixed with sesame oil; then let her lie and strain for an hour: now the baby will come.
Et se les II mains issent fuer, si covient que tu les ramoinne legierement poc et poc; et s’elles n’i puent entrer, si met la femme sus I siege, et li lieve les piés en haut; puis deboute le siege sus terre, et teigne on la femme, qu’elle ne chiece au deboutement; et se li mains n’i puet entrer, et li enfes muert, si li cope les mains au couteil qui est ci devant mis, et estrai l’enfant, et ramoine igalment.	And if the two hands go out again, then you should repeat this lightly; and if they cannot enter, then set the woman on a chair, and have her lie down with her feet up; then take the chair off the ground, and tie her so that she does not stand up; and if the hands cannot enter, and the baby is dead, then cut the hands with the knife that has been placed here before, and pull out the child, and do it equally.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses piés	of the birth of a child on its feet
Quant li enfes vient sus ses piez, si lou covient bouter en haut; et puis le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit igalz; puis preigne I des piez et l’estende poc et poc.	When the child comes down on its feet, so it must be raised up again; and then turn it from side to side little by little until it is even; and then hold it with your hand little by little.
Cant il saut jusc’as cuixes, si la comande a preindre, et la fai esternuer de condisi; si saut fuer, se Deus vuet.	Until he jumps up to his knees, if he is instructed to squeeze and make him shake with fear; if he jumps, may God help you!
Et s’il n’ist fuer si com nos avons dit, si le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit selonc la figure natureil.	And if it does not jump as we have said, if it turns little by little, until it is according to the natural shape.
Car adonques ist il legierement.	For then he becomes light.
Et s’il ne vient fuer si com nos avons, dit si pren muscillaige de altee, et oile de sisament, et gomme fondue, et broie tout en I mortier; et met sus la nature de la femme dedens et defuer cest oignement, puis la fai seoir en aigue tede jusque desoz les costelz; et quant elle est moillifie desoz, se li fai I coliere de mirre, et li met desoz, et li laisse une houre; puis la fai seoir sus I siege, puis la fai esternuer et estraint sa bouche et son neis, et li preint le ventre legierement, car li enfes saut maintenant.	For then he becomes light. And if it does not come as we have said, if you take muscillaige of water, and oil of Sisamente, and gum melted, and grind all in a mortar; and put on the nature of the woman inside and away this glue, then let her sit in a water bed until she is soaked; then let her sit down, then make her shake and squeeze her mouth and nose, and lightly squeeze her belly, because the child now jumps.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses genous	of the child's birth between the thighs
Quant li enfes vient en ceste forme, si i mette li baile ses mains poc et poc; puis soit sovinee sus son col, et li pendent li piez aval, et soit gisans sor I lit; et plie ses mains poc et poc, et puis li preint les mains sus lou ventre, et li oste les cussins desoz, tant qu’elle soit appareillie aval; et se li enfes ne saut, si pren ses piez et li muef forment, puis li muef lou ventre amont, puis i boute tes mains; et ewe l’enfant poc et poc; et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse.	When the baby is born in this way, if it is placed on its back and then lifted by the hands; and then being hung over the bed, and lying down on the bed; and then it lifts its legs little by little, and then its navel hangs down; and then it moves its legs little by little, and then moves its navel upwards, and then it puts its legs; and thus the baby is born. And order the woman to lie down until the baby is born.
de l’issue de l’enfant qui vient dou large une main pendant	of the child who comes out with a wide hand
I covient engignier a ramener la main: s’on ne la puet ramener, si fai lever la femme, et aler; s’elle ne puet aler, si la fai gesir sus I lit, et li deboute les jambes forment; puis amenistre lou muscillaige que j’ai conteit; et s’elle n’enfante, si la fai seoir sus I siege, puis estudie au rameneir la main; et ewe l’enfant selonc la figure natureil, et la fai esternuer, et li comande qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse fuer.	to bring back the hand: if it cannot be brought back, let the woman get up and go; if she cannot go, let her lie down on the bed, and stretch out her legs in turn; then I will mention the massage that I have described; and if she does not give birth, let her sit down on a chair, and try to bring back the hand; and bring the child according to its natural shape, and make it stretch, and order her to lie down until the baby is born.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus son col, et ait espandues ses mains, et sa faice tornee devers lou dos sa mere	of the birth of the child on his neck, and had spread his hands, and his face turned toward his mother's back
I covient que li baile teigne sa main, puis le torne poc et poc, et l’ewe legierement; et quant il est igalz, si met sus la nature muscillaige de altee et oile, si com nos avons dit, puis li comande qu’elle se mueve poc et poc; et quant tu avras ce fait, si la fai seoir sus I siege, et li comande k’elle se preigne; et la fai esternuer.	I think that the bailif should grip his hand, then little by little, and lightly; and when it is even, if he sets it on the muscled part of her back and oil as we have said, then he orders her to move little by little; and when you have done this, let her sit on a chair, and he orders her to lean; and she shakes.
de ceste meisme maniere a tout la secondine	of this same manner for all the second part
Quant il vient fuer en ceste maniere a tout la secondine, si cope la secondine a ton ungle, tant que li moistors soit vuidie; et se li enfes pent sus sa faice et sus son col, si la cope des la boude, qu’elle ne soit retenue, et muere li enfes; puis boute l’enfant dedens, tant que tu l’aies mis si com il covient, et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne aucune fois: adonques si istra legierement.	When it comes to this manner for all the second part, if he puts his hand on his thumb until the moisture is gone; and if he ties himself down on his face and neck, so that he does not get caught, and the child dies; then put the child inside, as long as you have put him in the right way, and order the woman to lean back slightly: and then do it lightly.
de l’issue des gemelz	of the issue of twins
Saiches que gemeil naissent maintes fois, et aucune fois en naissent III ou IIII; et ceu n’est mie estrainge chose, et poc avient.	Saches that twins are sometimes born, and never more than three or four at a time; and this is not an unusual thing, and it does not happen often.
Dui sont estrainge chose, et ne vivent mie, se poc nom; je sai ceu, qu’il soient multipliiet, et sont desevrez par lou syfac qui les devise, qui est liiez a la boude; et aucune fois issent ausi naturelment com uns tous sous, si com nos avons dit.	Two are an unusual thing, and they do not live long, unless one is born alone; but if they are multiplied together, and brought forth by the doctor who is skilled in this matter, he is bound by the bid of the king; and they are never born naturally as all others, as we have said.
Et s’il issent griement, si la cure si com nos avons dit, et soit li baile subtilz, et faice tost et legierement ceu qu’elle fait; et faice ensi com il vaut mues a salut.	And if they are born with a twitch, as we have said before, and the doctor is skilled in this matter, and does it quickly and lightly; and he should do so as well as possible for their salvation.
de plusors enfans	of many children
Aucune fois sont formez en la marris I ou II ou III ou IIII ou V ou VI ou VII, ou plusors jusc’a XV, et sont tout formeit en forme d’enfant par le mesurement dou saige glorious, et couvient que li baile saiche tout ceu, car par aventure semblans chose li avient; si faice selonc ceu qu’il covient.	No child is ever formed with more than one or two or three or four or five or six or seven, or more than fifteen, and they are all formed in the shape of a child by the measurement of the wise king, and he knows how to do it well, because sometimes strange things happen; so do as you think best.
de l’enfant mort	of the dead child
Quant tu cures la femme de l’enfant mort ou ventre, si com j’ai dit en la division, et il ne vient fuers, et tu es constrains d’ovraige de mains; si covient que tu saiches se li femme est de saine vertut, et n’ait accident ou elle ait paor de mort; si covient que li femme soit sovinee sus son dos, et soit ses chiés enclins aval, et les jambes levees; et li ministre la teigne de II pars, ou elle soit liie au lit si qu’elle ne soit traite au dessendement de l’enfant; puis frotez la bouche de la marris d’oiles moistes avec muscillaige de altee et de fenugrec et semence de lin, puis oigne li baile ses mains de ces oiles et de ces muscillaiges; puis les boute en la marris legierement, puis quiere I leu ou elle boute les oncines que soient covenaubles a ceu, et pren warde se li enfes est apparilliez qu’il dessende sus son chief; si fiche les oncines en ses eulz ou en son col ou en sa bouche ou en som palais ou desoz la barbe ou en la forcele ou pres des costez, et se li dessendemens est sus piez, se li fiche ou poignil et as costes moienes; et covient qu’il teigne l’oncine a sa main destre, et mette la corbeure entre ses dois de la senestre main, et li boute a tout sa main legierement, et fiche l’oncine en aucun de ces leus que nos avons dit, tant qu’il viegne a la chose vuide; et c’est li forme de l’oncine:	When you treat the woman of a dead child or her womb, as I said in the division, and it does not come out, and you are forced to work by hand; if it is necessary that you know whether the woman is of sound health, and she has no accident or fear of death; if it is necessary that the woman be tied down on her back and her legs raised; and the minister drips oil on both sides where she is tied up so that she can be treated for the falling out of the child; then rub her mouth with moist oils made from althaea and fenugrec and linseed seed, then dip the doctor's hands in these oils and these muscaraigns; then pour them into the woman lightly, then wants to put him down or she pours the oil on his head where she pours the oil on his hair, then puts it on his head lightly, then wants to put the oil or pinch it and press it against her sides, and the falling out is at her feet, if he pinches it or pinches it and presses it against her cost, and the falling out is at her feet, let him dip the oil in his hand, and put the cup between his two hands on his left side, and pour the oil lightly with his right hand, and dip the oil in any of the places I have mentioned, as long as he comes to the empty thing; and this is the form of the oil:
puis fiche encontre I autre oncine, ou le tier se tu en as mestier, si que li estractions soit igalz; et puis l’estent igalment en movant d’une part et d’autre, por mues issir, et soit li oncines dentez por mues tenir, si com ci est li forme:	and then take another piece of twine, where you need it to be equal; and then make them equal by moving one side and the other, so that they come out, and let the teeth of the twines hold them in place, as is shown here:
Et s’il en demoure une partie, si oigne li baile aucuns de ses dois d’oile, et les boute en celle partie, et traie l’autre partie; et s’il en i demoure point, si met cest oncine ou plus haut leu, et fai ceu tant qu’il s’en isse tout fuers.	And if one part stops, so oil some of its two strings and squeeze it in that part, and pull the other part; and if none of it stops, so put this twine or higher up, and do this as much as it comes out completely.
Et se l’une mains vient devant l’autre, et il ne puet ramener por l’estreignement, si covient que tu envoloupes sus I drapeil, tant qu’il isse tote; puis la cope en la jointure de la plante ou au coute, et ensi covient que tu faices en l’autre main, et as II piés.	And if one hand comes before the other and cannot be brought back by the contraction, so you must wrap it in a cloth until it is all out; then tie it at the joint of the sole or the ankle, and likewise for the other hand, and at the feet.
Et se li chiés de l’enfant est gros et il est estrois en l’issue, ou il ait ou chief aigue assemblee, si covient que tu boute le spatumile espinous entre tes dois, et fent le chief et estrai l’aigue; ou tu la ront a l’estrument qui est apelez «almidach», de coi li forme vient avec les estrumens ou chapistre qui est aprés cestui; et ensi meisme faice se li enfes a grant chief naturelment; et puis traie fuer les osses as tenailles, et se li chiés saut fuer et il estraint a la forcele, si soit fendus, tant que li moistors qui est ou pis issue fuer; et s’elle ne puet issir, si le cope par pieces au mues que tu pues; et s’il est enflez au ventre ou desoz les costez, si covient que tu lou perces tant que li moistors corre.	And if the child's loins are large and he is stricken in the birth, or if there is a sharp point assembled, then it is fitting that you press the thorny spittle between your two hands, and shape the point and draw out the sharp; or you put it into the instrument which is called 'almidach', of which the form comes with the instruments or chaplet which follows this one; and so likewise do I make the child's loins naturally large; and then pull the bones with pliers, and if the loins leap, they are drawn out with force, so that they are split, until the moisture which is in the birth runs out; and if it cannot come out, then chop it into pieces by the edge of your hand; and if it swells in the belly or breaks the ribs, then it is fitting that you pierce it as long as the moisture runs.
Et se li enfes est sus ses piez, si est li attraction legiere, et li adrecemens a la bouche de la marris est legier.	And if it is stuck on its feet, then the mild pulling, and the direction is towards the mouth of the mare.
