If it is necessary that you apply the stitch in this way: take a twisted thread and put it into a needle, and then bring the thread over and pierce the needle from the other side, and tie the two ends of the thread together around the needle, and make it large; and then pull out the thread, and do the same with all the others, and leave it to drain blood; then put on the base a wet drape coated with oil or wax, and place it on the base, and command the patient to rest; and then leave him until he has coughed up, and when he has, clean him of wound infection and other cures until he is well.
dou sechement dou fiens ou fondement	to dry at the end or foundation
Maintes fois avient sechement de fiens en l’intestine, et par constrignement de nature, et quant li maladie est vielle et medicine n’i vaut.	Often there is drying out at the end of the intestine, and by necessity of nature, and when the illness is old and medicine is no longer effective.
Si covient que tu reses a la point d’un spatumile ou a ton ungle l’escorce desus, qui ne le laisse a moistir; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sodez si com il covient; et s’il ne puet soder, si rencomence la rasure plus fort que devant, tant qu’il saine mout, et soit escorchiez; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If it is necessary that you rub the scald on top of a spatula or your nail, which does not leave it moist; then treat it until it is hard as it should be; and if it cannot be hardened, start rubbing more vigorously than before, until it heals and is scorched; then treat it until it is healed.
dou fremit	What rubs
Formice est une petite apparance fautree antor le cors, et va mout em parfont; et aucune fois la trueve li frois, et le sent on ausi comme mort de fremit, et vient en tout le cors, et plus as mains que autre part.	It is a small spot that starts to itch in front of the neck, and it rubs perfectly; and there is no need for the trueve (a type of surgical blade), and one can feel it as if they were dead, and it comes all over the body, and more so on the hands than anywhere else.
Et li cure si est que tu pren une cainne d’une penne d’oie, ou une penne de vultul fort, et met celle caine sus le fremit, tant que li cercles porpreigne le fremit tot entor; puis torne ta main a tout la cainne tant que tu copes tout entor le fremit, et le met em parfont, et esraiche le fremit de ses racines.	And the cure is that you take a feather from an owl or a strong vulture, and put that feather on the itch, until it turns red all around; then turn your hand over the entire feather as much as you can; and put it in place, and scorch the itch from its roots.
Et se tu vues, si fai ceu d’une caine d’arain ou de fer selonc ceste forme, et soit subtilz desoz et traians desus:	And if you see that it is a dog of iron or of steel according to this shape, and is subtle and runs on top:
ne mie perciet, por mues tenir au doi, et mues presser Et se tu vues, si cauterize lou fremit, si com il est devant ou chapistre de cautere.	do not cut it off, lest it be two-edged, and press it together; and if you see that the fire cautery is boiling, as it was before or with cautery paste of fire.
de la forme dou clistere	of the form of the bubble
Aucune fois fait on clistere d’argent ou d’archaut, ou d’arain fondut ou mailliet; et aucune fois fait on de ces estrumens petis et grans, selonc ces a cui il sont amenistrez.	No one should make a bubble of silver or of oak wood, or of melted iron or brass; and no one should use these instruments, little or great, according to those to whom they are sent.
Cil donques c’on amenistre en la cure des enfans et qui sont foible et dolorous, sont petis.	These, therefore, that one brings as a remedy for children who are weak and suffering, these are small ones.
Li forme dou clistere petit et grant si est desus large, ou li ventres est liiez selonc ceste maniere:	The form of the bubble is small and large above it, or the belly is tied according to this manner:
et i ait une desevrance ou li ventres soit liiez, si com tu vois, et li chiez soit dedens perciez; et ait a l’un des costez II pertus, et en l’autre I; et soit li ventres ou om met les medicines d’une vessie de beste ou de parchemin, et soit perciez tout entor de menus pertus, et ait entre chescun pertus I doit d’espaice, puis boute en ces pertus I fil fort de fil crut tort en X ou enqui entor, et assemble le ventre si com est une chievre; et quant li medicine est dedens, si la lie a l’estrument devant d’un fil fort, puis clisterize; et c’est li forme dou cercle:	and I say there is a rupture where the belly is tied, as you see, and the loins are pierced from within; and one of the sides has a hole, and in the other; and let the medicine be put into a bladder of wine or parchment, and pierce all around the small holes, and place between each hole I yard, then bottle into these holes a strong thread twisted in X or string inside; and assemble the belly as if it were a sheep; and when the medicine is within, if the instrument is before a strong thread, then it should be clotted; and this is the form of the circle:
Et soit li medicine ne trop chaude ne trop froide, et oint le chief dou clistere d’oile ou d’aubun d’uef, ou de semblant chose, puis le boute ens legierement; puis l’espreigne li ministres a ses II mains ensamble, tant qu’il soit toz vuis, puis estrai lou clistere, et lieve li malaides ses jambes a la paroit, et se li medicine vuet issir, si la teigne tant com il puet; et s’il dort une nuit atot, si est plus grans aide.	and let the medicine not be too hot or too cold, and oint the head of the clister with oil or honey, or a similar thing, then bottle it lightly; then the minister takes it in both hands together until he is completely full, then removes the clister, and places the patient's legs against the wall, and lets the medicine come out as far as it can; and if he sleeps all night, so is greater help.
Et se tu le clisterizes em maladie de decorrement de ventre, et li medicine se haste d’issir, si le rencomence tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you clisterize him with the disease of corruption of the belly, and the medicine hastens to come out, then remind him until he is healthy.
Et se li emorroide sont ou fondement, ou aposteme, si soit li clistere ausi subtilz com por I enfant; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil sus coi li cuir soit estraint:	And if the hemorrhoids are at the foundation or an abscess, then let the clister be as subtle as for a child; and this is the form of the subtle clister on which the skin is stretched:
des plaies	wounds
Nos avons jai dit en la division la cure des plaies; or vos dirons les cures de mains et de medicine, selonc l’acomplissement.	We have said in the division the cure of wounds; or we will tell you the cures of hands and medication, according to completion.
Je dis que les plaies sont diverses selonc ceu qu’elles sont faites, et selonc les leus ou les plaies sont faites, et de coi elles sont faites.	I say that wounds are various according to what they are made, and according to the places where they are made, and because of this.
Les choses par coi plaies sont faites sont par gitement de piere, et taille d’espee et de couteil, ou de lance ou de fust ou de siette, ou de semblans choses; ou que sont faites selonc les leus dou cors, si com plaie que chiet sus le col, ou sus le chief, ou le peis, ou le ventre, ou le foie, et semblans membres; et je vos dirai la cure de chescune plaie, et encomencerai as plaies dou chief simples, car li remenbrance venra en son chapistre.	The things by which wounds are made are by a fall of stone, and cutting with a sword or a dagger, or a lance or a staff or a spear, or similar objects; or that are made according to the places of the body, such as a wound that strikes on the neck, or on the head, or the back, or the abdomen, or the liver, and similar limbs; and I will tell you the cure of each wound, and I will begin with the simple wounds, for the reminder will come in his chapter.
Je dis que quant simple plaie vient ou chief, et li os n’est brisiez, si pren garde se c’est de gitement de piere ou de semblans choses, et li cuir est toutevoie rompus et est li plaie grans, et tu doutes levement d’aposteme chaut: si le fai tantost sainier de la cephalique meismement s’il vient poc de sanc de la plaie, et soit li sainie au contraire de la partie navree; et eschuisse li malaides repletion de vin et de viandes grosses.	I say that when a simple wound comes about where the bone is not broken, take care if it is from a fall or from similar things, and the skin is torn everywhere, and the wound is large, and you doubt whether it is an abscess: if you do this quickly, save the patient's head in person if the wound comes from blood only out of the head, and let the patient eat no wine nor fatty meat.
Et s’il ne vuet sainier, si soit amenuisie sa viande, et ne boive point de vin, ne ne menjuce point de char; et met sor la plaie, se apostemes chaus i vient, coton moilliet en oile roset soulement, ou en vin stiptice; et s’il n’i a aposteme chaut, si met sus la plaie, s’elle est fresche a tout son sanc, et elle n’est muee par l’air, poudre, que je dirai un poc ci aprés; et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucuns oignemens, tant qu’il soit sanez.	I say that if he cannot be saved, and his flesh is weakened, and he drinks no wine, nor eats fatty meat: and place on the wound, if it is hot, a warm compress made of cotton soaked in oil and applied gently, or with wine that has astringent properties; and if there is no hot abscess, place on the wound, if it is fresh, and has not been moved by the wind, powder, which I will speak of a little later; and if he has moved it, place on some onions, until he is healed.
Et se li plaie est grans si com de tailleure d’espee et de semblans, et les levres ne se pueent assembler par tentes, si les assemble par cousture, si com je dirai as plaies dou ventre, de la costure.	And if the wound is large as from a sword's blade and of appearance, the lips cannot be put together by tenderness, but are put together by縫ing, as I will say to the wounds of the belly, from the stitching.
Se li plaie est descoverte de l’os, et pent, et ne tient mais que a un poc, si le cope; puis cure la plaie de medicine, et restoure char dure en leu de cuir, et comande au malaide a mengier grosses viandes, si com testes et froment cuit, ausi com poulz, et semblans choses.	And if the wound is exposed to the bone, and it can hold only a little bit, then cover it; afterwards, cure the wound with medicine, and restore it with hard material instead of leather, and command the patient to eat large meats, such as tested and baked wheat, and also birds, and similar things.
Et se tu trueves ou cuir porriture, et il n’aert a l’os, si cope lou porrit tot, et giete fuer, puis le cure; et se il ait artere en la plaie ou voine, dont sans cort, et il ne puet estainchier par medicines, si quier l’artere, et se tu la trueves desloie, si la lie d’un fil; et se ceu ne profite mie, si la cauterize.	And if you find leather corruption, and it has not reached the bone, then cover it all, and pour over it, then cure it; and if there is an artery in the wound or a vein, which cannot be stopped by poultice, then cut the artery, and if that does not help, then cauterize it.
Et se ces plaies sont petites et simples, si est li cure legiere: et est que tu mettes ens ceste poudre qui soude ainsois que li ars l’ait muee.	And if these wounds are small and simple, then the treatment is light: and that you put this powder into them so that fire has moved them.
Et li maniere de la poudre si est: pren encens une partie; sanc de dragon II parties; chalz vive III parties, et le poudre subtilment, et emple la plaie, et l’estraint forment, tant qu’elle s’aerse bien et se joigne a tout son sanc; et puis la lie bien, et la laisse sens desliier, s’elle n’enfle; car on n’oste la madicine tant qu’ele soit sanee.	And the way of the powder is this: take incense one part; dragon's blood two parts; live coal three parts, and mix it finely, and apply the powder to the wound, and bind it tightly, until it has completely healed and joined together; and then bind it well, and leave it undisposed, unless it swells, for we do not bandage the medicine while it is still unwell.
Et aucune fois fait on ceu de chalz soulement, quant on n’ait l’encens ne lou sanc de dragon, mais que li ars n’ait muee la plaie.	And never make any of this powder unless you have incense and dragon's blood, but let fire move the wound alone.
Et se li ars ait mueit la plaie, meismement en esteit, si n’i met om mie ceste poudre; mais met sus aucuns oignemens digestis, ou poulz de farine d’orge faites d’aigue et de miel, tant qu’ele giete bowe; puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if fire has moved the wound, at least put some of this powder on it; but put on some digestible ointments or bread made from water and honey until it heals; then treat it with other treatments until it is well.
Et se li brisure d’os vient avec la plaie, et elle est petite, si l’estrai as pinceures subtilz; et je vos dirai ci aprés les brisures dou chief.	And if the fracture of bone comes with the wound, and it is small, then extract it with small needles; and I will tell you hereafter about the fractures of the head.
de la plaie dou col	of the wound of the neck
Se plaie vient ou col et elle est simple, si n’a point de difference entre li et celi dou chief, mais se li ners dou col ou li artere est copee.	If the wound is in the throat and it is simple, then there is no difference between it and that of the head, but the throat where the artery is cut.
Se c’est li ners, si n’i a autre engien que laissier la cure, et n’i mettre nulle chose restraignant, car il nuit as ners et les fait retraire; et ne mettre sus la plaie rien froit, car li substance des ners est froide, et li continuation d’aus si est avec le cerveil, qui est li plus haus membres; mais soit li medicine souez, si com chalz lavee en aigue douce, et mellee avec oile roset, et cucie lavee ausi en aigue douce, et autres pieres de mine selonc ceste maniere, et oignemens moistes.	If it is the throat, then there is no other art than to let the cure take place, and not put anything restraining on it, because it harms the throat and makes it retract; and do not put anything on the wound, for the substance of the throat is cold, and its extension with the brain, which is the highest bone; but be the medicine soft, as warm water mixed with oil rosin, and boiled water too, and other stones of a mine according to this manner, and wet oils.
Et se li plaie est grans, si la cout et lie de bendes, puis la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the wound is large, then bind it with bandages, then treat until he is healed.
Et se les plaies sont parfondes et ele est chevee et pleinne de bowe, si la perce ou plus bas leu; et se li artere est copee, et decorremens de sanc en vient, si la desoivre, et la loie, et la cauterize se mestier est; et se li espinee de la gorge est copee, ou li keurs, et li conduiz est gardez, par coi la viande va, si cout le keur sus la cainne de la gorge, et ne touchier la gorge mais la remet selonc sa figure naturel; et puis l’estraint avenanment, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le cure d’oignemens desechans tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li plaie a fait empression en l’os, si la quier; et s’il i a pieces d’os, si les trai fuers toz se tu pues, et ces que tu ne pues avoir, si laisse tant que li plaie porrisse, et soit desevree et aligie li issue; et se li plaie est fresche, si poudre sus la poudre que j’ai dit.	And if the wounds are deep and he is thin and full of bowels, then cut into the flesh or deeper; and if an artery is cut, and bleeding comes from it, then stop it, and cauterize as needed; and if his throat is sore or swollen, then cut it away, and guard its course, so that meat goes through, if he cuts his throat on the chin of the throat, and does not touch the throat but sets it back to its natural shape; and then binds forward, and leaves for some days, then treats with ointments that are different until he is healed; and if the wound has impressed into the bone, then cut it out; and if there are pieces of bone, then throw them away all, and leave them if you cannot get them, then leave as long as the wound rots, and be sick and let the issue come out; and if the wound is fresh, then powder it with the powder that I said.
Et s’il a en la plaie os et il i a fistule, si la cure ensi com j’ai dit en son chapistre.	And if there are bones in the wound and there is a fistula, then heal it as I said in my chapter on the plague.
de la plaie de lance ou de coutel	from the lance or sword wound
Se c’est cop de lance ou de coutel, et li plaie est parfonde, si regarde se de la plaie saut ventositez cant li malaides alainne: saiches adonques que li plaie est mortelz; et s’elle n’est parfonde, et elle est fresche a tout son sanc, si n’i mettre mie a la premiere houre la poudre, ne ne la liier mie por le sanc que ne demorse em parfont, et reviegne au cuer, et ocie lou malaide; mais i met oignement atractif, et le lie II fois le jor; et se tu n’as oignement, si met en la plaie viel coton por succier fuers la moistor, et fai dormir le malaide sus la plaie III jors, ou IIII, ou plusors; si n’i venra mie spasme, ne tremor male de cuer n’estraingnemens d’alainne; et quant tu vois les bones dispositions, si saiches que li plaie est sauve.	If it is a lance or sword wound, and the wound is deep, then examine the wound to see if the patient has wind in his bowels: for then the wound is fatal; and if it is not deep, and it is fresh all throughout the body, then do not put the powder on at once, nor tie it up so that it does not move freely, and let the body rest, and ease the pain; but if you have no ointment, put raw cotton in the wound to absorb the moisture, and let the patient lie on the wound for three days, or four, or more; then will come spasm, or a bad tremor of the whole body, or strangulations; and when you see the bones moving, know that the wound is saved.
Cure la donques de tentes et d’autres cures, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’elle ne puet saner, et oevre, adés saiches que il i a fistule; si la cure si com on doit.	Cure the boils and other cures, as long as it is healthy; and if it cannot be healed, operate and then make sure there are no fistulas; thus as it should.
Et se li plaie est d’incision d’espee ou de coutel, et elle est simple, ou pis ou au dos, si la cure de ceu qui est devant; s’elle est grans, de cousture; et s’elle est petite, de poudre, et s’elle est empressee en l’os, et en a copeit pieces, si quier la plaie, et les trai fuers s’il sont desevrez; et s’il ne sont desevrez, si laisse porrir la plaie, si aligera li estractions; et des autres plaies as autres membres est li jugemens si com nos avons dit.	If the wound is from a sword or knife cut, and it is deep, or in the back, then treat with what is in front; if it is large, stitch it; and if it is small, use powder, and if it has broken into pieces, clean out the wound, and deal with any lodged objects; and if there are no lodged objects, let the wound fester, so as to facilitate extractions; and for other wounds on other members, the judgment is as we have said.
dou derrompement dou ventre	the breaking of the womb
Li derompemens dou ventre est grans et moiens et petis; de la grant plaie saut aucune fois li intestine, ou li ners des intestines, par coi li intromission d’aus; et li costure est plus malaisie, et aucune fois vaut pis li petite plaie que li grans, por ceu c’on remet plus a poinnes les intestines en, s’on ne les i remet de chaut en chaut; por ce que li intestine enflent tantost qu’il sentent le froit, si rentrent plus a poinnes, et por ceu vaut mues li moieinne plaie, por ceu c’on ramoine mues l’intestine a son leu que as autres II Et saiches que li routure dou ventre est selonc IIII manieres: les II costures communes avienent en la costure dou ventre, et li costure des autres plaies dou cors et II autres costures propres sont communes as autres plaies; et toutevoie elles sont plus propres avec la costure dou ventre, et je dirai une chescune et declairerai.	the rupture of the womb is great and small and small; therefore a large wound does not break the intestines or the nerves of the intestines, because of the intrusion of air; and the stitch is more difficult, and there is no less pain from a small wound than from a large one, so that we put the intestines back in one place after another, whether they are warm or cold; for the intestines swell sometimes until they feel cold, if we put them back in one place, and because of this they feel pain; and let us know that the rupture of the womb is according to three ways: the common stitches come into the stitch of the womb, and the stitch of the other wounds of the body and the other proper stitches are common with the other wounds; and yet they are more proper with the stich of the womb, and I will say each one separately and I will declare.
Je di que quant li plaie est petite, et aucune chose de l’intestine ist fuer, et griés chose est dou remettre, ceu est par l’une des II manieres: ou por la petitece de la plaie, si com nos avons dit, ou por ce que li intestine est enflez por le froit.	I say that when the wound is small, and nothing of the intestines is foreseen, and there is something to be done, it is by one of the two ways: or because of the smallness of the wound, as we have said; or because the intestines are swollen with cold.
Et quant il est frois, eschaufez lou en teil maniere: moillie une esponge ou I mol drapeil en aigue tede soulement, ou tu cuis en aigue squinant et cipre et spique, et arose l’intestine tant que li enfleure soit ostee; et aucune fois fait ce vins restraingnans, et est muedre que awe soule por desenfler.	And when it is cold, heat it by the third way: moisten a sponge or I mold a cloth in warm water only, or you cook it in hot water and saffron and cumin and spice, and rinse the intestines until they are swollen; and never do this with restraint, and let it rest so that it swells.
Et quant tu vois l’enfleure departir, si amoiste l’intestine d’aigue ou altee et malves soient cuites, car par ceu est aligie li entree a poc de chose; et s’il n’i puet entrer, si fent un poc la plaie a l’estrument de coi on cope les emorroydes; et li premiere cure est muedre que li taille, que nus n’i doit taillier sens grant necessiteit n’i ait; et c’est li estrumens por le fendre: si trenche dedens en la corbeure et defuer non, et vez ci la forme:	And when you see the swelling depart, if you moisten the intestines with water or cook it, for by this is the entrance to a little thing; and if it cannot enter, then make a small cut in the wound with the instrument with which we chop hemorrhoids; and the first cure is to let it rest, that we do not cut it unless there is great need; and this is the instrument to split it: if you cut it from inside out and not, and see this form:
Et quant li plaie est enlargie, et li intestine saut fuer, si le remet arer selonc la forme naturel en son leu propre, se tu en as pooir, car ce vaut mues.	And when the wound is enlarged, and the intestine comes out, if you can put it back in its natural place in its proper position, for that is necessary.
Quant li plaie est large, et elle est en la partie desoz lou ventre, si covient que tu faices gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et met ses jambes plus haut que son chief; et s’elle est en la partie desoz le ventre, si met le chief et le pis plus haut que les parties desoz, et ausi se li routure dou ventre est en l’une des II parties si met t’entente en ceu que li partie navree soit plus haute que li autre; et ensi covient amenistrer ceu que je dis en plaies grans et moienes.	And when the wound is large, and it is in the part of the loins of the belly, let the patient lie on his back, and raise his legs higher than his head; and if the wound is in the part of the loins, let the head and the chest be raised higher than the parts that are wounded, and also the tear in the belly is in one of the two parts, so you have to arrange it so that the part that is wounded more is higher than the other; and thus it is necessary to treat what I said in large wounds and small.
Es plaies petites met ceu que t’est apparilliet, puis aies entre tes mains I ministre pitous ki teigne toute la routure a sa main, et assemble les levres; et c’est la maniere commune de costures, et est que tu preignes une aguille ou plusors, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce de la plaie, puis laisse des le chief de la plaie I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une aguille ou il ait I boin fil fort; et perce les II chiés dou cuir avec les II chiés dou siphac, qui est desoz le cuir dedens, tant que tu la faices percier de celle partie, et assemble les II chief dou siphac les IIII ensamble; puis l’estrain d’un fil double entor l’aguille de II pars, puis assemble les II chiés de la plaie avenanment, et puis laisse I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une autre aguille; puis la lie dou fil si com tu as fait la premiere aguille, et ne cesser de ceu faire selonc ceu que tu as mestier des aguilles, tant que toute li plaie soit restrainte; et soient les aguilles moienes, entre subtilz et grosses, car les aguilles subtilz copent toute la char, et les trop grosses si ne pueent mie bien entrer: por ceu covient qu’elles soient moienes; et ne covient mie bouter les aguilles trop au defuer de la char et dou cuir, k’elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie devant la soudure; et puis cope les chiés des aguilles, qu’elles ne blecent lou malaide au dormir, et i met tentes ou drapelz au chiés des aguilles por mues tenir, et les laisse tant que li plaie soit soudee; et ceste maniere de costure as aguilles est plus covenauble en petites plaies, car il i soffist une aguille ou II Li seconde costure si est commune, et est que tu assemble les II chiés dou cuir et les II chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait I fort fil moien; et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz IIII ensamble, si ramoinne l’aguille a la partie ou tu as encomenciet, en la maniere c’on cout les dras; et met d’espaice entre chescune costure la grossece d’un menor doi; ceste costure sevent li home, et je cousi une plaie c’uns hons avoit ou ventre, qui estoit navrez d’un coutel, et estoit li plaie plus d’une palme de grant, et issoit des intestines bien II palmes de grant, et estoit li plaie enmi le ventre.	For small wounds, dress the patient, then take two sharp needles and thread with strong thread, according to the quantity of the width of the wound; then leave a little space from the head of the wound, and insert a needle or more, depending on the width of the wound, then leave II inches of space, and insert another needle; then draw the double thread through the needle from both sides, then assemble the two heads of the wound together, and leave II inches of space, and insert another needle; then draw the thread as you did with the first needle, and do not stop doing this with needles depending on what you need to do with the needles, until all the wound is sutured; and the needles are fine, small and large, because the fine needles go through the whole cloth, and the too large ones cannot enter well: therefore it is necessary that they are fine; and it is not good to push the needles too far from the edge of the cloth and the skin, so that they do not pierce and open the wound before the suture; then tie the heads of the needles, so that they do not hurt the patient when he sleeps, and I put blankets or drapes over the heads of the needles to keep them in place, and leave them until the wound is healed; and this method of sewing with needles is more suitable for small wounds, because the second stitch is common, and is that you assemble the two heads of the skin and the II heads of the flesh together with a needle or more, depending on what you need to do with the needles; then when you have pierced these heads all together, return the needle to the part where you began, in the way they sew clothes; and leave an inch or less between each stitch. This stitch is seven, and I sewed a wound that had once been cut with a knife, and was two palm-widths long, and there were two palms-widths of intestines, and the wound was in the belly.
Je li ramenai l’intestine puis k’il ot esteit XXIIII houres fuer, et fut li plaie soudee jusc’a XV jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.	I brought the intestine back when it had been outside for 22 hours, and the wound was sewed up until it was 15 days old, and I treated it, and it healed.
Et li mire l’avoient jugiet qu’il morroit, et ce fut miracle; et ne le curai mie d’oignement, car je estoie en I leu ou on n’en trovoit point, ne nule medicines; et metoie sens plus sus la plaie coton viel II fois le jor, et le lavoie d’aigue de miel tant qu’il fut sanez.	And the miricle was that he died, and I did not cure him with oil, because I was in a place where we could not get any, but I put cotton wool on the wound twice a day, and washed it with honey water until he was healed.
Or vos dirai les II propres manieres de cousture: pren l’aguille, et la boute des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens; quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l’aguille, et la fai percier d’autre part des la partie dedens jusc’a celi defuer; et li entendemens de ceste costure si est que tu cous ausi com li peletier font les pelz, et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d’une part, et le reprent d’autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie.	Or I will tell you the two methods of sewing: take the needle and thread it from the outside part all the way to the inside; when it has gone through the other side, take the knot of the thread and tie it tightly, so that the stitch is secure; this is how you should sew, just as the tanner does when he sews leather, and so that the stitch is complete once the skin has been joined together.
Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement, si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les II parties ensamble naturelment, et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere: fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, et fai percier celui leu soulement, et laisse les II chiés dou syfac; puis torne l’aguille, et la fai percier des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, as II chiés dou syfac; puis fai percier l’un et l’autre des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, en II autres chiés dou mirach que sont on l’autre costeit; et c’est li muedre maniere de costure et li plus commune.	The second method of sewing, which Galien describes properly, is if it were so that there is no suture, which joins the two parts together naturally, and applies one of the heads to the other head in this way: take a needle or thread near the end of the eye; pierce the skin only, leaving the two heads joined; then turn the needle, and pierce it from the outside part inside to the two heads; then pierce each of the two parts from the outside part inside to the two heads, in the two other threads that are on this or that side; and this is the method of sewing and the most common.
Galiens si dist ceste parolle, et aucun le tesmoignent, c’on doit coudre le ventre a II aguilles, ou il ait fil en chescune; et doit on bouter l’une aguille d’une part, et l’autre d’autre, en la maniere de ces qui cousent corroies; et saiches que quant li routure est enmi lou ventre, si est li cousture plus griez que des autres leus dou ventre.	Galien says this in his text, and no one disputes it, that you should sew the abdomen to two needles or threads, and you must insert one needle on one side and the other on the other, in the way of those who sew with a running stitch; and know that when the tear is in the middle of the abdomen, this type of sewing is more painful than any other type of abdominal sewing.
Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies: et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l’ait muee, si remet arer l’intestine, et lou cout; puis met sus la poudre enjanrant char, et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucun oignement que soit present, tant que li plaie bowe; et chicent li fil, et soient soudez li sifac, et li mirach; puis cure la plaie si com les autres, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu n’as medicines, si met sus, tantost qu’ele comance a giter bowe, coton viel, et le remue II fois le jor tant k’il soit sanez.	Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies: et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l'ait muee, si remet arer l'intestine, et lou cout; puis met sus la poudre enjanrant char, et se li ars l'ait muee, si met sus aucun oignement que soit present, tant que li plaie bowe; et chicent li fil, et soient soudez li sifac, et li mirach; puis cure la plaie si com les autres, tant qu'il soit sanez; et se tu n'as medicines, si met sus, tantost qu'ele comance a giter bowe, coton viel, et le remue II fois le jor tant k'il soit sanez.
Car tu n’as mestier d’autre medicine en plusors dispositions cant les plaies sont simples; et se tu doutes que li plaie ne faice communiteit as membres principelz, si covient ke tu moilles lainne legiere en oile de tempree chalor, ou en oile roset, et la met entor les angres, et desoz les asselles; et s’il sent dolor ou porriture en bouelz, et maintes fois avient, si les clisterize de vin noir tede, et meismement se li porriture vient jusc’a l’intestine; et le perce dedens, et saiches que quant c’est li gros intestines, si est plus legier a saner que li petis.	For you have no need of any other medicine in many cases when the wounds are simple; and if you doubt that the wound is communicating with the main members, then you should moisten another light one with warm oil or rose oil, and put it between the joints, and clean the swelled areas; and if it feels pain or putsrefaction in the balls, and often happens, then wash it with black wine, and more importantly, putrefaction comes from the gut; and pierce it inside, and know that when it is the large intestine, it is easier to heal than the small one.
Li intestine qui est apelez «jeun» ne puet saner quant il est navrez, et c’est por la planteit des voinnes que i sont, et por la subtiliteit de tout le cors, et l’aprochement de sa nature des ners.	The intestine that is called "jejunum" cannot be cured when it is torn, and this is because of the arrangement of veins, and the subtlety of all the body, and the proximity of its nature to children.
Et si li zirbe saut de la plaie, si le remet arrier ausi com l’intestine, tandis qu’il est fres; et s’il est vielz et devenus vers ou noir, si covient que tu lies le leu qui est noir, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, car il i a voinnes et arteres; puis cope ceu qui est entre le liien, et met les II chiés pendans des la partie desoz la plaie jusque defuer por aligier l’estraction quant li zirbes chiet, et li plaie bowe.	And if the tip of the intestine comes out of the wound, put it back behind as well as the intestine, while it is fresh; and if it is old and turned black, you must find the place that is black, since there are veins and arteries; then cut what is between the ties, and hang the two heads up from the part of the wound farther away so that the extraction comes when the tip comes out, and the wound heals.
de la routure dou boueil	of a rupture on the boil
Quant li intestine est rons, et li plaie est petite, si la puet on restorer en aucuns homes, por ceu que je vis que uns hons fut navrez ou ventre d’une lance; et estoit li plaie au destre de l’estomac, et fut envillie et devint fistule, et en issoit li egestion et li ventositez; je i mis cure selonc ceu que je poi, et ne cessai de subtilier tant qu’il fut sanez, et li leus soudez.	When the intestine is torn and the wound is small, it can sometimes be restored in some places, as I have seen that one that was torn or stabbed by a lance; and the wound was on the right side of the stomach, and it became swollen and turned into a fistula, and there was discharge and wind; so I put curative things on it as well as I could, and did not stop applying the medicine until it was healed, and the wounds closed.
Et quant je le vis souder, je doutai que li malaides n’eust mal en son ventre; et il n’i ot point de mal, mais demora en millors dispositions, et menjans et bevans; et dirent aucun experimentors que quant il a petite plaie en l’intestine, qu’il doit estre liiez en teil maniere: pren fremis a grans testes, puis assemble les levres de la plaie, et quant li fremis ait overte la bouche, si la met sus les II levres, si qu’elle estraigne sa bouche sus; et puis li cope la teste, et ce se tient si qu’il ne puet desliier, puis met I autre fremit aprés en celle maniere que devant, tant que li plaie soit toute porprise; et cout la plaie.	Et when I saw him well, I doubted that the patient would have ill in his belly; and there was no harm, but waited in better dispositions, and feasting and drinking; and no experimenter said that when he has a small wound in the intestine, it must be bound by some way: take two big teeth, then join the lips of the wound, and when the teeth have opened the mouth, put her on the two lips, so that she draws her mouth from above; and then he covers his head, and this stays like this that he cannot release it, then puts another tooth after in that way as before, until the wound is all bound; and stop the wound.
Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine, et ne vient nulle nuisance au malaide, et se puet on liier l’intestine d’un fil subtil qui est copez de l’intestine d’une beste, en teil maniere: pren le chief de cest fil d’intestine que soit mout descharnez, et puis lie au chief de cest fil I fil de lin subtil tort, puis boute le fil en l’aguille, et en cout l’intestine, et le ramoinne en la routure; et ceste maniere de costure de fremis nen est fuers que selonc la voie de fiance et d’esperance; et se li plaie est grans et large, meismement quant elle est en l’un des grailes intestines, si n’i a engien ne santeit, fuer que subtiliteit.	If the chief wound is in the intestine, and there is no harm to the patient, and the intestine can be bound by some way: take the chief of this intestine fil that is muterly cut off, and then bind to the chief of this fil one fine thread cut off from the intestine of an animal, in some way: take the chief of this thread of intestine that is muterly cut off, and then tie to the chief of this fil a fine linen thread, then bottle the thread into the needle, and when you cut the intestine, and turn it back in the tear; and this way of sewing with teeth is more strong than according to the path of engagement and hope; and if the wound is great and wide, most surely when it is in one of the small intestines, there is no medicine or cure but subtility.
de fistule ou qu’ele soit	of the fistula or that he may
Saiches que toute plaie ou aposteme, quant il enveillist, si est apelee universement «fistule», et meismement quant elle est chevee et rent bowe.	That all wounds and abscesses, when they have healed, are called "fistula" in general, and most especially when they have scarred and bent.
Et fistule est selonc la verteit nodation fautree dure et blainche, ou on ne sent dolor, et est ausi chevee com li penne d’un oiseil; et aucune fois en saut clere bowe, et autre fois espesse; aucune fois poc, et autre fois assez; et je en ai jai parleit en la division des plaies, que toute plaie que n’est sanee, et il n’i a char, ce n’est fuers que par une des VIIII causes: c’est a savoir, par la petitece dou sanc ou cors; ou por sa malice; ou por ceu qu’il i a char dure dedens, et sus les levres, que n’i laisse naistre char; ou il i a trop de bowe; ou li leus est porris, et li matiere est de male qualiteit; ou li medicine n’est mie bone en la cure; ou por ceu que li corruption est maniere de pestilence; ou por la proprieteit en la region est tardive li digestion, et tarde li santeit, et enflee par nature; ou il i a voinnes ou os: et j’ai ja mostreit toutes ces causes, et les signes, et les cures de medicines en la division.	And a fistula is according to the theoretical definition, hard and white, so that there is no pain, and it is also scarred like a bird's feather; and never clear bowels, and sometimes thick, sometimes thin, and never flat, and I have already spoken in the division of wounds about how any wound that has not healed, and does not heal, this is because of one of the VIII causes: namely, due to smallness of blood or corruption; or because it is evil in itself; or because there is something hard inside, and on the lips, which does not allow birth; or because there is too much bowels; or the place is rotten, and the substance is of bad quality; or the medicine is not good for cure; or because what corrupts is of a pestilential nature; or because digestion is late in that region and health is late to arrive, and is delayed by nature; or there are veins or bones: and I have already shown all these causes, and the signs, and the cures of medicines in the division.
Or covient que je te faice a savoir la cure de fistule qui est faite par oevre de mains.	It is necessary that I tell you the remedy for fistula, which is made by manual work.
Saiches que fistule avient en tous membres dou cors; car il i a fistules que vienent as grans voines, et as arteres, et as ners, ou au syfac, ou a l’intestine, ou a la vessie, ou a aucunes des costes, ou a l’espinee dou dos, ou a aucune jointe des mains ou des piez; et si a teil que vient a la proprieteit dou membre principeil, et as semblans leus.	Fistula can occur in all limbs of the body; for it comes from some vein, artery, nerve, or viscera, or from any of the ribs, or spine of the back, or from any joint of the hands or feet; and if so much as it comes to the principle limb, and to similar parts.
Et toutes les fistules que sont de ceste maniere sont de grief sanation, et n’i a fors que labour, et ignorance; et se il i a aucune fistule que ne veigne mie jusc’a leu que j’ai dit, et tu as fiance de la cure, et tu la vues conoistre, si pren une tente d’arain ou de fer, se li fistule est droite, si la quier; et se li fistule est torte, si la cerche d’une subtil tente de plonc, car li plons se ploie mues entor la tortuositeit; et se li fistule a mains pertus et tu ne la pues mie bien cerchier par tentes, si la clisterize par l’un des pertus, car la moistors si cort d’un pertus a autre, et la mundifie; puis la quier saigement a ton pooir, que tu conoisses s’il i a os ou nerf, et est chevee em parfont, et demande bien au malaide de la dolor qu’il sent au presser de ta main, et le leu ou il la sent; et quant tu savras vraiement le leu ou elle est, et s’elle est loing de jointure, ou de nerf, ou d’artere ou de voine, ou en aucuns des leus que je t’ai dit, si la cope selonc ceu que je t’ai dit, et oste fuer la fautreure et les chars corrumpues que sont dedens; et puis la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee, et se li fistule est bien parfonde de droit endroit, si covient que tu copes em parfont, tant com tu pues, puis i met tentes moillies en medicine ague, et les boute jusc’au chief de la fistule, tant que li medicine corrode la superfluiteit qui est demoree au fons; et puis i met oignemens enjanrans sainne char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez par ceu, si le cauterize si com nos avons dit, et se li os est corrompus de la fistule, si le cope.	And all fistulas that are of this manner are of great difficulty in the cure, and there is nothing but work and ignorance; and if there is any fistula that does not come to the principle limb, and to similar parts, I have finished telling you; and you have promised to cure it, and you have seen it clearly, take a piece of rawhide or iron, if the fistula is straight, see it with your hand; and if the fistula is twisted, see it with a thin piece of pliable rope, for the rope will bend around its curvature; and if the fistula has ruptured hands, and you cannot see it well by rope, see it with a needle, for the needle will penetrate through the thickness of the rupture, and cleanse it; then see it carefully with your power, to know whether there is bone or nerve, and it is thoroughly healed, and ask the sick person if he feels pain when you press it with your hand, and where he feels the pain; and when you have truly known the place where it is, and whether it is far from a joint, or a nerve, or an artery, or a vein, or in any of the places that I have told you, see it according to what I have said, and break up the foulness and rotten bones that are within; then cure it as long as it is healed, and if the fistula is very deep from the right place, it is necessary that you see it thoroughly, as well as you can, then put wet rawhides in medicine water, and bottle them up to the top of the fistula, so that the medicine corrode the superfluity that is reserved at the bottom; and then put ointments that spread the infection with a fresh unguent, as long as it is healed; and if it is not healed by this, see it with a cauterization as we have said, and if the bone is corrupted by the fistula, see it.
Se voinne ou ners ne te greve ou membres principelz, si com nos avons dit; et se li os est descovers, et il i a corruption et noiror, si lou reis tant que li corruption soit toute ostee, puis le cure de choses enjanrans char tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, et rent bowe si com devant, saiches que tu n’es mie alez jusc’a font: si descuevre et quier tant que tu soies au fons, et oste toute la corruption, puis restore le leu; et s’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	If in a primary member there is pain or if the bone is broken and there is corruption and blackening, the king should be treated for this as long as the corruption has not reached the entire bone, then cure it of any internal injury until he is healthy; and if he is not healed, return him to his earlier state, knowing that you have not yet finished: if you uncover and examine until you are at the bottom, then remove all the corruption, then restore the joint; and if it is thus healed, it is good.
Se ceu non, saiches que la corruption est trop en parfont, que tu n’i pues avenir; si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier a nature; et s’il i a i petit os corrumput, et tu le pues traire as tenailles, si l’estrai a I estrument covenauble a ceu, et s’il i a maint os, si les trai trestoz, ne n’en laissier nes un; et se li moistor te fait contraire, et il n’i a error ne paour, si cope et moistor et char, et delivre les os.	If not, know that the corruption is too complete so you cannot come; if there is no other problem except that it weakens by nature; and if there is one small corrupted bone, and you can pull it with pliers, if you extract it with a suitable instrument for this, and if there are many bones, then pull them all, taking care not to leave any behind; and if moisture makes it contrary, and there is no mistake or fear, chop and moistening and pulling, and deliver the bones.
Et se tu ne les pues oster a une houre, si met sus la plaie chose enjanrant porriture, et laisse tant que li leus soit porris entor les os, et adonc si avront plus legierement les os; et se c’est uns grans os, si com de jambe ou de cuisse, si reis tant soulement la corruption tant que li noiror soit toute ostee, puis restoure la plaie; et s’il en i a grant partie dou corrumput, et vient jusc’a mole de l’os; si le covient soier et coper tout jusc’a la corruption, et puis le cure tant qu’il soit soudez; et je te dirai d’une fistule qui avint I home en sa jambe, si que tu i preignes exemple et aide en ton ovraige.	And if you cannot remove them in an hour, then put on the wound something that prevents putrefaction, and let it remain until the sores are eaten away by the bones, and thereafter the bones will be looser; and if it is a large bone, such as of the leg or thigh, keep so long the putrefaction until the whole bone is black, then cover the wound; and if there is a great deal of corruption and it comes up to the root of the bone; if it is convenient, bind and cover everything up to the place of corruption, and then cure it until it is reunited; and I will tell you about a fistula which happened to a man in his leg, so that you may take example and help in your work.
Il fut I jovencelz entor XXX ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d’une cause que vint dedens le cors, tant que les matieres vinrent a la jambe, et fut enflee d’un gros aposteme, et n’ot point de cause defuer por ovrir; mais li mire par lor folie ovrerent tant sus que li apostemes ovri, et en corroient mout de matieres, et devint fistule, et i vint mout de pertus que tuit gitoient bowe et moistor dou cors; et maint mire i mirent cure entor II ans, et n’i ot nul saige en l’art de mains, tant que je i fui apelez, et vi sa jambe et les medicines dont on le curoit, et ceu que corroit par les pertus a grant cors; et devenoit rouges li cors dou jouvenceil, et avoit color citrine.	He was a young man of about thirty years who had pain in his leg from a cause that entered the body, so that the matter came to the leg, and was swollen with a great abscess, and had no apparent cause for opening it; but he looked at it because of his foolishness, and opened it so much that much matter came out, and became a fistula, and it came to such a pass that all went away from him bowing and moistening his body; and many times he was cured in two years, and there was no skill in the art of hands, until I was called, and saw his leg and the medicines with which he was cured, and what ran out through the perforations to great extent; and the color of his body became red, and his skin had a yellow hue.
Je boutai une tente en l’un de ces pertus, et puis cerchai toz les pertus, et trovai que li uns venoit encontre l’autre de toutes les parties de la jambe.	I set up a tent in one of those openings and then searched all the openings, and I found that one came against the other on all sides of the leg.
Je me hastai donques, et copai en l’un des pertus tant que je descovri une partie de l’os, et le trovai corrumput et perciet, et venoit li corruption jusc’a l’os dedens; je soiai ceu qui m’aparissoit de l’os corrumput, et cuidai qu’il n’i eust autre corruption, fuer que celi que je ostai; et comensai a restourer la plaie de medicines sodans par lonc tens, et ne pot souder; et puis rencomensai, et descovri l’os si com devant, et trovai la corruption continuee en l’os, et la soiai, et puis l’ostai, et me penai de souder le leu; mais je ne pou tant que je copai entor une palme de l’os, et le traï fuer a tout son mole, puis le restourai de medicines; et il fut sanez et soudez hastanment, et ne covint plus rencomencier l’ovraige fors por la foibleté dou malaide, qui ne pooit soffrir, et por la paour de mort que je avoie de lui.	I quickly set up a tent in one of these openings and then searched all the openings, and I found that one came against the other on all sides of the leg. I soon realized that there was a section of bone coming through one of the openings, and it was corroded and decayed, with the corrosion reaching down into the bone; I could feel the decaying part of the bone, and then I took care not to let there be any more corruption, otherwise I would have to remove it; so I started to apply medicine to the wound over a long period of time, but it wouldn't stick; and then I started again, and discovered the bone just as before, and found that the corrosion was continuing in the bone, which I felt, and then removed it, and then sutured the opening; but I couldn't hold the sutures in place because I cut into the bone by accident, and the patient couldn't tolerate it, and out of fear of death I had to perform the surgery again.
Car por l’evacuation sanglotoit sovent, mais il fut sanez entierement, et nasquit en leu de l’os une char dure, et fut de bone disposition et n’ot point de nuisement ne de contraire dou tout en tout, ne a l’aleir ne a venir.	Car por l'evacuation sanglotoit sovent, mais il fut sanez entierement, et nasquit en leu de l'os une char dure, et fut de bone disposition et n'ot point de nuisement ne de contraire dou tout en tout, ne a l'aleir ne a venir.
Et se li os est brisiez en aucun leu dou cors, si le covient soier en ceste maniere: pren I liien, et l’estrain au chief de l’os qui apert, et comande aucun k’il l’estende en haut; et met I autre lien de lainne plus gros dou premier liien, et le lie sus la char qui est desor l’os, et estent le chief, si que tu traies la char corrumpue au desoz, et descuevre la char sus le leu ou tu vues soier, que li soie ne blece la char; et met I tison ou une tauble desoz l’os por mues coper la char corrumpue; et covient tant soier com on puet veoir et sentir la corruption, et soier ancor autre fois.	Because of the bloody evacuation, he was completely healed, and in its place he born a hard bone, and was of good disposition and had no harm or opposite from anything at all, nor in his air nor in his coming. And if the bone is broken in any place of the skeleton, then it should be done like this: take a thread, and strain it to the head of the bone that has opened, and command anyone to extend it upward; and put another larger thread than the first one on top of the bone, and tie it to the char that is over the bone, and remove the head, so that you draw the broken char out of its place, and uncover the char on top of the place where you see or feel the corruption, so that the thread does not burn the char; and put a fire or a heated stone over the bone to cover the broken char; and it should be done as often as one can see and feel the corruption, and another time.
Et se li os est corrumpus, et n’apert mie, et li corruptions est en mileu ou en une partie, si descuevre la char toute; puis met I tison desoz, et puis soie des l’une partie a l’autre la corruption, et soit li soieure dou lonc de la corruption I poc, si com nos avons dit; et se li corruptions est en la jointure, si cope la jointure corrumpue, et soie l’os ou elle contient de l’autre part; et se li corruptions est en la continuation des II jointes, si n’i a autre angien que dou coper; et se li corruptions est ou poignil de la main, ou ou poignil dou piet, si est mout fort celle chose, mais toutevoie il covient que tu enquieres celle corrosion, coment elle t’apert; et la mundifie en toutes les manieres que tu pues, mais que li voine ou li nerf ne te faicent contraire; et saiches que li incisoire et les soies por coper ces os sont maintes, selonc l’assise des os et l’aparance d’ous, et lor grossece et lor subtiliteit, et lor grandor et lor petitece, et lor duresce; et por ceu covient il apareillier a chescune semblance d’ovraige son estrument; et saiches que l’uevre te moustrera l’estrument dont tu avras mestier, selonc la conissance de cest art, et le tesmoignaige des manieres des maladies; si porpense l’estrument dont tu as mestier selonc ceu qu’il le covient.	And if the jaw is corroded and does not open at all, and the corrosion is in the middle or in one part, then uncover the whole skull; then place a red-hot brand, and then sew the corruption from one part to another, and let the thread run into the length of the corruption as we have said; and if the corrosion is in the joint, then cover the corroded joint, and let it run on the bone where the other side is; and if the corrosion is in the continuation of the two joints, there is no other ache than that of covering; and if the corrosion is at the knuckle of the hand or at the knuckle of the foot, then it is very painful, but nevertheless you should inquire about the corrosion, how it opens; and clean it completely in all ways that you can, but so that the vein or nerve do not oppose you; and know that the saw and the threads for covering these bones are many, according to the size of the bones and their appearance, and their greatness and smallness, and their hardness; and for this reason it is necessary to arrange each instrument for every appearance of work; and know that the work will show you the instrument in which you will be skilled, according to the knowledge of this art, and the testimony of the ways of diseases; so think about the instrument in which you are skilled according to what is fitting.
dou feu	of fire
Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer; et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie, si covient coper celui membre jusques au leu ou li corrosion vient, si que li malaides eschaipe par ceu de la mort, ou par la malice, qui est plus grans, de la defaute dou membre; et li signes si est que li membres devient noir, si qu’il semble qu’il soit ars dou feu, et porrist aprés la noiror, pues va celle corrosions de membre em membre, et prent par tout le cors; si te haste dou coper, et se c’est par la percussion d’aucunes venimouses bestes, si com scorpion de mer et wivre et semblans, se li corrosion est au chief dou doi, si le cope, et ne li doner mie espaice de venir jusc’a la main. Et se decorremens de sanc vient quant tu oevres, si cauterize le leu hastanment, ou tu met sus aucunes poudres restraignans; puis revien a ta medicine tant qu’elle soit acomplie, puis lie le membre navreit d’un liien covenauble, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et je te conterai k’il avint a I home en som piet: il li avint une noiror qui sembloit arsure de feu, et celle corrosion vint premier en son doi dou piet, tant qu’elle porprist tout le piet; et quant li hons vit la corrosion, si se hasta de coper le piet, et fut sanez; et lonc tens aprés li revint li corrosion ou doi de la main, et il vint a moi, et je li mis sus choses repercussives aprés la mundification dou cors, et ne pot cesser li corrosions; et il vot que je li copasse la main, et je ne vou, que je avoie esperance de repercuter la matiere; et doutai ausi que se je tailloie sa main, qu’il ne morist, car li vertus de l’ome estoit foible; et il se despera toz, et revint en sa terre, et se hasta de coper sa main, et fut sanez; et je n’ai ceu conteit fuers que por ceu c’on faice autreteil, s’on en a mestier.	And if blood runs when you work, then cauterize the place very carefully, or put some powder on it that constricts it; and then go back to your medicine until it is complete, and bind the injured member with a suitable bandage, and treat it until it is healed; and I will tell you what happened to the man at home in a moment: he got a blackness which seemed like fire had burned it, and that corrosion came first from his foot down to the ground, so that it blistered all of the foot; and when the honor saw the corrosion, he covered the foot with copper, and it healed; and a long time later the corrosion returned to the palm of his hand, and came to me, and I put things that strike back after washing his flesh, and I could not stop the corrosions; and he said that he would have me cut off his hand, and I did not want to do that, because I hoped to recover the material; and I was also afraid that if I cut off his hand, he would die, for the man's virtues were weak; and he became completely despairing, and returned to his land, and covered his hand with copper, and it healed; and I only know this by hearsay, except for what others might do if they have to.
Aucune fois vient aposteme en leu charnut, et demore si longement qu’il fait grant assemblee de bowe; et puis ront et perce, et en saut li bowe, et demoure li leus vuis, ausi com uns vasselz; et li cuir qui est desus est ausi subtilz com I drapelz deliiez, et ne corront mie jusc’a l’os, ne jusc’au nerf, et telz maladie si est apelee «sain», et n’est mie apelee «fistule»; mais s’elle est si alongie qu’elle viegne jusc’a l’os em parfont, si est apelee «fistule»; et li cuire si est que tu cope celui cuir tout entor, et meismement quant il est subtilz, ausi com uns drapelz; et ne s’aert mie por sa corruption. Et se tu as fiance que li cuirs s’aerde, et li corruption n’est mie en parfont, et li cuir est espés de char, si le cure de clistere ensi: regarde se li seins est grans, et li bowe qui en ist est de puant odor, adonques le clisterize de medicine egiptiaine qui est ensi faite: prenez aisil, et oile, et litargire, igalment, et metez cuire en I vassel au feu, tant que li medicine soit rouge, et deviegne ausi espesse com miel; et puis pren de ceu selonc ta necessiteit, et le font en aigue et en miel, et en clisterize lou sein, et estraint le pertus; et laisse la medicine ens par II houres, puis l’estrai en espreignant; fai ce mout de fois, tant que li seins soit mondefiiez, et soit ostee li puor; et aucune fois est clisterizeis d’aigue de cendres, quant ceste medicine n’est presens, et est que tu preignes cendres de fust de vigne, et giete aigue desus, puis la coule, et en clisterize, tant que tu saiches que li seins est bien mondez; et se li malaides ne le puet soffrir, ne la medicine egiptiaine ne l’aigue de cendres, si le clisterize d’aigue et de miel ou il ait un poc de litargire broiet; ou tu la clistirize de miel et de vin melleit, que li mielz ait proprieteit de mundifiier et de laver, et li vins fait aerdre le sain; et quant tu as ce fait, et tu as fiance que li seins est bien mundifiiez, si le clisterize de ceu que fait naistre char en li, et est que tu preignes emplaustre diafinit, et le font avec oile roset et en vin; ou tu le clisterize d’aucunes medicines et d’oignemens, dont j’ai dit les proprietez ou traitier des oignemens; et se li pertus dou sein est petis, et li cainne dou clistere n’i puet entrer, si l’eslarge d’un fer un poc, et met ens une tente de l’oignement egiptiein, ou oignement basilicon, tant k’il soit eslargiez; et se li plaie est trop large, si la cout et i laisse tant soulement I leu ou li clistere puisse entrer, et se li pertus que giete bowe est au desus, si le cope ou plus bas leu que i est.	And if you are certain that the leather is corroding, and corruption has not yet been completed, and the leather is as thick as a char; then put this medicine made of Egyptian medicine into it: take oil and alum, and mix them evenly, and put the leather in the fire until the medicine turns red, and becomes thicker also as honey; and then take from that according to your need, and make it into water and honey, and clisterize the breast, and draw out the pus; and leave the medicine there for two hours, then remove it by squeezing; do this many times, until the breast is completely cured, and the badness of the disease is gone; and never use the medicine of water and ashes when this Egyptian medicine is not present, but you press ashes from a vine, and pour water on them, and then let it flow, and clisterize it, until you know that the breast is completely cured; and if the patient cannot tolerate the medicine, or the Egyptian medicine and water of ashes do not work for him, then make a clistere with honey and wine which has been made sweet, so that the sweetness of the honey has the property of curing and washing, and the wine makes the disease better; and when you have done this, and are certain that the breast is completely cured, then use this: press out an ointment very finely, and make it with oil of roses and wine; or clisterize it with various medicines and scents, about which I have spoken in the treatment of smells; and if the opening of the breast is small, and the catheter for the clistere cannot enter, then enlarge it a little with an iron tool, and put it in a tent made of the Egyptian scent or basilicon scent, until it has been enlarged; and if the wound is too large, then leave it to open so much that the catheter can enter, and if the opening that gueses bowe is above, then take it off or make it lower than where it is.

Car when the bowels are in perfect order, let them not be disturbed; and if you cannot cover the belly as you see fit, arrange it in such a way that the bowels run down to the lowest place that they can reach, for when the bowels are in perfect order, let them not be disturbed; and if you cannot cover the belly as you see fit, arrange it in such a way: that the bowels run lightly downward, leaving nothing of the bowels behind; and take medicines that strengthen it over the skin, and lie on a linen drape that covers all the skin; then cover with more force at the place where the belly pokes out a little wider than at the first, for ointments are applied according to the quantity of the protrusion, and put it over the belly hole to support the bowels, and do not remove the large drape until after many days once; and those who are on the belly hole often remove to remove the bowels, and know what runs from the bowels, whether it is venom or pus or enough or digested or indigestive; and take care that the patient feels pain or no, and if there is an abscess or not, and how the medicine has spread in a certain way and you see the nature that rises over the belly hole, know that the breasts are already beginning to move, and come closer to them; then remove it in the morning, or on the third day, and when you remove the wound, if you change another drape, and renew the ointment.
Et se li seins giete bowe indigeste aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie.	And if her breasts become heavy and swollen after many days, for her breasts are not yet developed.

de l’aposteme de l’ungle	from the nail bed
Panarice est un aposteme que naist desoz l’ungle dou pouchiet de la main, ou dou piet, ou par aventure naist en autres dois; et quant il est envielliez, et on n’i prent garde, si i vient I aposteme chaus, et corront et giete bowe tant qu’elle corront la racine de l’ungle, et par aventure la corront toute; et vient li corrosions jusc’a l’os, tant qu’il i vient dolor puant, et est li chiés dou doi larges, et est li color fuxe.	is a nail bed that grows out of the pouch of the hand, or foot, or perhaps grows in another two; and when it is torn, and no care is taken, so it comes The aposteme is chaus, and corront and giete bowe as long as they corront the root of the nail, and perhaps corront all; and comes li corrosions until the bone, so much that there is a painful pungent pain, and is the two chiés broad, and is the color fux.
Quant tu le cures si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu copes a i. fer toute la superfluiteit qui est demoree de l’ungle, puis cauterize la plaie aprés.	When you treat it as we have said in the division, and the treatment does not benefit, then you must cut off all the excess that is left of the nail, then cauterize the wound afterward.
Li cauteres est mout grans aide se li os est sains, et li ungle est sainne; et se li ungle apresse la char ens, et l’encomence a poindre, et la blece, si covient que tu mettes lou rait desoz l’ungle que point la char, et la boute en haut, et cope celi char subtilment et legierement, et met sus le remenant de la char medicines ardans et corrosives por oster tout; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	The cauterization is a great help if the bone is healthy and the nail is healthy; and if the nail is pressing on the flesh, and beginning to prick, and bleeding, then you must cut off the nail tip that pricks the flesh, and bottle it up, and cut off the remaining nail tip carefully and lightly, and put on the remnant of the nail burning and corrosive medicines to remove everything; then treat with ointments until it is healthy.
Et se li corrosion est en l’os, si le cope, et trai fuer, car tant com li os corrumpus i est, si ne puet saner; et se tu vois le doi corrumpre, si le cope en I des nous si com il est devant dit, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il est ferus, et boutez, et il sent grant dolor, si covient que tu le sainnes premier; puis cope l’ungle dou spatumile agut en taillant de travers desus, et warde que li taille ne viegne jusc’a la char qui est desoz l’ungle, car li malaides sentiroit trop grant dolor; et s’il avient, si met chose sus qui apaise.	Et si la corrosion est dans l'os, alors le cope et le traire fort, car tant que l'os est corrompu, il ne peut guérir ; et si tu vois le douaire corrompre, alors le cope comme il a été dit avant, ensuite guérir jusqu'à ce qu'il soit guéri ; et s'il est blessé et gonflé, et sent une grande douleur, alors il convient que tu le guérisses d'abord ; puis cope l'ongle avec du spatule obtenu en coupant travers de dessus, et garde que la coupe ne vienne pas à la tête qui est sous l'ongle, car le patient sentirait trop de douleur ; et s'il arrivait, alors mettre quelque chose pour apaiser.
la dolor dou sourdoit de la main	La douleur du sourdoit de la main
Li dois ajostez qui naist en mains d’aucuns homes par aventure est toz charnus, et par aventure i a teil ou il a osses, et aucune fois i a ungle, et aucun d’aus naissent en la racine de la jointure, ou li naissance est en aucuns nous des dois.	The two hands of some men are entirely flesh, and in others there is bone, and in neither has an nail, and the birth in either is at the root of the joint, or the birth is in some of us.
Cil qui naist en aucune nout dou doi ne se muet, et cil qui naist a la jointure dou doi, par aventure se muet; la taille de celui qui est charnus si est legiere, en teil maniere: taille le en sa racine d’un large spatumile.	Those who are born with two legs do not move, and those who are born with a joint between the two, may yet move; the size of that which is charnous is light, in this way: cut it at its root with a broad chisel.
Cil qui naist en la racine de la jointure si est grief a curer: si te tien dou coper.	Those who are born at the root of the joint must be carefully treated; if you hold them tight.
En celui qui naist ou doit au derrien nout, si covient que tu copes premier la char reondement jusc’a l’os, puis cope l’os a une soie convenable a ceu, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	In the one who is born or should be at the derrien nout, it is necessary that you first cut off the flesh in roundness up to the bone, then cut the bone with a suitable thread, and then treat it until it is healthy.
Li soudemens que vient as dois ensamble vient par naissance, ou par soudement de plaie, ou par arsure de feu, ou par semblans choses.	The joints that come together by nature, or by the joining of a wound, or by fire burning, or by similar things.
Si couvient que tu copes celle soudeure, si que li doit repairent selonc lor formes naturelz; puis met entre dous tentes ou drapelz moilliez en oile roset, qu’il ne se soudent; ou tu met entre dous pieces de plonc subtilz, tant que li leus soit soudez, si com il covient.	If you think that you can cut off the joint, so that it returns to its natural form; then place between two fabric pieces or drape-like materials wet with rosin, so that it does not soud; or place between two thin pieces of cloth, until the legs are souded together, as is necessary.
Se soudemens vient a aucun de ses dois avec la paume, si cope celle sodure si com il covient.	Se soudemens vient a aucun de ses deux avec la paume, s'il còpe celle soudure si com il convient.
des vils	The dislocated shoulder is moved back into place, and if it does not move easily, it must be forced back into position with care.
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors; et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.	And there are many evil wrapped up viscera full of excess melancoliousness that come from the members of the body; and more is seen in the legs of those who go on foot and work and carry, than in others.
Il covient donques que tu li aministres aucune fois espurgement de cole, et puis le saine de la basilique.	Therefore, you should not give him any more purging medicines, and then heal the foundation of the temple.
Li cure de fer si est selonc II manieres: l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir; et li autre maniere si est que tu lieves la voinne, et la trai toute fuer.	The treatment for iron is according to two methods: one is that you kop them, and then draw out the black blood; and the other method is that you hold the vein, and then draw it all out.
Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere: arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez, puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil; puis cope la voinne en I leu, ou en II ou en III, d’une taille large, puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l’un chief jusc’a l’autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir; et puis la lie, et li comande qu’il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire; et recomence l’evacuation et la sainie quant les voinnes sont plainnes, et nuist au malaide.	The following are the methods for treating iron: First, raise the leg of the healthy person very strongly with hot water until the large blood is thinned out, then draw out the leg of the sick person from above the hip all the way to the knee; then kop the vein either in one place, or in two, or in three, widely open, then drain and draw out the black blood by your hand, from one end to the other, as much as the virtue of the sick person can bear; then bind it, and command that he bathe his meat with black blood; and then restart the evacuation and dressing when the veins are clean, and keep doing so until the patient is better.
Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere: reis la jambe dou malaide, s’il i a mout de poil, puis le met ou bain, et li arose la jambe d’aigue chaude tant qu’elle deviegne rouge, et enflent les voinnes; et se tu n’as point de baing, si le chaufe au feu, et puis le cope endroit la voinne dou lonc au chief dou genoil, ou en la partie desoz a la cheville; puis aoevre le cuir a l’oncine, et escorche la voinne de chescune part, tant qu’ele apere quant on la sent; et on la voit rouge et noire, et quant elle entre ou cuir si semble ausi com une corde blainche; puis boute le rait desoz, tant qu’ele soit alevee dou cuir, et puis la pent a l’oncine legier, puis le cope en I autre leu ensus III dois; puis escorche le cuir sus la voinne tant qu’ele apere, puis la lieve au rais, si com tu as fait, et la pent a un autre uncine, si com tu as fait premiers; puis cope une autre taille, ou plusors se tu en as mestier, puis la lieve, et la cope au doi dou piet, puis la trai et lieve jusc’a la seconde taille; puis l’estrai de taille en taille, tant qu’elle isse toute fuer, puis la cope; et se tu ne la pues traire et lever, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil fort double, et la lie et la trai, et i boute desoz I rait, et torne ta main d’une part et d’autre, tant qu’il en isse; et garde qu’elle ne cope, car s’elle cope, si ne la puet on traire ne lever, et en vient nuisement au malaide; et quant tu l’as toute traite, si met sor le leu de la plaie laine moillie en vin et en oile roset; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez. de la voinne civile	of the civil vein
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor; et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir, si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	This vein is found in the legs, in hot parts where there are no herbs or trees, and in the earth where there is no moisture; and perhaps it grows elsewhere than in the legs, and this causes the decay of the skin that comes from within the body, like a snake creeping and curling up, destroying between skin and meat.
Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation, puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante. des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	vers which are born between leather and cart
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués, et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant, et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer; et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre; et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil, par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil; et ceu avient maintes fois.	This disease is called in our land "buff disease," for it often attacks buffaloes, and it is a small worm that borns between leather and cart, and goes everywhere ascending and descending, and feels well from one member to another, until it destroys the skin where it goes, and sometimes enters, and destroys the oil; and this happens often.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait: si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement, puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves, si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire; et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit; et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer; et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries, et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	When you treat and draw it out, do not be able to force it but when it goes: then, indeed, should you pull the joint well up and tightly with a strong rope, then cut it off and draw it out, and let it fall completely into the cart, and if you don't find it, cauterize it with fire from above so that it dies; and the greatest damage it does is when it corromps the oil, as we have said. And if you see it coming near the oil at the head, then strain it off well, then cut it off and draw it out. And it is necessary to use medicine that dissolves the bad humors from the skin, and to wash with meat that is corrupted by putrefaction.
de la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	of pain which comes from wind
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres, et pues se mue de membre en membre; et je vis ceu que je vos di.	This disease is called "vakirir" in our land, and it is a pain that comes to some limbs, and moves from limb to limb; and I have seen this one that I tell you about.
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais; et I poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule, plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre; li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule, et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais; puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	I was called to a sick woman, and I discovered some of her arms, and saw a small swelling in the vein of the arm; and I felt it afterwards, it rose as high as a worm does on its own, and went up as quick as if it were silver, when it comes from one place to another; the pain departed from that place, and stuck in her shoulder, and then a little later corrupted all over her body, until it came to the other arm; then she told me that she twisted herself again around her body, just as I saw.
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I marveled much at how she moved from limb to limb in this way, for I have never heard of such a disease in such a way.
