And if the wound is exposed, then you should bring forth a linen cloth, according to the quantity of the wound, and soak it in oil, and place it on the wound; then take another cloth, double, double, or triple, and soak it in wine and oil, and place it on the first cloth; and do so more lightly than you can, so that you do not aggravate the wound, then tie it up again, and do not remove it until the abscesses have calmed down a little; and then take off, and apply medicines as roots of plants, flour of dates, incense powder, and similar things; and of these things make a powder, and place it on the wound, and administer it with medicines that cannot be tasted; and guard against the wound being dirty, so you do not leave it oozing, or let it gather dirt, because when bowels gather on the cloth under the skull, if they corrode and stick to them, they bring great harm upon the sick person; for when something is applied to the wound that stings, if it is taken away quickly.
Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.	Prend garde donc, que nul mauvais accident arrive au malade, si comme nous avons dit, s'il est douteux sans doute.
Et se noiror n’i vient fuers que por la medicine c’on a mise sus, que teil vertu ait, si covient que tu preignes une partie de miel, et III parties d’oile roset et en glue I drapel, et lou met sus lou syfac; puis lou cure de manieres de cures qu’il couvient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Take heed then, that no bad accident comes to the patient, if as we have said, it is doubtful without doubt. And if black bile comes only because of the medicine put there, which has its virtue, then you should squeeze a part of honey and three parts of rosewater and mix one drapelet with it, and apply it to the sick one; then cure in the ways that seem good to you until he is well.
Saiches que aucune fois sont brisies les II parties dou neis desus, ou li une par li soulement, car ce sont II os; et cil desoz est cartillaginous, et ne brise mie, si ne fait fuer k’enbower ou tordre, et puis saine.	Know that the two bones above are never broken if one falls on them by accident, for they are like bone; and this bone does not break unless it is bent or twisted, and then it heals.
Et se l’une des II parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil; et fai ce legierement, et warde que li malaides ne sente dolor par ton ovraige.	And if one of the two bones is broken, then you should drive your little finger or pertus of the neck into it, and make it even inside the index finger and at the heel by turning, until the neck regains its natural form; and do this lightly, and take care that the patient does not feel pain from your work.
Et se li brisure est en la partie desus lou neis, et ne puet venir li dois au leu, si couvient que tu lou mettes igal au chief d’un rait un poc gros.	And if his break is in the upper part of the neck, and he cannot come to his place, then you should put it equal to the head of a small ray.
Et se li brisure est de II pars, si refai autretel, et te haste de restorer lou premier jor, se tu pues; se ce non, aprés lou septime ou le disime, quant li apostemes chaus est apaisiez, puis bouthe au chief dou neis tentes de drapelz de lin, se li brisure est en une partie.	And if his break is in two parts, then do otherwise, and hurry to restore the first day if you can; if not, after the seventh or ninth, when the abscess is calm, then bind at the neck with strips of linen cloth if his break is in one part.
Ou tu boutes I autre d’autre part, se li brisure i est; et soient les tentes si grosses qu’eles emplissent les pertus dou neis.	Or you bind another from the other side, if his break is; and let the strips be so thick that they fill the apertures of the neck.
Et dirent aucun restorour c’on doit moillier les tentes em burre, et muer chescun jor.	And say that one should moisten the strips daily.
Il ne me semble mie que ce soit bien, mais covient qu’elles soient moillies en confection d’aubun d’uef, et de poudre de molin; puis laisse la tente, tant que li os soit fers, et li cartilaiges endurcis.	It seems to me that it is not good, but it is necessary that the strips be moistened in sheep's fat and powder of millet; then leave the bandage, until the bone is hard and the joints dury.
Et aucune fois boute on ou neis pennes d’oie en leu de tentes, et si a I souef drapeil entor, et se tient la briseure, et soffle li malaides parmi; or fai lou kel ke tu vues.	And never stuff feathers in tents, and if it is not well covered, the wind blows through it and hurts the patient, or do as you see fit.
Et se apostemes chaus vient au neis tandis com tu i oevres, si i met cerote ou coton moilliet en oile roset, ou en I poc de dyaquilon.	And if the abscess breaks while you are operating, put cotton wadding soaked in oil or a little piece of gauze.
Et se apostemes chaus n’i vient, si met emplastre par defuer, de farine de sisament, et de poudre d’encens, confites avec aubun d’uef, puis met sus estoupes legieres, et ne liier mie lou neis; et se li brisure dou neis est petite, et il est brisiés em menues pieces, si l’estrai as estrumens covenables a ceu, puis cout la fendure, et la cure de choses enjanrans char, et soudant, si com emplastres et oignemens covenables a ceu; et s’il n’a dedens lou neis nule plaie, si lou cure de tentes, et i met cainnes de plonc, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the abscess does not burst while you are operating, apply paste to the outside, made from flour and powder of salsify, mixed with honey and oil, then put a light bandage on it, and do not tie it tight; and if the rupture of the abscess is small, and it breaks into little pieces, extract them with suitable instruments, then cut off the break, and cure the injuries that come with it, and apply pastes and oils appropriate to it; and if there is no injury inside the abscess, cure the tent and put wadding made from cotton in oil.
de la routure de la mandibule	Of the rupture of the jaw
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n’i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n’est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement.	When the jaw is broken and there is no wound, and the break is not very great, and it is not broken in two, but only cracked a little within, then let it be known slightly.
Il covient, se li brisure est en la destre partie, que tu boutes ton doi indice en la bouche dou malaide; et se li brisure est en la mandibule senestre, si boute ton doi indice de la main destre, et boute la brisure dedens legierement, et l’afaite a l’autre main par defuer, et met igal.	If the break is on the right side of the jaw, then insert your index finger into the mouth of the patient; and if the break is on the left side of the jaw, then insert your index finger of the left hand into it, and push the break in slightly, and fix it with the other hand to one side, and make it even.
Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en II, si covient que tu aministres extension de II pars, tant qu’il soit igalz.	And if the break of the jaw is in two places, then it is necessary that you make an extension of the two parts, until they are even.
Et se commovemens des dens avient, ou routure, si les estrain d’un fil d’or ou d’argent ou de soie, puis met sus la mandibule brisie cerote, et met sus I drapel double; et met sus lou drapel une grant estele bien faite, ou une piece de cuir igal, longe et large selonc la mandibule, et la lie sus au mues que tu pues, et comande a malaide qu’il se repose, et menjuce viandes legieres.	And if the movement of the teeth has occurred or the break, then take out a string of gold, silver, or silk, and place it on top of the broken jaw, and place over it a double cloth; and place over the cloth a long and wide piece of leather made even according to the shape of the jaw, and fasten it with nails that you can use, and command the patient to rest, and eat light food.
Et se tu vois que li figure se chainge, si le deslie au tier jor, et puis remet a point ceu que c’est chaingiet; et met emplaustre sus, de la poudre dou moulin avec abun d’uef ou farine de sisament, aprés ceu que tu as osteit lou cerote; et met sus l’emplaustre lainne legiere, et se li emplaustres s’aert, et li disposition dou malaide ne se chainge, laisse le tant k’il soit sanez; maintes fois est sanez en III semainnes.	And if you see that the figure has changed, if you let it rest on the third day, and then put back what has been changed; and apply plaster to it, of the powder from the mill with much ash or flour from the barley meal, after you have taken off the cerote; and apply to it a lighter plaster, and if the plaster applies itself, and the disposition of the sick does not change, let it be until he is well; many times he is well in three weeks.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit maintes fois.	And if abscesses come forth, if you administer what we have said many times.
Et s’il i a brisure et plaie ensamble, rewarde se nule piece de l’os en est ostee; si subtilie de l’oster as estrumens covenaubles a ceu.	And if there is a fracture and a wound together, do not take any piece of bone out; if the osteoporosis is subtle, use tools suitable for this.
Et se li plaie est estroite, si l’eslarge a flaime selonc ta necessiteit.	And if the wound is narrow, broaden it with fire according to your need.
Et quant tu avras ostees toutes ces pieces, et il n’i demore nule, si cout la plaie, s’ele est large, et met sus I des emplaustres covenaubles a ceu, por enjanrer char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have removed all these bones, and there is no delay, if the wound is wide, put on it a plaster that suits this, to dry up, until it is healed.
de la forcele	and with force
Li forcele brise plusors fois devant, devers l’espaule, et li brisure si est selonc III manieres: ou elle est brisie et desevree en II, et i a pieces, et est li plus legiere a restorer; ou il i a brisure avec plaie.	and with force he breaks several times before, towards the shoulder, and the break is according to three ways: or it is broken and dislocated in two, and there are pieces, and it is the lighter to restore; or there is a break with injury.
Et li ovraiges si est quant li brisure est sens plaie, que tu aies II ministres, si que li uns teigne l’ajutoire que sent la forcele brisie; et li autres estende lou col vers la partie; puis met igal la brisure a tes dois, si que li forme soit si com il covient, et n’i ait ne apparance ne chevement.	And the repairs are so when the break is without injury, that you have two ministers, so that one washes the shoulder that is broken with force; and the others stretch the neck towards the part; then make the break even on both sides, so that the shape is as it should be, and there is no appearance or tangling.
Et se tu a mestier de plus estendre, si met desoz l’espaule au malaide une spere reonde de drap, ou de lainne, et soit grosse selonc ta necessiteit; et estent et lieve la forcele, et estraint le spere a ta main, si que tu mettes igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And if you are to extend your skill further, then cover the shoulder of the patient with a round pole of fabric or another material, and make it as large as your need requires; and put pressure on it, and hold the pole in your hand, so that you set back the break evenly, just as is right.
Et se tu ne pues traire le chief de la forcele au defuer, por ceu qu’elle vient em parfont, si covient que li malaides gise sovin sus son hatereil, et met desoz l’espaule I oreillier moien, et boute li ministres l’espaule aval, tant que li os de la forcele soit levez.	And if you are unable to pull the head of the shoulder away from the back, so that it comes out perfectly, then the patient should lie down on his back, and have the shoulder raised a little, and the assistant pulls the shoulder towards the ear, and presses the shoulder bone down, until the bone comes out.
Et puis adrece la brisure a tes dois, et se tu lou trueves debrisiet, si covient que tu fendes sus; et trai fuer les pieces legierement, et se li os ne puet joindre por aucun sormontement, si le cope a l’un des incisoires que tu as; mais que tu mettes desoz la forcele cest estrument, por warder lou syfac:	And then place the break at your sides, and if you find it difficult to split it, then split it with your tool; but hold the pole away from the instrument for safety.
et semble une cuiller, et n’est mie chevez, et soit ausi large com il lou covient, selonc la grandor de l’os et la possance de l’uevre; et ait II chiés, si com tu vois, et soit li uns larges, et li autres estrois, si com est li routure de la plaie que tu as fait quant tu as trait les os; et quant tu es asseurez d’aposteme chaut, si cout la plaie, et se li routure est petite, ou tu doutes aposteme chaut, si emple la plaie de drapelz et de tentes, selonc sa quantiteit.	and appears like a spoon, and is not a hair, and it is also as wide as it should be according to the size of the bone and the ability of the work; and it has II shoulders, if you see it, and one is wide and the other is narrow, just as is the rupture of the wound that you have made when you fractured the bone; and when you are sure of the apoplexy being hot, if the wound is great, and the rupture is small, or if you doubt about the apoplexy being hot, then employ the wound with linen and tents, according to its quantity.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si moille I drapel en oile roset et en aisil et en vin, et met sus.	And if hot apoplexes come, so soak them in oil, rosewater, and wine, and put on them.
Li estrignement de l’os, quant il est sens plaies et sens tailleure, est que tu mettes sus l’os l’enplaustre de la poudre dou molin et d’aubun d’uef, et met estoupes legieres sus, et met une spere desoz l’assele, se tu en as mestier; puis pren une tres grant bende d’une palme de large, puis met I drapeil double sus estoupes, et l’emplaustre; puis pren une estele subtil de III dois de large et de lonc, et l’envoloupe entor celui bendeil, si que li chief dou bendeil soient pendant; et met l’estele sus la briseure, et torne le bendeil sus lou col, et desoz l’asselle sainne, et desoz l’asselle malaide; et la ramoinne de chescune partie, et quant tu vois ke li lieure tient la briseure avenanment, et tu vois clerement que li estele ne se muet desus l’os brisiet, si le rewarde chescun jor, et quant li liiens eslaiche, si lou restraint; et fai gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li met quant il dort I petit orillier desoz l’assele, por lever l’ajutoire en haut; si aligera li brisure de la forcele par l’aligement de l’espaule, ou tu li lie lou bras au col, et ne lou desliier se malvais accidens n’i vient, jusc’a XX jors; puis rencomence l’emplaustre, se tu vois qu’il en ait mestier, et l’estraint et le laisse ensi, tant qu’il soit restorez; et elle est restoree au plus en XXVIII jors, et en moins a aucuns homes.	And if hot apoplexes come, so soak them in oil, rosewater, and wine, and put on them. For the extraction of the bone, when there are wounds and no fracture, it is that you put on the bone the plaster of the mill powder and the ash of uff, and put light splints on, and put a spine around it if you need it; then take a very large bandage one palm wide, then put the drape double splints on, and plaster it; then take an extremely thin staff three fingers wide and long, and wrap it around that bandage so that the chief of the bandage hangs down; and put the staff on the fracture, and turn the bandage back on the neck, and extract the staff with care; and return to each part, and when you see that the bandage holds the fracture in place, and you see clearly that the staff does not move on the bone, so let it rest for a day or two, and when the bonds loosen, if they hold, and the restraint is removed, and make the sick man walk on his heels with care, and put a small splint on him behind the shoulder, in order to raise the dislocation; since the fracture of the clavicle is held by the alignment of the shoulder, or you tie the arm to the neck, and let it not be loosened except if there is a bad accident, until about 20 days; then begin to plaster again, if you see that it is needed, and extract it and leave it like this, until it is healed; and it is healed in 28 days, and less for some men.
de la brisure de l’espaule	of the dislocation of the shoulder
Poc avient que li espaule brise ou large leu ne em mileu, et ne lou seit on fuers que par lou touchement; si l’apareille selonc la figure de la brisure, et la ramoinne selonc sa forme natureil, en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis met sor le leu poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, et estoupes legieres, et met sus I drapeil double; puis met sus une estele large et subtil, un poc plus large de l’espaule, et se desoz l’estele est chevemens en aucun leu de l’espaule, si emple celle cheveure d’estoupes de lin, si que li estele siece igalment; et puis l’estraint a tout une grant bende fermement, si que li estele ne se mueve de son leu, et regarde le liien chescun jor; et toutes les fois k’il amolist, si l’estraint, et met igal l’estele s’elle est fuer de son leu, et gise li malaides sus son costeit; et li espaule est restouree en XX jors ou en xxv, Et quant cist nombres est acomplis, si le deslie, et soies seur, car ce n’est mie os qui se mette fuer legierement.	of the dislocation of the shoulder
Et se une piece de l’os tent avant, et point desoz lou keur, si fent sus, et l’oste, et fai ceu que nos avons dit en la brisure de la forcele d’apaisier aposteme chaut.	And if a piece of the bone comes forward, and does not pull out the nail, then fix it in place, and the bone, and do as we said in the dislocation of the shoulder to relieve an abscess with hot water.
de la brisure dou pis	from a break of the foot
Li peis est aucune fois brisiez em mileu, mais ce avient poc; mais il brise sovent au defuer.	The feet are never broken in mid-air, but this sometimes happens; but they often break at the end.
Et quant il est brisiez emmi, si decline au desoz, et sent li malaides grant dolor, et faute d’alainne, et toust, et par aventure vomist sanc, et apert li chevemens en l’os brisiés, et lou sent om bien.	And when they are broken in mid-air, if they fall on their sides, and feel great pain, and lack support, and sometimes vomit blood, and the bone is broken, and it hurts a lot.
Et li restoracion si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, et li met I cussin entre les espaules, puis presse les espaules, et li assemble les costes des II costelz a tes mains, et subtilie dou mettre igal a toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que li figure de l’os soit si com il covient; puis met sus emplaustres et estoupes desus l’estele subtil de salz, ou d’autre fust legier, et l’envoloupe en I drapeil, et la lie sus l’os brisiet, si qu’elle ne se mueve; et torne le liien reondement au dos, et l’estraint avenanment, et rewarde chescune houre la liure, et s’elle ramolist, si l’estraint; et s’il lou covient desliier, por corrosion ou por prurite que vient au leu, ou dolor ou aposteme, si te haste, et lou deslie, et raie l’emplaustre, et adresce ceu qui i est venus de manieres de cures; puis ramoinne l’emplaustre, et l’estraint tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the restoration is that the patient lie down on his back, and you put a cloth between his shoulders, then press the shoulders together, and assemble the ribs of the two ribs with your hands, and carefully put it together in all ways as much as possible so that the figure of the bone is like this; then put him in a plaster and wrap it around with a thin fabric, and tie it to the broken bone, so that it does not move; and turn the bandage around the back smoothly, and tighten it, and untie it every hour, and if it relaxes, tighten it again; and if he needs to be loosened because of corrosion or itching that comes to the surface, or pain or abscess, do it quickly, and loosen him, and remove the plaster, and treat it in a way that is fitting; then remove the plaster, and tighten it until it is healed.
de la brisure des costes	of the rupture of ribs
Saiches que li briseure des costes ne vient fuer que en leus gros aprés le dos, et au chief dedens, et ne ploient fuer que por ceu qu’eles sont glairouses; et le sent om bien a l’inquisition as dois.	I know that the rib-breaker does not come from the outside but from within, from deep within the back, and it does not bend much because they are rigid; and it hurts very much to the inquiry.
Et li restoremens si est que tu met igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And restore them so that you make the rupture even, as is appropriate.
Et puis met l’emplaustre, et l’estraint d’une estele, se tu en as mestier.	And then put on plaster and tie it with a strap, if you need to.
Et se li brisure des costes est declinans au dedens, si sent li malaides tres grant dolor, et pointure, ausi com de pleuresin, car li os point la toile; et alaine a poinnes, et toust et vomist grant planteit de sanc, et c’est de grief santeit, et li ancien i ont mis grant engien.	And if the rib-break is facing inward, the patient feels great pain and crying, as if they were weeping, because the bone hurts; and he vomits a lot of blood, and it is a sign of illness, and there was great discomfort in the old days.
Et si a de ces qui dient qu’il le covient aministrer viandes qui enflent le ventre, por bouter la briseure au defuer.	And if one of those who serve does not administer meat that swells the belly, to push the break out.
Nos ne faisons mie ceu, que apostemes chaulz n’i viegne, s’il n’i est venus.	We don't make this, unless warm blood comes out, if it doesn't come out.
Et s’il i est venus, si le saine.	And if it has come, let the wound be cleaned.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on met ventouses sor le leu, por sucier forment, et c’est semblant a raison; toutevoie, doutance i a que li ventouse n’atraie les superfluitez au leu por la disposition de foiblece.	And no one should put vents on the spot to draw out the form, and this seems reasonable to me; however, there is doubt that the vents do not attract the excesses to the spot for the purpose of weakness.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on doit covrir le leu de lainne moillie en oile chaut, et met on tentes entre les costes por metre igal la lieure entor, puis soit curez de la cure de pleurisin, de viande et de medicine.	And no one should cover the spot with another wet cloth in oil, and put tents between the ribs to make the place even, then it is cured with the cure for boils, meat, and medicine.
Et se li malaides sent grant dolor qu’il ne puet soffrir par l’os qui point la toile, et doutance est au malaide, si covient fendre sus lou leu de la coste brisie, et covient mettre desoz I estrument por warder lou syfac; et adonques doit on trenchier l’os, et traire legierement, et puis coudre les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, et le curez d’emplaustres, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the patient feels great pain that he cannot bear because of the bone that hits the tent, and there is doubt about the patient, then it is necessary to split the bone in two places at the broken rib, and put on the syringe with medicine; and then the bones should be trimmed, and pulled lightly, and then sewed the two ends of the wound, if it is big, and treated with poultices until it heals.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si met sus drapelz moilliez en oile roset, et met sus lou leu; et cure tandis le leu de ceu qu’il covient a aposteme, et soit gisans sovins sus lou costeit ou il doit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the abscess comes up, if you dip it in oil and put it on your back; and while waiting for the oil of what needs to be an abscess, and make a good bandage at the cost where it is, until he is healed.
de la brisure dou col	of the break from the neck
Aucune fois vient briseure as os dou col, et poc avient k’il ploie; et ausi a l’espinee dou dos.	Once comes the breaker of the bones of the neck, and that he plows; and also to the spine of the back.
Et quant ce avient a aucun, et tu vues savoir s’il sera sanez ou non, si pren warde se tu vois ses mains mollifiies et enflees et mortes, et ne les puet movoir ne estendre, et quant tu les poins d’une aguille, si ne lou sent.	And when this has come to anyone, and you can see if he will be healed or not, if you notice that his hands are soft and swollen and dead, and cannot move them nor stretch them, and when you pinch them with a needle, if they don't hurt.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz em plusors dispositions, et s’il les muet et sent bien quant on les estraint et point, saiches que li jointure de l’os est sauve, et que li malaides iert curez, s’on i met cure.	Know that it is fatal in many situations, and if he does not hurt and feels well when he is pulled and does not feel anything, know that the joint of the bone is saved, and that the patient is healed, if you put the cure on him.
Et se semblans chose vient a l’espinee dou dos, et tu vues savoir s’il iert sanez ou non, si pren warde se li piez sont amollis, et se li accident i sont qui sont em mains, et sus lou dos saut ventositeit et egestion sens volonteit; et quant on l’a sovineit sus son ventre, si saut egestion sens volonteit.	And if similar things come to the back of the neck, and you can tell whether it is healthy or not, take note if the muscles are soft, and consider the accident that happened and the pain and discomfort in the hand, and when it is revived on its stomach, if there is pain without will.
Et quant il est sovinez sus son dos et il vuet asseller, si ne puet.	And when it is revived on its back and it tries to move, it cannot.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz: si ne laboreir mie en sa cure.	Know that it is fatal: do not try to work on it in treatment.
Et se cist accident ne li vienent, si est li chose plus legiere.	And if this accident does not come from somewhere, then this is the lightest thing.
Et li cure si est que tu rewardes s’il i a aposteme chaut, si met sus l’espinee oile roset ou oile de moieuf d’uef, tant qu’il soit apaisiez; puis met sus un des emplaustres confortans et sechans, et le lie d’un liien, et comande au malaide a reposer; et ne dorme mie sus celle partie ou il sent la dolor, tant k’il soit sanez.	And the treatment is this: if there is an abscess, put oil or linseed oil on it until it is calm; then put on one of the plasters and cover it with a bandage, and tie it up, and command the patient to rest; and do not lie down in that part where he feels pain until he is better.
Et se aucuns os se dessevre, si covient coper sus lou keur; et oste l’os, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, a une costure, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li chiés de l’os est brisiez, ki est apelez li «chiés de la kowe», se i boute ton pouchet de ta main senestre, et le met igal a l’autre main a ton pooir, puis met l’emplaustre et l’estele sus, se tu en a mestier; puis l’estraint, et s’il i a os desevreit, si fent sus, et l’oste, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee.	Et si certains os sont désarticulés, couvrez-les avec du goudron; then oste l'os, puis assemblez les deux lèvres de la plaie, s'elle est grande, avec une couture, puis appliquez le cataplasme en utilisant du charbon, jusqu'à ce qu'il soit guéri; et si li chiés de l'os est brisiez, ki est apelez li «chiés de la kowe», si fent un creux dans ton pouchet avec ta main senestre, et le met igal a l'autre main a ton pooir, puis met l'emplaastre et l'estele sus, s'il en as mestier; then l'estraint, and if there are desevreit os, fent-les puis curez la plaie tant qu'elle soit sanee.
de la brisure de l’os de la hainche	For the break in the bone of the thigh
Poc avient que li os de la hainche soit brisiez, et s’il avient, si n’avient fuer c’un poc d’amenuisement au chief; et fent dou lonc, et decline au pardedens, et vient au malaide dolor au leu, et pointure, et enfle ceu que brise.	If the hip joint becomes dislocated, and if it does, there would be a little loss of movement in the head; and let it lengthen, and decline towards the back, and bring pain to the patient in that place, and a swelling where it is broken.
Et li restoration si est que tu estendes ta main sus, tant que tu soies sus la briseure; et saiches quelz est li brisure et li figure de li; et se li brisure est au chief soulement, si met igal cele brisure, tant qu’ele soit a figure natureil.	And the restoration is that you extend your hand over it as long as you are above the break; and know what is the break and its shape; and if the break is at the top, make it even as much as possible until it is in its natural shape.
Et se li brisure est dou lonc, ou elle decline au dedens, si fai gesir le malaide sus son ventre, tant que li restauration de cele brisure te soit aparillie.	And if the break is long, or if it declines inward, make the patient stand on his stomach as much as the restoration of that break allows him to.
Et quant tu l’avras mise igal, si met sus l’emplaustre, puis met sus une estele de fust ou de keur, et estraint la briseure, si qu’ele ne se mueve; et emple le leu desoz les costes, tant que li lieure soit igalz.	And when you have made it even, if you put the plaster on, then put a wooden or cork splint on top of it, and tighten the break so that it does not move; and fix the position of the bones as much as possible.
Et comande au malaide k’il dorme sus son costeit sain, ou sus son dos.	And command the patient to sleep on his back or side.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si n’i tochier, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et met sus ceu que nos avons devant dit; et puis revien a la restauration, et l’estraint si com il covient, s’il n’i a nul mavais accident; et c’est li maniere.	And if the abscess bursts, if it is not infected, as long as the abscess burst has healed, and put on what we have said above; then return to healing, and hold it like that, unless there is any accident; and this is the way.
de la brisure de l’ajutoire	of the dislocation of the shoulder
Li adjutoires est ceu qui est entre lou coute et lou chief de l’espaule, et s’il est brisiez, si le doit on restorer selonc l’une des II manieres: dont l’une est que tu pren I fust plain de moiene groissor, selonc ceste forme:	the shoulder is what is between the collar and the top of the shoulder, and if it is broken, then one should restore it according to one of the two ways: one is that you take a strong piece of wood, according to this form:
Et lie as II chiés II liens, et les pent en haut, et siece li malaide sus I siege; puis li giete som bras brisiet sus le fust, tant qu’il viegne a l’aissele, et ait em mi une corbeure de fust, puis pent sus aucune pesant chose ou li ministres l’estende aval; puis mette li mires la briseure igal a ses mains ensamble, tant que li briseure retorne si com il covient.	And lay down two stakes of wood, and tie the patient to them, then hang him up by one leg; then let him fall onto the wood, until he reaches the ground, and have a strong piece of wood ready, then tie the broken arm to it, so that the patient hangs by his arms; then make sure that the broken arm does not move.
Et li autre maniere si est que on sovine le malaide sus son hatereil, et li lie la main a son col, puis comande a II ministres que li uns teigne ceu qui est sus la briseure a ses mains, et li autres teigne desoz a tout I liien, et estende chescuns a sa partie.	Et l'autre manière si est que on souvine le malade sur son haireil, et li lie la main à son col, puis commande à II ministres que li uns teigne ceu qui est sus la briseure à ses mains, et li autres teigne desoez à tout I liien, et étend desoz chescuns à sa partie.
Et se tu vues que li estraction soit plus fors, si estraint I liien desoz la briseure, et sus la briseure, et estende chescuns des ministres a sa part.	And if you see that the extraction is too strong, then remove the chain from the break, and on the break, and extend each of the ministers to his part.
Et se li briseure est prochiene au chief de l’espaule, si covient que tu mettes I liien moien desoz l’assele, et I autre vers lou coute, desoz la briseure; et ausi se li briseure est devers lou coute, si i covient mettre I liien legierement, sens labor, tant que li briseure soit igalz sus lou leu, et sus lou coute; puis met igal la brisure, si com il covient, et l’estraint, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the break is near the shoulder's head, then you should put the chain gently from the assembly, and on the other side of the break; and if the break is on one side of the collar, then you should put the chain lightly, without effort, as long as the break is even on its place, and on its side; then put the break even, if it is to come, and hold it, so that the abscesses do not come.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si ne l’estraindre mie jusc’a VII jors, et met sus lainne moillie en aisil et en oile roset, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez; puis l’estraint, et li maniere de l’estraindre si est que tu mettes l’emplaustre sus la briseure, puis assemble le bras sus l’ajutoire, et met ta main sus l’espaule ou sus lou sein; et met le drapeil, et estraint sus l’ajutoire, et sus lou bras, si que li bras soit en leu d’esteles, s’aucune chose ne le te deffent, ou se li os n’est muez.	And if an abscess comes out, do not extract it until seven days have passed; and put a wet cloth on it with rosewater, until the abscess is calm; then extract it, and the way to extract it is that you put the plaster on the broken part, and then join the arm to the shoulder, and put your hand on the shoulder or on the loins; and wrap it up, and extract it by the shoulder and by the arm, so that the arm stays in its place, if nothing hurts it or if the bone does not break.
Et se tu doutes que li os ne se mueve, si use d’esteles, et met sus la brisure une estele plus large et plus fort des autres, et ait entre chescune estele I doi d’espaice, et soit chescune estele si grans qu’elle passe la briseure III dois de chescune part; puis estrain sus les esteles, ensi com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre sus la briseure, plus fort et moins en aloignant.	And if you doubt that the bone moves, then use a splint, and put a larger and stronger splint on the broken part than the others, and leave two inches of space between each splint, and let each splint be so big that it goes over the break by three inches on either side; then extract it with the splints, as I said at the beginning about the plaster on the break, more firmly and less by moving away.
Et se tu vois l’assise des esteles, et l’estrignement, si com nos avons dit, en l’oure que tu restoures le membre brisiet, et tu doutes l’aposteme chaut, si le laisse a liier jusc’a septime jor, si com nos avons dit; puis regarde chescuns III jors lou lien, que prurite ne enfleure n’i viegne au leu, ou li norrissemens ne puist venir au membre por ceu k’il est trop estrois.	And if you see the setting of the stars, and the extraction, as we have said, in the hour that you restore the broken member, and you doubt the incision warm, let it be tied up until the seventh day, as we have said; then observe each three days whether there is a pain or not; do not allow the swelling to come into place, or the healing will not come to the member because it is too tight.
Si l’adrece, si com nos avons dit.	If you doubt, as we have said.
Et se nulz telz accidens n’i vient, si ne lou desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou plus, et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ait ses mains sus son stomac; et met desoz l’ajutoire I cussin plain de laine igalment, et regarde chescune houre dou jor ou de la nut, que li figure dou membre brisiet ne se mueve, ou ne soit amollis li liiens; si l’adrece par la vertu de medicine, et li done la viande que nos avons devant mis, en teil maniere que li viande soit au premier subtilz; et quant il comance a reprendre, si soit grosse.	And if no such accident happens, and he does not loosen it than after three days or more, and the patient sleeps on his back, and has his hands on his stomach; and fasten the shoulder with one piece of linen evenly, and observe every hour of the day or night, that the figure of the broken member does not move, or is not softened by the ties; if it heals with the power of medicine, and gives him food that we have mentioned before, in such a way that the food is at the first layer; and when he begins to recover, let it be thick.
Et est costume que li ajutoire et li jambe doient estre repris en XL jors dou tout; et adonques lou doit on desliier et aministrer bain et medicines d’oignemens por le leu adrecier.	And it is fitting that the shoulder and leg should be put back in place after 40 days of all; and then one should untie it and administer to it bath and medicines of ointments to apply.
Et se li estricture est laide et emboee, si demore a desliier L jors ou II mois.	And if the contraction is ugly and blocked, if it does not separate in one day or two months.
de la brisure du bras	of the fracture of the arm
Li bras est compos de II os, qui sont apelez li dui «foscile», de coi li uns est petis, et est cil qui enseut le pouchet; et li autres est grans, et est cil qui est desoz, devers lou petit doi; par aventure brise li grans foscile soulement, ou li petis, et par aventure andui ensamble.	The arm is composed of two bones, which are called the "fosciles," one small, and that one is the elbow; and the other large, and that is the shoulder, towards the small one; perhaps a fracture of the large foscile alone, or of the small one, and perhaps both together.
Quant li petis fosciles est brisiez, li restaurations est legiere, et li sanations; et quant li grans est brisiez, si est li sanation male, et plus griés que quant il sont brisiez andui ensamble.	When the small foscile is broken, the restoration is easy, and the recovery; and when the large one is broken, the recovery is bad, and more painful than when it is broken both together.
Se c’est li petis foscile qui est brisiez soulement, si le covient poc estendre legierement, et mettre igal.	If this little fowl is just slightly bruised, then it is necessary to lightly stretch it out, and place it in a straight position.
Et se c’est li grans foscile, si le covient estraindre plus fort; et l’estende sus I cussin, et teigne le pouchet de la main plus haut des autres, et li petis dois plus bas des autres dois, et soit li malaides croisiez sus lui meisme, et I cussin devant lui plus haut, que li malaides ne soffre nule labor; puis estende li ministres som bras a la partie desoz a sa main, ou a I liien, et uns autres ministres a I autre au desus.	If the large fowl is injured, then it must be pulled out more forcefully; and extend it on one knee, and raise the leg with your hand higher than the other two legs, and the small fowl lower than the others, and so that the patient lies across it in the middle, and one foot before him higher than the other, so that the patient suffers no effort; then extend the other legs with your arms to the wounded part at their side, or at their feet, and another minister on the other foot above.
Et puis le mette li mires igal, selonc sa millor forme.	And then he should be made equal, according to his best form.
Et se en la brisure a pieces, si met chescune en son leu, et s’il en i a nule desevree ke poigne lou keur, et tu ne la pues restorer en son leu, si fent sus et l’oste, si com nos avons dit devant.	And if there are broken pieces, then each one should be put in its place; and if any of them have come loose and cannot be held in place, then you should fix it with a pin or nail, as we have said above.
Et se avec la briseure a plaie, je en ai parleit au chapistre singuler; si pren la cure.	And if with the cautery there is an injury, I have spoken to it in the singular chapter of the ointment; if he takes the cure.
Et se en l’encomencement dou restorement sorvient apostemes chaus, si glue I drapeil de cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire blainche, que ne soit mie ne trop durs ne trop molz; et lie I drapeil par sus subtilment, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez.	And if in the beginning of the restoration there are abscesses, I will cover them with a paste made of oil and white wax that is not too hard or too soft; and I will cover them from above gently, until the abscesses are calmed down.
Et puis oste lou cerote, et i met l’emplaustre de la poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, pues met les esteles, et soit li estele de la briseure adés plus fors, et un poc plus large que les autres; et saiches que il doit avoir VI esteles ou bras em plusors dispositions: soit que li briseure soit en l’un des os, soit en II; et estraint plus sus la briseure que autre part, et toz jors moins en aloignant, si com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre; et soient li drapelz que sont sus la briseure molz et moistes, et ne soient mie dur ne aspres; et soit li filz, dont il est estrains, de lin, ne trop gros ne trop menus, si com nos avons dit.	And then cover the bone with the paste, and I will put the ointment of the miller's powder with a lot of ink, because I will put the splints, and let the splint of the injury be higher by a hand and more wide than the others; and know that there should be VI splints or arms in several positions: whether the injury is in one bone or in II; and stretch it further up than anywhere else, all the time less pulling away, as I said at the beginning of the chapter of the ointment; and may the drapes that are on the injury be soft and moist, and not too hard or sharp; and let the thread from which it is stretched be made of linen, nor too thick nor too thin, as we have said.
Et rewarde lou membre et lou liien aprés aucuns jors.	And rest the member and the lien for a few days.
Et se aucuns mavais accidens vient au membre, si com prurite ki vient au membre, si covient que tu aroses lou membre d’aigue chaude, tant que cil prurites soit apaisiez; et laisse le membre ne mie estroit reposer.	And if any bad accident comes to the member, such as itching that comes to the member, then it is convenient that you dip the member in hot water, until the itch is calmed; and let the member not rest too tight.
Et puis rencomence l’estrignement, et se li liiens est amolis et li os desevrez, et semblant chose, si l’adresce.	And then start the extraction again, and if the liens are softened and the bones deviated, and similar things, then address them.
Et se pren warde se li norrissemens ne puet venir au membre, por ceu qu’il est trop estrois, si covient que tu l’amollisses I poc, et laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant que li norrissemens i corre, et puis l’estraint.	And if one is not warned that the member cannot be reset, because it is too tight, then it is convenient that you soften it a little, and leave it thus for a few days, until the swelling goes down, and then extract it.
Et se nules de ces choses que nos avons dit ne vient au malaide, si ne lou desliier jusc’a XX jors.	And if none of these things that we have said comes to the patient, then do not remove the bandage until XX days have passed.
ou enqui entor, puis li pent les mains a son col, et soit ses cols igalz, et se warde de movement et de degitement, et dorme sus son dos; et saiches que ceste briseure est restoree en XXX jors ou en XXXV, et par aventure en XX jors, selonc les compositions et les complexions des vertus.	At the end of the first sentence: "And so he keeps his hands at his throat, and makes his neck even, and wards off movement and turning over, and sleeps on his back; and know that this breaker is healed in 30 days or in 35, and perhaps in 20, according to the compositions and complexions of the virtues.
de la brisure de la main	of the breaking of the hand
Saiches que au dos de la main et as nous des dois avient poc de briseures, et n’i vient mais que ploieure maintes fois.	is that at the back of the hand and to us on both sides there are few breaks, and comes only that it bleeds many times.
Et quant li plante de la main est brisie ou ploie, si covient que li malaides siece croisiet, et siet droitement devant lui igalement; puis met sa main sus la toie estendue, et estende li ministres les os brisiez, et les mete igalz li mires, tant qu’il soient bien joint; et met l’emplastre et les estoupes, se apostemes n’i vient, puis i met une estele selonc la quantiteit dou leu; et soit envoloupee en I drapeil de lin.	And when the plant of the hand is broken or bleeds, it is necessary that the patient cross his fingers and sit straight evenly; then he lays his hand on the extended cloth, and extends the broken bones, and makes them even, as long as they are well joined; and he puts the plaster and the poultices, if an abscess comes, then he puts a patch according to the quantity of the place; and let it be wrapped in a sheet of linen.
Et se li briseure est au pardedens entor lou ventre de la plante, si fai une spere de drapelz, et comande au malaide qu’il l’estrigne a sa plante brisie; et puis l’estrain d’un lonc drapeil, et soit li estele de keur souef ausi grans com li plante de la main, et l’estraint, si com il covient.	And if it breaks within the garden of the plant between the loins, so make a flagpole, and command the sick that he strangle to his broken plant; and then draw out with a long curtain, and make its steele of great air as well as the plant of the hand, and draw.
Et se li brisure est au defuer, si covient que tu mettes une estele sus, et une autre desoz en la plante, si que li mains soit overte et droite, puis le lie tot entor la main, et estanche lou liien entre les dois.	And if it breaks on the back, so that you put a steele on, and another desos in the plant, so that the hands are open and straight, then bind it all around the hand, and tie the ligature between the two.
Et se li briseure vient a aucun des nous des dois, se c’est li pouchés, si le met igal, si com il covient; et l’estraint avec la plante, et se tu vues si met une estele droite petite por lever la briseure, et ne se mueve; et se li brisure est as autres dois, si com en l’indice ou l’un des autres, si le met igal, et lou lie avec lou doi sain qui est aprés; ou tu les lie toz en I tenant, que mues vaut, ou tu met sus une estele, si com ou pouchet; et pren warde en la restauration et en la disposition d’aposteme chaut, et secor ceu qui i vient, si com j’ai dit.	And if the break comes to one of the two, it is a pouch, so make it even, as it is right; and hold it with the plant, and if you see that there is no movement, then put a small straight steele to lift the break, and do not move it; and if the break is in the other two, as in the index or one of them, make it even, and bind it with the healthy hand that comes after; or you bind all three together, holding them so they don't move, or you put a steele on it, as though you were poking; and take care in the restoration and arrangement of the aposteme, and help those who come to it, as I have said.
de la cuixe brisie	of the breast wound
Li os de la cuixe est maintes fois brisiez, et bien le voit on quant elle torne devant et derrier; et li restauration si est c’on lie I liien desus la briseure, et I autre desoz.	The chest bone is often bruised, and one can clearly see it when it turns forward and backward; and the healing process is good if we wrap it tightly with a bandage, and another above it.
Et li malaides gise sus sa faice, puis estende chescuns ministres son lien a sa part igalment; et c’est quant li brisure est emmi l’os.	And the patient lies on his face, then extends each minister his bandage equally to his part; and it is when the fracture has entered the bone.
Et se li brisure est prochiene a la racine de la cuixe, si soit li uns des liiens devers lou poignil, et li autres liiens desoz la briseure.	And if the fracture is near the root of the breast, let one minister's bandage go forward to the fist, and another's go backward from the wound.
Et ausi s’elle est prochiene au genoil, et adonques soit li liens delez lou genoil, et soit li extension aval; puis mette li mires l’os igal a ses II mains, tant qu’il soit selonc sa figure natureil, et puis met l’emplaustre, et lou lie, se apostemes chaz n’i vient.	And if it is near the kneecap, and then let one minister' bandage go forward to the knee, and another' s go backward from the wound; and then put the master at equal levels with his two hands until it is in its natural shape, and then apply the plaster, and wrap him up, so that no cut comes to him.
Et s’il i a aposteme chaut, si le laisse apaisier puis revien a ton ovraige et a ta cure; li lieure est faite en teil maniere.	And if there is an abscess that has become hot, let it calm down again and then return to your work and your treatment; the time is appropriate in this way.
Il covient que tu envoloupes sus la briseure I bendeil dur doublé en II ou III, et en demoure li superfluitez, puis torne la jambe tant que li talons veigne a la racine de la naige, et boute I fil lonc entre la cuixe et la jambe, delez lou genoil desoz, et veignent li chief dou fil au desus; puis torne sus la jambe et sus la cuixe le bendeil, puis met sus la briseure esteles, et met une estele sus l’os de la jambe; puis emple le leu vuit entre la jambe et la cuixe de drapelz souef por mettre igal l’estrignement, puis comence a liier forment III tors ou IIII sus la briseure; et quant plus vas en sus de la briseure, et moins l’estraint; puis enten as II chiés dou fil que tu as bouteit entre la jambe et la cuixe, et en lie III esteles que sont desus, puis revai au desoz au chief dou fil, tant que tu veignes delez le piet; et l’estraint, si qu’il ne se mueve de son leu, puis le laisse ensi, puis k’il n’i vient ne aposteme ne enfleure n’autre semblant.	And if there is an abscess that has become hot, let it calm down again and then return to your work and your treatment; the time is appropriate in this way.
Et s’il i avient, si le deslie, et adresce ceu que i vient, si com nos avons dit maintes fois; et se il i a pieces de l’os que poigne, si le covient ewer, s’om puet; et s’on ne puet, si covient fendre le leu, et traire fuer; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant k’il soit sanez.	And if it happens, if it falls, and turns this way or that way, as we have said many times; and if there are pieces of the bone that hold on, then one should take care; and if one cannot, then one should split the place, and pull it out hard; and heal it as we have said, until it is well.
Et aucune fois est brisie li cuixe ensi c’on i met esteles, si com en l’ajutoire et ou bras; toutevoie, en la restauration ensi faite ne cloche mie li malaides.	And in no case should the surgeon use a knife there, as we have said for the shoulder and arm; however, when restoring it in this way does not improve the patient.
Et saiches que li cuixe est restoree en L jors, ou poc moins ou poc plus, selonc les diversitez des complexions.	And know that the chest is restored in a day or less or more, according to the diversity of complexions.
de la ruelle dou genoil	from the knee joint
Saiches que en la ruelle dou genoil avient poc brisure, mais elle ploie maintes fois.	And know that in the knee joint there is little rupture, but it bleeds many times.
Et s’elle brise, si n’est mais c’une fendure, ou I pertus, et avient a tout plaie, et sens plaie, et ce sent om bien.	And if it breaks, except for a split or a gap, and comes to all the pain, and without pain, and this feels good.
Et li restauration si est c’on mette igal ceu qui est rons a ses dois, tant qu’il soit assemblez mues c’on puet; puis met l’emplaustre, et i met une estele reonde, se tu en as mestier, et l’estraint si com il covient, puis rewarde toutes les dispositions que nos avons dit ens autres briseures, si com aposteme chaut et autre semblant; si met a chescun accident ceu k’il li covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the healing process is so that one who is bent on both sides is made straight again as much as possible; then apply the plaster, and put a round bandage on it if you need to, and hold it in place as it should be held, and then follow all the measures we have spoken of in other chapters, such as a hot blister and others that are similar; then apply to each accident whatever is appropriate until it is healed.
de la brisure de la jambe	About the breaking of the leg
Saiches que en la jambe ait II os, de coi li uns est apelez par droit non «mustelz», et li autres est apelez «foscile»; et avient tout auteil briseure com il vient au bras, et por ceu est li restauracion si com celle dou bras igalment, et li ovraiges est tout i. Et se li dui os sont brisiet ensamble, si torne li jambe de toutes pars.	We know that in the leg there are two bones, one which is called by right "mustelz" and the other "foscile"; and it happens with the breaking of the leg just as with the arm, and for this reason the healing process is the same; and if the two bones are broken together, the leg turns on all sides.
Et se li os subtilz est brisiez, si torne devant.	And if his thin nose is broken, then turn away from it.
Et se li gros os est brisiez, si sent on grant dolor, et le voit on bien; et torne desoz.	And if the thick bone is broken, then one feels great pain and can see it well; and turn aside.
Adonques amenistre extension, et le met igal, et lie les esteles igalement; mais toutevoie, il covient se li brisure est laide, et il i a plusors pieces, que li extension soit menor et plus legiere; et l’alige selonc ta vertu.	And then make an extension, and make it even, and bind the joints evenly; however, the break is ugly, and there are many pieces, so that the extension is smaller and lighter; and align it according to your skill.
Et quant tu as tout acomplit ton ovraige, si pren II faixes de fust chevees que porpreignent la jambe d’une part et d’autre, et soient dou lonc de la jambe des le genoil jusque desoz; puis envoloupe en II leus I bendeil desus et desoz, et le lie em mileu ausi, et a ceste lieure ne pora li jambe decliner a destre ne a senestre, et ensi est bien; et aucun i aministrent I bers dou lonc de la jambe, et s’est de fust, et i met on la jambe por warder de movement, et proprement fait on ceu en la brisure ou il a plaie; et remue chescun jor la jambe, por veoir s’il i a aposteme chaut n’autre accident; si le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have finished your work, take two long pieces of wood that will overlap the leg on one side and the other, and be long from the knee to the heel; then wrap them over it two by two on top and below, and bind it tightly in the middle, and at this binding no leg should hang down to the right or left, and so is good; and no one administer I darts of the long leg, and if it is, put the leg in order not to move, and properly do that in the break where there is a wound; and stir every day the leg, to see if there is an abscess or any other accident; then heal as long as it is healthy.
de la brisure des os dou piet	of the break of the bones of the foot
A la cheville ne vient point de brisure, mais as os dou piet vient aucune fois brisure et as dois poc, et n’i avient fuer que quassure em plusor dispositions.	At the ankle there is no break at all, but from the bones of the foot comes a break only sometimes and in two ways, and has never been seen except in many cases.
Et s’il avient as os dou piet brisure, et tu vois ces os sormonter l’un l’autre, si mette si malaides som piet sus la terre, ausi com s’il voloit aler, et puis met maintenant ton piet sus lou sien, lai ou li os sont levez, puis le presse tant k’il reveignent en lor leus; puis met l’emplaustre et estoupes sus, et met desoz lou ventre dou piet une petite tauble a II chiés plains, puis l’estraint au piet avenanment, puis que tu as envoloupez drapelz entor, et autres choses dont tu as mestier.	If there is a break in the bones of the foot, and you see these bones overlapping each other, so that if he wants to walk, then now put your foot on his own, let the bones come up, then press them together until they get back into their places; then apply plaster to it and wrap it up, and place a small table of II flat pieces in front of the foot, then fasten it to the foot with a rope, and then take the drapelz you have laid out, and other things that you need.
Et quant III jors ou IIII seront passez, si deslie lou liien, car tu troveras les os igalz, soient brisiez, soient desaluez.	When three days or four have passed, if the leg is still swollen, for you will find the bones even, whether they are broken or dislocated.
Et s’il i a aucuns des dois brisiez, si les restoure, si com nos avons dit as dois de la main; puis met au doi brisiet une estele selonc la longesce dou doi, et soit un poc plus large, puis met desoz le piet celle tauble que j’ai dit, et l’estrain avenanment; et s’il en i a II ou III, ou plus, brisiez, si met sus chescun doi une estele selonc sa quantiteit, envoloupee en I drapeil de lin, et estraint la tauble desoz lou piet; et soit estans sus lou chief de la tauble defuer lou ventre dou piet, si qu’il le teigne bien.	And if there are any of the two broken, if you restore them, as we said to the two of the hand; then put on the broken one a stone according to its length from the two, and let it be a little more wide, then place below the stone that I have said, and strain going forward; and if there are II or III, or more, broken, then put on each one a stone according to its quantity, wrapped in a linen cloth, and strain the stone below the stone; and let them remain on top of the head of the stone far from the belly of the stone, so that it covers it well.
Et covient que tu n’oblier mie les autres choses que j’ai dit as autres briseures, des que nos avons dit; et secor chescun accident si com il covient.	And you must not forget the other things that I have said for the others breakers, since we have said it; and heal each accident as it is needed.
de la brisure de l’os dou poignil	of the breaker of the bone of the hand
Quant li os de la nature la femme est brisiez, si la fai seoir enlargie, puis l’encline a la partie dou dos, et soit tenue par derrier; puis emplisse li baile la nature de la malaide de couton, et en i mette ausi gros com I sto; puis deboute la femme, et lieve lou dos poc et poc, et adonques saut li coton, tant qu’il vient a l’entree de la nature, et revient li os avec lou sto; et quant elle vuet pissier, si oste lou coton, et quant elle a pissiet, se li remette, et ensi faice VII jors ou entor: si sera restoree li brisure, et se tu vues, pren une vessie de berbis, et lie au pertus une cainne, et boute toute la vessie en la nature; puis soffle en la cainne forment, tant que li vessie soit enflee dedens: la nature si revenra li brisure; puis soit emplie de coton, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit sanez.	When a woman's nature is broken, if she is set upright enlarged, then lean her to the back part of the loins and be held from behind; then fill the nature with cotton of the sickness, and put in it as big as I stand; then take off the woman, and lightly touch her loins little by little, and then jump the cotton, until it comes to the entrance of nature, and brings back the bones with a stand; and when she wants to urinate, if she jumps the cotton, and when she has urinated, let her return, and in this way do seven days or more: then will be restored the break, and she will die, take a bladder of sheep, and tie a cord around the neck, and pour all the bladder into nature; then blow into the bladder making a form, until the bladder is inside: nature will return the break; then be filled with cotton, and let it stand for some days, until it is well.
Et quant li os dou poignil de l’ome est brisiez, ou de la femme, si le restoure ensi com nos avons dit en l’os de la hainche; et ne sont mie occultees ces briseures prochienes a celui qui i met son estude et son us, et entent mon livre.	And when the jaw of man or woman is broken, if it be set back as we have said in the hip bone; and these fractures are not hidden from him who puts his study and use thereon, and hears my book.
Car li brisure li signifie em plusors dispositions la droite voie de la restauration: enten le donques.	For the break means many things right way to restore it: hear then.
En la verge, quant elle est brisie, pren une gorge d’oie et i boute la verge; puis envoloupe drapelz entor, et le laisse III jors ou enqui entor, et il sera sanez hastanment.	In the neck, when it is broken, take a goose's beak and bottle it up; then wrap it in a cloth, and leave it three days or more, and he will be healed without hospital.
de brisure avec plaie	of fracture with wound
Il covient a celui qui a brisure avec plaie, meismement s’elle est grans, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire ou semblant, qu’il soit sainiez maintenant, si que les sainies que nos avons dit le tesmoignent.	It is good for the fracture with wound, even if it is great, as the hip bone or shoulder blade or similar, that he be healed now, so that the healers that we have said testify.
Et se li plaie saine, si la restainche de vitriole, se tu n’as autre chose, puis rencomence a restorer la briseure en cele meisme houre, ou celui jor, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the wound heals, and you do not have any other remedy, then begin to restore the broken one in that same hour or day when the blisters come out.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si laisse la restauration jusc’a nuevime jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et n’i touchier ne au tier jor ne au quart, car tu i feroies venir malvais accident.	And if the blisters come out, and you leave the restoration until the next day, as long as the blisters are calm, and you don't touch them neither on the third nor on the fourth day, because you would bring about a bad accident.
Et se li os brisiez est aparans sus lou keur descovert, si covient que tu lou mettes a point legierement a tes mains, a extension petite.	And if the broken bone appears on the outside of the knee cap, it is necessary that you put it into position gently with your hands, with a small extension.
Et se li extensions ne t’est apareillie por mettre igal a tes mains, si le ramoine a cest estrument qui est de fer, qui a VII dois ou VIII de lonc, et li largesce est selonc la quantiteit de la plaie; et por ceu est mestier au mire qu’il empreigne III ou IIII, selonc ceu qu’il en ait mestier en chescune cure de briseure; et soit rons et un poc gros, k’il ne ploie mie a la compression sus lou membre a ton ovraige, et soit agus devant, et gros des le mileu en avant, ensi:	And if the extensions are not equal to your hands, put them into position with an iron instrument, which has seven or eight inches in length, and whose width corresponds to the quantity of the wound; and for this purpose it is necessary that one should use three or four, according to what is needed in each cure of a broken limb; and they should be round and a little thick, so as not to press on the member by your work, and be sharp at the front and thick in the middle:
Et est apelez «palainche», por coi il covient que li chiés corbes soit mis sus lou chief de l’os apparent; et le boute a une fois, tant k’il reviegne, et soit igalz l’un encontre l’autre.	And is called "pallanche," for it is necessary that the bent shoulder be placed on the top of the head of the visible bone; and is set once, until he recovers, and is even one against the other.
Et se li brisure est subtilz, et li estrumens ne puet bien prendre l’os, si covient que tu copes lou chief de l’os, tant que li estrumens en ait possance.	And if the fracture is subtle, and the instrument cannot take the bone well, it is necessary that you chop the head of the bone, until the instrument has the ability.
Et se tu ne pues ramener l’os, si com nos avons dit, si lou cope d’un estrument covenable a ceu, ou incisoire ou soieure, a ton pooir; puis reis ceu qui est demorez en l’os d’aspreteit et de menues escorces.	And if you cannot bring the bone back, as we have said, with an appropriate instrument, either an incision or a saw, at your power; then make those who are delayed in the bone with roughness and small scrapings.
Et quant li os est ramenez, et li malaides sent grant dolor aprés, saiches qu’il n’est mie en son leu natureil.	And when the bone is brought back, and the patient feels great pain after it, know that it is not in its natural position.
Si fai tant qu’il soit en son leu, puis moille I drapeil en vin stiptique noir, et proprement se c’est en esteit; et ne mettre mie sus la plaie cerote ne autre chose ou il ait oile, qu’il n’i faice venir porriture et corruption; puis aministre esteles quant tu as restoreit l’os, et laisse la plaie descoverte, et cope la coverture tout entor, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et te done bien en garde que li plaie ne soit estrainte avec la brisure; et maintes fois ont ce fait li fol mire, et ont fait venir sus le malaide ou mort ou corrodent aucune fois; et soit li estrignemens plus molz et plus souef des autres brisures.	If you do so that it is in its place, then dip the drape in black wine vinegar and clean it properly; and do not put on top of the wound wax or any other oil where there is oil, lest it cause pus and corruption; then administer leeches when you have restored the bone, and leave the wound uncovered, and wrap the covering all around, according to the quantity of the wound, and give yourself well in guard that the wound is not tightened with the fracture; and many times such a thing has happened, and has brought about the death or corruption of the patient on one occasion; and the instrument is softer and less acute than other fractures.
Et se li plaie est male ou grans, et tu doutes que mavais accidens n’i veigne, si com nos avons dit, et tu trueves dolor au leu, si n’i covient mie mettre sus esteles; mais envoloupe entor, en leu d’esteles, drapelz durs, et les lie.	And if the wound is bad or large, and you doubt that a bad accident will not come to it, as we have said, and you feel pain in the place, then it is not good to put it on splints; but wrap hard drapes around it instead of splints, and bind them.
Et quant tu vois aprés I jor ou II enjanrer bowe a la plaie, si oste ceu que tu as mis sus a tout vin, et i met oignement sanant plaies, si com oignement tetrafarmaçon et semblans.	And when you see after one or two days that bow is going into the wound, if you have put anything on it yet, and you make a clean break with four-fold bandaging and similar things;
Et covient que tu deslies lou membre II fois le jor, lou matin et au vespre, tant qu’il soit soudez et sanez.	Then you must disconnect the limb twice a day, in the morning and at night, until it is healed and restored.
Et covient que li membres soit aparilliez en teil maniere que li bowe corre aval legierement.	And the limbs should be taken apart in such a way that the bow does not run down quickly.
Et se maint jor trespassent, et il ne puet souder mais rent adés bowe, saiches k’il i a petites pieces d’os, por coi il covient que tu quieres la plaie avec tente, et oste toutes ces pieces desevrees que font venir celle dolor.	And if one day passes, and he cannot keep the limb apart but lets it run together again, knowing that there are little pieces of bone, you must make a clean break with bandages, and remove all these troublesome pieces which bring about pain.
Et se fistule vient au leu, ou autre maniere de corruption, si covient que tu le cures, selonc ceu qu’il dist en son chapistre ci devant.	And if a fistula comes to light, or some other form of corruption, then you must cure it according to what he said in his chapter above.
Et quant li os est brisiez, et apert sus lou membre, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire, et autres semblans des grans membres, si ne le traire mie, car maintes fois en vient li mors, mais le laisse tant qu’il porrisse; par aventure cherra par lui aprés XX jors ou XXX, puis cure la plaie, se tu pues; et se tu ne pues, si la laisse.	And if the bone is broken and opened on the limb, as with the hip or shoulder bone, and other large bones, then do not pull it out, for many die when this is done, but rather let it rot; perhaps after XX days or XXX, then treat the wound if you can; and if you cannot, then leave it.
des brus qui vienent sor la sodure	Of wounds that come from the outside
Nous vienent maintes fois aprés la santeit de la briseure, meismement quant c’est pres de la jointure, et laide chose est a veoir li figure dou membre; et par aventure ne puet faire li membres ses ovraiges naturelz.	Come often do we see after the health of the broken bone, especially when it is near a joint, and what an ugly thing it is to see the limb's shape; and perhaps cannot make the limbs move naturally.
Pren warde donques se li nous est fres: si li aministre medicines stiptiques, si com aloes, encens, et mirre, et sarcocolle, acaice, et semblans autres, ensi que tu preignes aucune de ces choses, ou toutes ensamble, et les confit avec vin stiptique ou avec abun d’uef ou avec aisil; et les met sus le nout en estoupes, et l’estraint bien, et ne la desliier en mains jors; et puis la desloie, et rencomence une autre, tant que li nodations soit ostee; ou tu estrain sus une piece de plonc bien faite; car li proprietez dou plonc si est qu’il oste toutes les enfleures desus les membres; et se li nodation est ja convertie en durteit ausi com piere, et il est besoing de l’oster, si la cope desus, et fent la superfluiteit apparent; ou tu la reis a aucun raseur, tant qu’ele soit ostee, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Take care, therefore, that we are not ill: if the administrator prescribes medicines that are stinking, such as aloe, incense, myrrh, and sacrum collybum, so that you do not press any of these things, or all together, and mix them with wine that is stinking, or with a lot of egg white, or with oil; and put them on the knot in heaps, and bind it well, and do not loosen it for many days; and then loose it, and start another one, until the knottedness is bone; or you press it onto a piece of cloth that is well made; for the property of the cloth is that it takes away all swelling from the limbs; and if the knottedness has turned into hardness like stone, it must be cut off, if the excess is taken off, and the apparent surplus is removed; or you take it to any barber, until it is bone, and cure it as long as it is healthy.
dou membre qui est foibles aprés la garison	the limb which is weak after confinement
Quant li brisure de l’os est restoree, et demoure aprés li membres foibles et subtilz, si avient por mout de causes: de coi l’une est por ceu qu’il fut liiez trop estroit, et ne fut mie liiez si com il covenoit; ou por ceu qu’il i ot trop de liiens, et ne pooit venir li norrissemens au membre; ou por multitude d’arosement; ou por trop grans movements, ne mie en son houre; ou por ceu qu’il a poc de sanc en son cors, si est foibles.	When the break in the bone has healed, and there remains after weak and delicate members, for several reasons: for one, because he was too tightly bound, and was not bound as it should have been; or because he had too many strings, and could not get the right tension on the member; or because of numerous scrapes; or because of too much movement, not at the right time; or because he has little blood in his body, so he is weak.
Et li cure si est que tu faices mengier le malaide, et faire le cors tendre, tant que li sans soit multipliiez en lui; et li aministre bain, et li done joie et liesce; puis met poix sus le membre, si que li poix atraie a li grant norrissement, et l’arose sovent d’aigue tede, tant que li norrissement corre au membre; et reviegne a sa figure natureil.	And the cure is that you make the patient eat, and make his body soft, until his blood increases in him; and give him baths, and provide pleasure and rest; then put ointment on the member, so that the ointment attracts the great amount of circulation, and dampen it often with warm water, until the circulation corrects the member's shape; and return it to its natural form.
dou membre tort aprés la santeit	the two broken limbs after sickness
Quant li membres est tors aprés la restauration, et li os brisiez apert, et li forme dou membre est laide, toutevoie ne pert mie son ovraige natureil: si ne croire mie les folz qui dient c’on doit brisier lou membre tout de noveil, et maint fol mire ont ce fait en nostre terre; et cist ovraiges est blamez, et en vient grans malz, et par aventure li mors; toutevoie, se li nodations et li torture sont fres, si covient k’il soient arosez d’aigue chaude, ou herbes mollifians soient cuites, si com foilles de vismalve, et racines, et mellilote, et semblans choses; et li fai I emplaustre mollificatif, si com dyaquilon bien fait, et tu pren le muscillaige de vismalve, et la confit avec graisse de geline ou oile de sisament, et fai emplaustre sus; ou tu pren figues graisses, et les broie avec fien de colon, et semblans medicines que amenuisent le soudement.	When the limbs are twisted after restoration, and the broken bone is open, and the form of the limb is ugly, nevertheless it does not lose its natural function: do not believe those fools who say that the member should be broken anew, for many foolish people have done this in our land; but such practices are blamed, and they bring great harm and even death. Nevertheless, if the joints and torments are fresh, it is good that they be soaked in warm water or soft herbs are cooked, as leaves of eels, roots, melilot, and similar things; and the salve made with a gentle balm, such as well-made hydrastis, and you take the musk of eels, and confound it with lard of swans or oil of sesame, and make the plaster; or you take fat figs, and grind them with hay of coles, and similar medicines that soften the torment.
Et aucune fois est ostee li nodacion por froter continuelment et longement a mains moistes.	And never is the bone moved by constant and prolonged rubbing with moist hands.
Et soit amenistrez movement au membre chescune houre.	And keep the limb moving every hour.
Et se li tortuositez est enveillie et endurcie, ausi com piere, et besoins est de l’oster au fer, si la covient coper jusc’a l’os, a l’incisoire subtil legierement; et mettre cusenson et estude en la cure.	And if the limb is twisted and stiffened, as in the case of a stone, then it must be opened with a sharp blade lightly; and put poultice and study in the treatment.
Ci encomence li livres des dislocations	Here begins the book of dislocations:
Dislocations est issue d’aucune jointe de son leu, por coi il ne se puet muevre, et est li membres mal figurez, et sent li malaides grant dolor et grant lesion.	Dislocation occurs when a joint moves out of its place, which prevents it from moving, and the limb is misaligned, causing the patient great pain and injury.
Quant dislocation vient a aucun, si le covient maintenant ramener sens targier.	When dislocation comes to anyone, if it is now brought back by gentle movement.
Car s’on tarde, si enfle li leus, et par aventure si le remet on a poines au leu; por ceu ne covient mie c’on le mueve a l’oure k’il est enflez: maintes fois fait venir spame et autres dolors; toutevoie, quant ce avenra, si fai sainier lou malaide, puis le laisse, tant que li apostemes chas soit apaisiez; puis arose le membre d’aigue chaude et d’oile, puis le ramoinne legierement, et cure chescun membre si com li cure venra en son leu.	For if one delays, and the leaks increase, and by chance he is reset to his place; because then it cannot be moved at all: many times it brings about spasm and other pains; nevertheless, when this will come, if you make the patient well, then let him rest, until the abscesses are quietened; then raise the limb with warm water and oil, then move it lightly, and cure each limb as the pain comes; then treat it.
Et j’ai ordenez les chapistres des dislocations des lou chief jusc’a piez.	And I have ordered the treatments for dislocations of the shoulder joint up to the wrist.
des mandibules	the jaws
Poc avient que les mandibules soient desaluees andous, et li dislocations d’ambedous est selonc II manieres: ou elles sont un poc ostees de lor leus, et mollifies un poc; ou elles sont desaluees entierement, et pendent vers lou pis, et cort li salive de la bouche qu’il ne la puet tenir, ne ne puet clore sa bouche, et envoloupe sa langue avec la parole.	And then the mandibles are dislocated and they are two ways: either they are a little out of place and a little soft; or they are completely dislocated, hanging towards the chest, and the saliva of the mouth goes down, and he cannot keep his mouth closed, and enwraps his tongue with words.
Quant li dislocations est petite, si revient par li em plusors disposicions.	When the dislocation is small, return it to its place with multiple positions.
Et s’elle est entiere et acomplie, si covient que tu la ramoinne hastanment, et ne targier mie; et en tel maniere que li ministres teigne le chief dou malaide, et boute li mires som pochet de l’une de ses mains en la racine de la dislocation de la mandibule dedens la bouche, se li dislocations est de II pars; et li autre doi des mains soient defuer, por mettre igal; et comande au malaide qu’il les amollisse, ses mandibules, et les mueve de toutes pars.	And if it is whole and complete, then you must quickly bring it to the hospital, and do not wait; and in this way that the minister holding the head of the sick person, pours a little medicine from one of his hands at the root of the mandibular dislocation inside the mouth, the dislocation is of two parts; and the other two hands are far away, to make it equal; and order the patient that he softens his mandibles, and moves them in all directions.
Et li mires la mete igal, tant qu’elle reveigne en son leu.	And let the wound be equal, until it returns to its place.
Et se li ramener est griés, meismement se ce sont les II mandibules ensamble, si les arose d’aigue chaude et d’oile, tant que les ramoinnes legierement; ne ne targier mie dou ramener, si com nos avons dit.	And let it be brought back with the greatest care, especially if both jaws are involved, by using hot water and oil, gently at first; do not delay in bringing it back as we have said.
Et quant elles sont ramenees igalment, et li bouche dou malaide clot bien sens mollifiier, si met sus drapelz moilliez en cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire, puis le lie legierement de molz liiens; et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ses chiés soit estans entre II cussins, si qu’il ne lou mueve ne a destre ne a senestre, ne ne s’efforce mie de maixier, mais preigne legiere viande, tant que les dolors soient ostees, et soient noees les mandibules; et puis menjuce ce qu’il vuet legierement, et ne se travaille mie d’ovrir la bouche au mengier et au boivre, tant que li mandibule soit bien noee et sanee.	And when they have been brought back with equal care, and the mouth of the sick person closes easily with a softener, place it on a pad soaked in oil and wax made from olive oil and wax, then leave it there lightly; let the patient sleep on his back, with his head between two pillows, so that he does not move or try to improve his position, but eat a little and drink a little, until the pain is relieved, and the jaw is well set.
Et se les II mandibules ne pueent estre remises a point a une houre, et ne sont mie converties a lor leus, si en vient fievres et sode acostumees, et par aventure solution de ventre, et par aventure vomist cole pure.
