And if the two jaws cannot be reset within an hour and do not return to their places, then fever and usual heat come, and by chance there is a solution of the abdomen, and by chance it vomits pure bile.
Et quant tu verras ceu, adonc saiches que c’est perdicions; et maintes fois muert cil cui il avient, en VIIII jors.	And when you see that, then you know that it is a loss; and many die within nine days.
de la forcelle	of the fork
Li forcele ne puet desaluer dou costeit dedens la continuation de li et dou pis, et est desaluee aucune fois au defuer, et bien le sent on.	of the jaw does not dislocate from within its extension on the side of the face and is dislocated only once to the outside, and it can be felt well.
Et li restauration si est que li malaides gise sovin sor son dos, et estende ses bras; et puis presse le leu forment a ta palme, et elle revenra; puis met sus l’emplaustre et lou bendeil, et l’estraint; et li chiez qui est devers lou coute ne puet desaluer; se poc non, et se il desalue aucune fois, si le ramoinne a son leu, si com nos avons dit; puis met sus l’emplaustre et le bendeil, et l’estraint, et coumande au malaide qu’il se repose tant qu’il soit sanez; et ensi meisme est ramenez li chiés de l’espale, quant il est desevrez de son leu.	And the restoration is that the patient lies down on his back and extends his arms; and then press on the form with your palm, and it will return; then put the plaster and bandage on, and hold it in place; and the jaw that is next to the face cannot be dislocated; if not, and if it is dislocated once, let it return to its place as we have said; then put the plaster and bandage on, and hold it in place, and order the patient to rest until he is well; and thus also is the shoulder joint returned when it is dislocated from its place.
de la dislocation de l’espaule	of the shoulder dislocation
Saiches que li espaule n’est desaluee fuer que selonc III manieres: de coi l’une est qu’ele desalue a la partie de l’assele au desoz; et li seconde est a la partie dou pis; et par aventure desalue a la partie desus, et ceu avient poc; et ne desalue mie derrier por l’espaule, et ne desalue mie dedens por les ners; et plusors fois desalue desoz vers l’assele, meismement a ces qui ont poc de char, car a ces saut ele fuer hastanment; a ces qui ont assez char, saut ele a poines, et rentre a poines.	I understand that the shoulder dislocates only in three ways: either it comes out at the edge of the shoulder blade; or at the top of the arm pit; perhaps it comes out at the back of the shoulder, and this is hard to treat; it also comes out towards the bottom of the armpit, although this is harder to notice, and there are often no signs that something is wrong. For those who have a lot of pain in their shoulders, they should go to hospital; for those with moderate pain, treatment is not necessary, and they will feel better on their own.
Et par aventure avient a aucuns homes percussion ou casseure, et enfle li espaule d’un aposteme chaut, et cuide qu’elle est desaluee par ceu.	Sometimes, after a fall or blow to the shoulder, the shoulder joint becomes stiff and painful; it is then that the dislocation becomes apparent.
Il covient donques que tu l’esprueves, tant que tu en soies certains; et adonques encomence la cure.	It is therefore necessary for you to test this, as long as you are certain of it; and then start the treatment.
Et est conue li dislocations quant il est aval vers l’assele, et met difference entre l’espaule malade et la saine, et tu troveras entre lor diversiteit manifeste; et troveras au chief de l’espaule une fosse, et desoz l’assele au tochier le chief de l’espaule, ausi com se ce soit uns oes; et ne puet li malaides ramener sa main a son neis, ne movoir de nulz movemens; et ausi, s’elle est desaluee en haut, si n’est mie occultee, car tu le trueves manifestement au tochier; et ceste maniere de dislocation n’est mie fors a ramener, quant elle est novele, ou se li enfes est malaides.	Et est conue li dislocations quan il est aval vers l'assele, et met difference entre l'espaule malade et la saine, et tu troveras entre lor diversiteit manifeste; et troveras au chief de l'espaule une fosse, et desoz l'assele au tochier le chief de l'espaule, ausi com se ce soit uns oes; et ne puet li malaides ramener sa main a son neis, ne movoir de nulz movemens; et ausi, s'elle est desaleeee en haut, si n'est mie occultee, car tu le trueves manifestement au tochier; et ceste maniere de dislocation n'est mie fors a ramener, quan elle est novele, ou se li enfes est malaides.
Et li maniere est que li ministres lieve la main dou malaide en haut, puis met tes peuchas desoz l’assele, et lieve la jointure a force en haut au leu; et li ministres lieve la main, et l’estende en haut, pues le mette desoz; si venra hastanment.	And the method is that the minister will place the sick hand up high, then put on the splint, and force the joint back into place high up; and the minister will place the hand, and extend it high up, so that it comes out; then come to the hospital quickly.
Et s’elle ne vient si com nos avons dit em mains jors aprés, si covient ke li malaides soit baigniez en aigue chaude; et li amenistre arosement mollifiant et assouajant, si com decoction de altee et de fenugrec et de mellilote en aigue, et soit amenistree; puis soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos, et mette on desoz l’assele un sto de lainne igal, ne trop mol ne trop dur, puis mette li mires son talon sus le sto, et lieve le chief de l’espaule vertuousement, et traie la main dou malaide; et uns autres ministres teigne lou chief dou malaide, si qu’il ne se mueve aval; celle espaule revient tout maintenant, et se tu vues si le ramoinne selonc ceste maniere: et est que tu faices estre present I home qui soit plus grans que li malaides; et soit drois devers lou costeit, et boute s’espaule desoz l’assele dou malaide, et lieve l’assele en haut, si que li malaides pende en l’ar; et uns autres ministres traie la main dou malaide aval devers lou ventre.	And if it does not come as we have said before, in a few days, it is necessary that the patient be bathed in warm water; and soft and soothing infusions are prepared, as an infusion of wormwood and fenugrec and melilot in water, and they are given to him; then the patient is placed on his back, and the shoulder is dislocated a little with a smooth lever, not too soft nor too hard, then the doctor strikes the patient's heel against the lever, and gently raises the shoulder, and the doctor's hand pulls down the patient's arm; and other ministers dye the patient's shoulder, so that it does not move; this shoulder returns immediately, and if you do this according to this method: it is necessary that a man be present who is greater than the patient; and he is positioned on his left side, and the doctor raises the shoulder with a lever that is dislocated from the chair of the patient, and lifts the lever so that the patient hangs in the air; and other ministers pull the patient's hand down towards his belly.
Et se li malaides est trop legiers, si pent avec lui aucune chose pesant, et li dislocation revient maintenant.	And if the patient is too weak, then without anything heavy with him, the dislocation comes back now.
Et le ramoinne on ausi en autre maniere: et est c’on fiche I lonc tison en terre, dont li chiés soit ausi reons com I pistal, et ne soit ne trop gros ne trop graile; puis soit mis desoz lou malaide, mais k’il ait drapelz souef sus, et li malaides soit estans dou lonc dou fust; puis soit estendue sa main aval d’autre part forment, et li jointure revenra en son leu hastanment; et s’elle ne vuet revenir por toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si fai ceste cure: pren I tison de II bras de grant et IIII dois de large, qui ait le chief reont por mues entrer em parfont desoz l’assele, selonc ceste forme:	And if he is very weak, then without anything heavy with him, the dislocation comes back now. And this is how it is done: and if a long stake is driven into the earth, whose tip is also like a pistol, and not too thick or too thin; then let the dislocated person lie on his back with his feet together, but so that he has a drape underneath him, and his hand is extended upwards from the other side, making a joint, and the joint will return to its place securely; and if it does not come back because of all these things that we have said, then do this cure: take a stake of the two arms long and three hands wide, which has the tip pointed so that it can enter perfectly under the axletree, according to this shape:
puis lie sus le chief dou fust drapelz souez, que li fust ne blece lou malaide, puis le met desoz l’assele dou malaide; et estende som bras sus le fust dou lonc, et lie l’ajutoire sus le fust, et lou bras au chief de la main, puis met le bras sus I eschillon d’une eschiele dou large, et soit estendue li mains aval, et soit laissiez li cors pendans d’autre part: li jointure reva ens maintenant.	Then let him lie on the long table, that he might not be hurt by the fire, then place him on the table's shoulder; and extend his arms over the table, and place the shoulder under his armpit, then put his arm on a block of wood in front of him, and let his hands hang down, and let his body swing freely: the joint has now been set.
Et quant elle est ens, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient que tu mettes desoz l’assele une spere de laine igal, puis met l’emplaustre aparilliet de poudre dou molin, avec encens et aubun d’uef, sus toute l’espaule et entor, puis l’estrain desoz l’assele avenanment, et torne le liien sus l’emplaustre, et embraice la main a son col, et soit li mains demorans ensi.	And when it is set, in whatever way, place under the shoulder a bunch of equal wool, then put on the plaster with powder from the mill, with incense and myrrh, all over the shoulder and around, then pull the shoulder forward, and tie it to the plaster, and embrace the hand at the neck, and let the hands remain thus.
Et covient qu’il menjuce poc, tant que li membres soit confortez, car il sanera plus tost; et puis menjuce plus aprés V jors ou VII, et le mueve; et s’il est fermeis et il n’est mollifiez, si est sanez.	And it is necessary that he suck a little, as long as the limbs are comfortable, because he will heal faster; and then suck more after 5 or 7 days, and move them; and if they are firm and have not become softened, then they are healed.
Et se li jointure est fuer de leu por moistor que i est venue, ou por autre cause, si covient que tu i aministres cauteres a III pertus, si com il est mis devant ou chapistre des cauteres.	And if the joint has come out of its place due to moisture or some other cause, you must apply the fire cauterization to three parts, as it is done with the章 章 章 章 章 章
Et se tu fais tout ceu, et il deslie aprés VII jors, et li jointure ne se tient, et ne puet lever som bras amont, adonc saiches que li nerf au chief de l’espaule sont copeit ou estendut ou amollis; et saiches que li jointure n’iert jamais fichie en son leu.	And if you do all this, and it slides after 7 days, and the joint does not stay in place, and he cannot raise his arm above, then know that the nerve at the head of the shoulder is torn or stretched or softened; and know that the joint has never returned to its place.
Li dislocation qui est devers lou pis, et les mameles, ou derrier, si est faite par impulsion, et estendement de mains, et i aministre on autre lieure; et cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	The dislocation that is toward the loins and breasts, or behind, is made by an impulse and extension of the hands, and another place is administered; and he is cured as long as he is healed.
Et se aprés la sanation vient grietez au membre, et tardemens em movement, si use li malaides bain maintes fois, tant que celle grietez soit alegie, et reviegne a sa premiere nature.	And if after healing the member comes to be gray, and slowly moving, so use the patient many times, until that greyness is healed, and returns to its first nature.
de la dislocation dou coute	of the dislocation of the neck
Saiches que li jointure dou coute est desaluee a poinnes, et a poinnes revient; et s’est desaluee de toutes pars, et meismement devant et derrier, et li dislocations n’est mie reponue, car on la voit bien et sent bien; et desalue selonc chescune figure.	I know that the joint of the neck is dislocated to the ends, and returns to the ends; and if it is dislocated from all sides, most especially in front and behind, and the dislocation is not returned, for we can see and feel it well; and dislocate according to each figure.
Et quant tu joins le coute malaide avec lou sain, si le pues veoir apertement.	And when you join the sick neck with the sound one, if you can see it open.
Car li jointure est chevee, et ne puet ploier lou bras, ne touchier son espaule a tout.	For the joint is chopped off, and cannot bend the arm, nor touch its shoulder at all.
Et covient que tu le ramoinnes ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne, car se apostemes chaus i venoit, si seroit grief li ramener; et par aventure ne puet estre ramenez dou tout en tout, meismement quant ele est au derrier; si vaut pis que les autres dislocations, et est de plus grant dolor, et par aventure i vient li mors.	And it is necessary that you reset it in the same way as the abscesses come out, for if the abscesses come out, if it were to be set back, it would be grief; and perhaps can not be reset from all sides, most especially when it is behind; so much less than the other dislocations, and it is of great pain, and by chance comes death.
Et li restauration si est, quant elle est telz c’on la puet ramener, que tu li estendes sa main a tes II mains; et ses bras soit espandus, et les mains dou mire selonc le coute entor, desor et desoz, et boute la jointure a ses peuchas ensamble, ou a la racine de sa palme, tant qu’ele reviegne a son leu.	And the restoration is so, when it is such that you can bring it back, that you extend its hand to your two hands; and its arms are spread out, and the hands are in contact with the wrist according to the cuff, from behind and from the front, and push the joint into the palm roots together, or at the root of the palm, until it returns to its place.
Et se li dislocations est au devant, si revient quant il double sa main a sa main, et fier de la racine de la palme lou coute qui est desaluez.	And if dislocation is in front, so return when it doubles its hand to its hand, and firm at the root of the palm the cuff that has come off.
Et s’il ne vuet revenir au leu, si aministre fort extension; et est que dui ministre estendent le bras, et le teignent dui ministre, si qu’il ne se mueve a l’estension; puis torne le bras de chescune part, puis que tu as envoloupeit un drapeil double lonc et large; et quant li mires a jointe la jointure a sa main, si l’oigne d’aucun oile por amolir la jointure, puis boute la jointure forment, tant qu’ele reviegne; et quant elle est au leu, si met sus emplaustre sec avec aubun d’uef, et l’estrain forment, et pent le bras au col dou malaide, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le deslie.	And if it does not return to its place, so administer a strong extension; and it is that the two ministers extend the arm, and tint them together, so that it does not move at the extension; then turn the arm of each part, then that you have wrapped a double long and wide cloth; and when you see joined the joint to the hand, if you oil it with any oil to soften the joint, then press the joint together, until it returns; and when it is in place, put it on plaster dry with auburn of egg, and strain it together, and tie the arm to the neck of the patient, and leave it for some days, and then unbind it.
Et se li jointure est ferme en son leu, si deslie lou liien, et le laisse; et se tu vois que li jointure n’estrigne bien, si rencomence l’emplaustre et lou lien, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit fermement mis; puis le deslie.	And if the joint is firm in its place, then let it be; and if you see that the joint is not well set, then begin to plaster and bind it, and leave it thus for some days, until it is firmly set; then remove it.
Et se il sent grieteit aprés le ramenement de la jointe, et elle se muet, si le baigne et frote bellement, et presse tant qu’il soit assouagiez; ou tu met sus la jointure une naige de mouton grasse, puis la laisse I jor et une nuit, puis l’oste, et lou fai entrer ou bain; et quant il sue, se li frote la jointure tempreement, puis remet la naige sus, et puis entre ou bain; et ensi fai II fois ou III, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues, si met sus fien de vaiche moiste chaufeit avec burre, et l’estrain sus; si revenra a sa disposition.	And if he feels pain after the re-alignment of the joint, and it moves, then let him bathe and gently rub, and press until it is relieved; or you put on the joint a layer of fat sheepskin, then leave it for a day and a night, then remove it, and let him enter or bathe; and when he sweats, let him gently rub the joint, then put the skin back on, and then enter or bathe; and do this II times or III, until he is well; and if you see it, then put on the joint a layer of hot fat with butter, and apply it; so it will return to its position.
li dislocation de la main	the dislocation of the hand
Li jointure de la main desalue, et li revenue est legiere, plus que les autres jointures Toutevoie, il la covient ramener au leu hastanment, en l’oure meisme qu’ele est desaluee, ainsois que li leus soit enflez, ou qu’il i viegne aposteme chaut.	the dislocation of the hand should be restored quickly, more so than with other joints However, it is necessary to restore it to its place gently in the middle of the dislocation, so that the joint is swollen or there is heat.
Et li ramenemens si est que tu mettes la main malaide sus une tauble, et estende li ministres la main, et li mires la mette igal, ensi que il mette sa paume sus l’aparance de la jointure, et la boute tant qu’elle reviegne Toutevoie, il covient que vos regardez s’il est bien a leu; adonc mette li malaides lou dos de sa main sus une tauble a l’estension et au ramenement.	And when you restore it, so that the sick hand is placed on a table, and extends its members, and makes it equal, so that its palm is placed on the joint face, and puts it back until it comes back However, it is necessary to check whether it is in place; then put the patient's back of the hand on a table for extension and reduction.
Et se li dislocations est au dos de la main, si mette li malaides son dos de sa main sus la tauble, et li mires mette sa main sus cele apparance de la jointure.	If the dislocation is at the back of the hand, then put the patient' s back of the hand on a table, and make it equal to the face of the joint.
S’elle revient maintenant, c’est bien Se ce non, si l’estrain d’emplaustres apaisans apostemes chaus, et lou laisse ensi sens rencomencier.	If it returns now, that is good; but if it does not, and the extraction of the spittle-like abscesses calms her, then let it be left as it is.
Et s’il ne le puet soffrir, et tu ne la pues mettre au leu aprés aucuns jors, si demore li jointure torte; et ne nuist niant au malaide fuer que tant que li mains est amoillie, et ne puet estraindre aucune chose a tout: adonc saiches que li nerf sont copez, ou li artere; si n’i a autre engien fuer que d’estraindre par cautere delez le cas, et par aventure n’i vaut autre chose.	If he cannot bear it, and you cannot put it back in place after a few days, then let the joint twist; and do not use any force on the patient except to extract anything by fire: therefore know that the nerves are cut, or the arteries; otherwise, except for extracting by fire, there is nothing else.
Et quant li mains est au leu, si met sus l’emplaustre que nos avons dit, puis l’estrain et le laisse V jors, puis le deslie et laisse ensi.	When the hand is in place, put it on the spittle-like abscess that we have mentioned; then extract it and leave it for 5 days, then remove it again and leave it alone.
Et s’il ne la puet bien movoir, et il i a aucune grieteit, si la moille d’aigue chaude, et le frote tant qu’il soit sanez.	If he cannot move it well, and there is no fracture, if the moist heat of water is applied, and it is rubbed until it is healed.
de la dislocation des dois de la main	of the dislocation of the two fingers of the hand
Aucune fois sont desaluez li doi de la main a chescune part, aucune fois au dos de la palme ou au ventre; adonques estent le doi, et boute la dislocation a tes pouchés tant qu’il reviegne, puis sostien lou chief dou doi, et le pent vers la partie ou il est desjoins; et le laisse II jors, et puis le met igal celui jor; et de nut le lie, si com nos avons dit, et lou deslie de jor, et lou fai movoir, et le relie la nut; et fai ce sovent, tant qu’il soit estroit, et tout ausi fai, se il est desaluez au ventre de la main, et fai si com tu as fait ci devant, tant qu’il soit sanez; et tout ausi fai, quant il est desaluez d’autre part.	De the dislocation of the two fingers of the hand: Never is one finger dislocated from one side to the other on the back of the palm or the abdomen; then are they joined again, and push down the joint of the two fingers as far as it comes back up, and then hold down the head of the two fingers, and turn it towards the part where it is joined; and leave it there for a day, and then put it right that day; and let it rest, so that the finger does not move, and do this often, as long as it is tight, and do the same if it is dislocated from the bottom of the hand, and do this as you have just done, as long as it is healthy; and do the same, if it is dislocated from another side.
dou desaluement de l’eschinee dou dos	of the dislocation at the back of the neck
Quant l’eschinee dou dos ou dou col est desaluee, ou il en i a plusors desaluees, si n’i a point de cure, car li mors haste le malaide.	When the shoulder is dislocated, or several are dislocated, there is no cure, because death quickly comes to the patient.
Et li signes si est que li egestions saut fuer sens volunteit, ne ne la puet tenir, et maintes fois sont mollifiez aucun membre, ou les II cuixes ou li dui bras ou I Et maintes fois se muet li eschinee a IIII pars; celle qui se muet au derrier si est apelee «gilbositez»: li cure si est que tu rewarde se li gilbositez est venue d’enfance: si n’i ait point de cure ne de sanation dou tot.	And the signs are that the excision has been done without willingness, it cannot be held, and many times a limb is weakened, or the II legs or the II arms or I And many times the shoulder moves in IV directions; this which moves at the rear is called "gilbositez": the cure is that you reward if the gilbositez comes from childhood: if there is no cure nor healing of all.
Et celle que vient de cheoir ou de percussions ou de semblans choses, dirent li ancien manieres de cures par grans paroles, ou il n’a mie en toutes grant profit; mais je l’ai abregiet selonc mon entention, et ai formez estrumens en diverses manieres.	And that which comes from sitting or striking or similar things, the ancient manners of cures said by great words, but there was no great benefit in them; but I have simplified it according to my intention, and have formed instruments in various ways.
Je dis que en la gilbositeit que vient au pis devant, nen a engien ne santeit; et ausi cele que vient droitement en II costez, et ne puet on curer fuers que celi proprement qui vient au dos, si com je dis; et est que li malaides soit estendus sus sa faice en I leu igal, et ait de l’estrain desoz lui, qu’il ne se blece; puis fiche I tison au chief en terre forment, et I autre as piez, et lie un liien pardesoz les asseles dou malaide, et I autre as hainches, et as genous, et as chevilles; et dui ministre saichent les liiens, li uns au chief et li autres as piez, parmi les II tisons; et soient bien fermez, li tison si com nos avons dit, et li mires mette ses paumes sus l’espinee forment, tant qu’ele reviegne.	I say that in the swelling that comes to the foot before, there is no remedy nor cure except what comes from behind; and also that which comes straight on both sides, and cannot be cured but only that which comes from behind properly, as I said; and it is that the sick person should be stretched out on his face in an even place, and have someone strain on him so he does not burn himself, then put a stick to the head in the ground shaped, and another at the feet, and tie a ribbon around the legs of the sick person, and another at the ankles, and two ministers know the ribbons, one at the head and the other at the feet, between the two sticks; and let them be well fastened, the stick as we have said, and the minister put his palms on the spine shaped, until he revives.
Et s’elle ne revient par ceste cure, si pren une tauble de III bras de lonc, et chevé desoz la paroit, et li malaides soit en costé, et boute le chief de la tauble desoz la paroit, puis met le mileu de la tauble sus l’espinee; et mette li mires ses piez sus l’autre chief de la tauble, et presse bien, tant qu’il reviegne au leu; et se tu vues, si le fai au tornet qui torne a la main.	And if she does not come back by this cure, then take a barrel of three arms long, and shave off the wall, and let the sick person be on one side, and pour the head of the barrel from the wall, then put the middle of the barrel on the spine; and put the minister's hands on the other head of the barrel, and press well, until he revives in place; and if you see this, do it to the tourniquet that turns with the hand.
Et est que tu fiches II tisons au chief dou malaide d’un bras de grant, et devers les piez II autres, et ait entre chescun tison, desoure et desoz, une paume d’espaice de lonc; et ait en chescun tison I pertus, ou li tornet corre, et soient li tison fermement en terre, si qu’il ne se muevent; et entre chescuns II tisons ait I tison tornant, sor coi li liien tornent, et ait en II tornans II petis tisons d’une paume de lonc, por torner le tornet; et puis lie lou lien qui est parmi les asseles au tornet devers le chief, et l’autre liien devers les piez a l’autre tornet, et chescuns des ministres torne son tornet a tout le liien, et li maistres mette l’espinee igal si com nos avons dit.	And is that you stick II torches to the head of the sick person with an arm long, and across the other hair, and between each torch, up and down, a palm's space long; and in each torch has I pit, where the turn goes, and let the torch firmly into the ground, so that it does not move; and between each pair of torches has one torch turning, for the sake of the bond which is among the Torches to the head, and the other chain across the hair at the other turn, and each helper turns its turn on all the chain, and the master puts the spine even as we have said.
Et quant elle est igalz, si met sus emplaustre desiccatif avec abun d’uef, et puis les estoupes, et puis l’estele d’une tablete de III dois de lonc, que porpreigne lou leu de la gilbositeit et la partie de l’espondile sainne, puis le lie d’un liien, si com nos avons dit, et use li malaides de norrissement subtil, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’aucune chose vient en la fin de la santez, si covient aministrer medicines amollissans et asouajans, avec l’estele que nos avons dit ci devant; et aucune fois i aministre on une piece de plonc, et aucune fois vient li apparance en la derriere spondile dou dos, et cuide on que ce soit dislocations; et c’est li os qui apert, por coi on n’i doit mie avoir presumption: par aventure feroit venir la mort.	And when it is even, so put it on plaster drying with abundance of wool, and then the stakes, and then the piece of a tablet of III legs long, that forpurify the place of the gibbosity and the part of the spine healthy, then the thread of a chain, as we have said, and use the patient of subtle fastening, until he is healthy; and if anything comes at the end of the health, so administer soft medicines and soothing, with the piece that we have said before; and never does one administer a piece of lead, and never comes the appearance in the posterior spine of the back, and take care that it is dislocations; and this bone opens, for they say that one should not have presumption: perhaps death would come.
des dislocations de la hainche	of dislocations of the hip
Saiches que as jointures de la hainche et as jointures de l’espaule ne vient fuers que dislocacions soulement, ne n’i vient mie si com as autres jointures; et li jointure de la hainche est desaluee selonc IIII parties: dedens et defuer ,et devant et derrier; et plus dedens c’aillors, et poc desalue devant et derrier.	I understand that hip and shoulder dislocations occur only due to dislocation, not as with other joints; and the hip joint is dislocated according to IV parts: inside and outside, front and back; and more inside, and less front and back.
Et li conoissance de sa dislocations dedens si est que quant on joint la jambe malaide avec la sainne, si est plus longe, et apert plus li malaides genous que li sains, et ne puet li malaides doubler son genoil au feu; et est li leus qui est delez enflez d’aposteme chaut, por ceu que li chiés de la cuixe vient lai.	And the knowledge of their dislocations inside is that when one joins the leg with the sick, it is further away, and more than the leg of the healthy person, so that the patient cannot double his knee; and this is the location which is swollen and heated by an abscess, because the hip joint comes out.
Et li signe de celui cui il vient au defuer, si est que cist accident sont contraire a ces devant.	And the sign of that for whom it comes from behind, is that this accident is opposite to these in front.
Et li signes de celui cui avient au devant, si est qu’il estent bien sa jambe selonc l’acomplissement; toutevoie, ne double mie le genoil sens dolor, et s’on le vuet faire aler, si ne puet avant, et retient son urine, et enfle li angre, et quant il vait, si passe sus le talon.	And the signs of that for whom it comes from the front are that his leg is well arranged according to the accomplishment; however, he does not double his knee with pain, and if one makes him walk, he cannot go forward, and he holds his urine back, and his ankle swells, and when he walks, he goes on the heel.
Et li signes de celui cui il avient derrier, si est qu’il ne puet espandre son genoil, ne doubler, et est celle jambe plus torte de l’autre, et li angre est mollifié, et est li chiés de la cuixe au leu desoz les costes.	And the signs of that person who has behind him, if he cannot spread his knee, nor double it, and that leg is more twisted than the other, and the hip joint is relaxed, and the pelvis is in place at the sides of the ribs.
Li ramenemens de ceste semblance de dislocation si est que tu rewarde se li dislocations est anciainne, et elle demore selonc sa disposition, si n’i a nule cure; et n’i covient mie qu’il ait presumption.	And those who have this appearance of dislocation should be treated if the dislocation is old and it delays according to its condition, there is no cure; and it is not appropriate that he has pride.
Et en celi dont li dislocation est fresche, et c’est des IIII manieres de dislocation, si te haste que tu tornes la jointe, et l’esten dedens et defuer, et la muef a destre et senestre; par aventure si revenra, et n’a mestier d’autre cure.	And in those who have this fresh dislocation, and there are the four ways of dislocation, if you hurry to reset the joint, and push it inward and outward, and move it from right to left; perhaps it will come back, and there is no need for any other treatment.
Et s’il ne revient en ceste maniere, si covient que tu apareilles I ministre fort, et esten la jambe fort a II mains, ou a I liien que soit liiez sus lou genoil; et uns autres ministres estende sa main desus en teil maniere qu’il boute ses mains desoz ses asseles, puis l’estrigne d’un souef liien sus la cuixe; et uns autres tigne lou chief dou liien; et estendent amont et aval tuit a une fois, tant que li malaide soit levez de terre a une fois, et demoure pendans.	And if it does not come back in this way, it is appropriate that you prepare a strong minister, and hold the leg very firm with two hands, or tie it to a staff so that it cannot move; and other ministers extend their hand above and below at the same time, until the patient is raised from the ground once, and remains stationary.
Ceste maniere d’estension si est commune as IIII semblances, et se li dislocation est revenue, si com nos avons dit, c’est bien.	This way of extension is so common in four appearances, and if the dislocation has returned, as we have said, it is good.
Se ceu non, si covient mettre cure a sa semblance Quant li dislocations est au pardedens, si covient que tu sovines le malaide sus son costeit sain, puis met le liien sus la racine de la cuixe, et le leu qui est desoz l’angre, puis estent le liien en haut devers l’angre, et devers la forcele; puis preigne uns autres ministres ses bras, et embraice le gros leu de la cuixe malaide, et l’estende au defuer forment: si revenra a son leu maintenant; et ceste maniere de dislocation est plus legiere des autres.	If not, then you must put the cure on his back correctly as we have said, then tie up the person's legs together, and then tie up the root of the thigh, and then the bandage goes up towards the hip, and then up towards the shoulder; then, grab another assistant to support their arms, and embrace the large band around the hurt hip, and stretch it out to the side: now, it will come back to its place at that time; and this way of dislocation is lighter than the others.
Et se tu ne la pues serrer en ceste maniere que nos avons dit, si covient que tu lies les II piés dou malaide ensamble d’un fort liien souef sus les II talons, et sus les II genous, et soit li jambe malaide estendue II dois plus que li autres; puis soit pendus sus le chief d’un fust, et soit en sus de terre II bras de lonc; puis comande a I ministre qu’il embraice le chief de la cuixe, et soit uns autres ministres pendans avec le malaide, qui embraice forment la cuixe, car li jointure revient maintenant hastanment.	And if you cannot hold it in this way that we have said, then you must tie the two legs of the person together with a strong bandage around their heels and knees, and make sure the hurt leg is stretched out more than the other; then, hang them from a beam by their ankles, and with long arms; and tell the assistant to embrace the root of the thigh, and let there be other assistants hanging the person up, who will hold onto the hip correctly, for the joint will come back now quite easily.
Et quant li dislocations est au defuer, si gise li malaides, si com nos avons dit en celui qui a gilbositeit, et estraigne I liien sus la jambe malaide proprement, et sus le peis ausi; puis met II tisons, I au chief et I autre as piez, puis fiche I tison entre les cuixes au malaide emmi la forme; et ait plantei de drapelz moistes entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide, puis estende chescuns ministre devers lui, et li mires mette igal a sa main la dislocation.	And when the dislocations are at a distance, if the patient lies down, as we have said in that which concerns gilhousie, and extrude the tie on the ill-limbed properly, and also on the breast; then place two torches, one on the head and another on the foot, then lay one torch between the thighs of the ill person against the form; and plant a flag of moisture around, that it may not hurt the patient, then extend each minister towards him, and let him put the dislocation equal to his hand.
S’elle revient, c’est boin.	If it comes back, it is good.
Se ce non, met sus .ie. table, et le presse ensi com nos avons dit en la gilbositeit, et gise li malaides sus le sain costeit.	If not, put him on a table, and press him in the manner which we have spoken of in gilhousie, and lay the patient on his sound side.
Et quant li dislocations est devant, si covient estendre la jambe malaide hastanment, et selonc ce que j’ai dit; et mette li mires sa paine d’estre sus l’angre malaide, puis presse a l’autre main, et l’estent aval devers lou genoil.	And when the dislocations are in front, if it is necessary to extend the ill leg suddenly, and according to what I have said; and let the minister hold his pain on the ill foot, then press with the other hand, and extend it downwards towards the knee.
Et se li dislocations est au defuer, si ne covient pas estendre le malaide aval, ne lever sus la terre, ains covient qu’il soit ausi com se li hainche estoit desaluee au defuer, si com nos avons dit dou couchement sus les II hainches; et soit sus sa faice, et li lien estendut si com nos avons dit ci devant, et doit om presser sus la jointure a la table; et sera a point quant li malaides estendra ses jambes, et elles seront igalz; adonques ajoste les cuixes, et met l’emplaustre, et l’estrain d’un bendeil, si que li hainche ne se mueve; et se repose III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie, et met l’emplaustre sus; et se tu vois qu’elles soient igalz, si l’estrain, si com devant, et le laisse III jors; puis le deslie, et lou fai aler belement, tant que li membres soit confortez.	Et s'il est délocalisé au-delà, il ne convient pas de l'étirer vers l'avant, de le lever sur la terre, mais qu'il soit plutôt étendu comme s'il était dans une position assise, ainsi qu'il a été dit pour le coucher sur les deux hanches; et qu'il soit sous sa face, et que la main soit étendue comme il a été dit ci-dessus, et qu'elle soit pressée sur l'articulation de la table; et elle sera bien lorsque le patient étendra ses jambes, et elles seront longues; alors mets l'ampoule, et tire d'un bandage, afin que la hanche ne bouge pas; et qu'il repose trois ou quatre jours, puis le changez, et mettez l'ampoule dessus; et si vous voyez qu'elles sont longues, alors tirez-les, comme il a été dit ci-dessus, et laissez-les trois jours; puis changez-les, et qu'il fasse du bruit avec ses membres jusqu'à ce qu'ils soient confortés.
de la dislocation dou genoil	of the dislocation of the hip
Li genous est desaluez selonc III manieres: c’est a savoir, dedens et defuer, et derrier; et ne desalue point devant.	The hip can dislocate in three ways: namely, inward, outward, and backward; but not forward.
Et li signes si est que tu comande au malaide qu’il plie sa jambe a sa cuixe, et s’ele ne s’aert a sa cuixe, saiches qu’il est desaluez; et li restauration de toutes si est que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et estende sa jambe s’il puet, et li met ton dos sus sa faice, et met son piet sus tes piez; puis pren son genoil a tes paumes, et retrai entre tes dois, puis plie les II costez dou genoil forment; et uns autres ministres estende son piet, tant que li genous reviegne a son leu, et li signes est qu’il aert bien sa jambe a sa cuixe legierement; et met l’emplastre sus, et fai aerdre la jambe a la cuixe, et les loie ensamble fort III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie; et ne se travaille mie li malaides d’aler, tant que li membres soit confortez.	And the signs are that you command the patient to bend his knee to his chest, and if it does not go to his chest, then know that it is dislocated; and the restoration of all this is that you cause the patient to sit upright, and extend his leg if he can, and place his back on his face, and put his foot on your feet; then take his kneecap in your palms, and pull apart between your two hands, then bend the two ribs of the knee cap together; and others make his foot go into the chest lightly; and apply the plaster, and make him raise his leg to the chest, and hold it firmly together for three or four days, then loosen it. And do not worry about making the patient walk until his limbs are comfortable.
Et se li membres n’est a point, si aministre estendement fort, si com nos avons dit en la cure de la hainche, tant qu’il soit sanez	And if the limbs are not in place, then give strong extension, as we have said in the treatment of the hip, until they are well.
de la dislocation dou talon	of the dislocation of the heel
Li talons est aucune fois esmeus, et aucune fois desaluez plenement, et dedens et defuer.	The heels are never dislocated, and never completely dislocated from each other, and inwards and outwards.
Et li signes si est que li cheville est enflee, et tent avant a la partie ou elle est desaluee: li ramenemens si est legier, et le doit on estendre legierement a ses mains quant il est esmeus soulement.	And the signs are that the ankle is dislocated, and the movement before the part where it is dislocated: the removers are slight, and one must slightly extend it with his hands when it is only slightly dislocated.
Et quant il est desaluez dou tot, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et le tigne I ministres fors par la jambe, desus la cheville; puis trai le piet a toi a ta main destre, et puis a la senestre II fois, puis l’estent en haut, et boute bellement lou piet en haut; et fai ce II fois, si com nos avons dit, em boutant et en traiant lou piet; s’elle revient, c’est bien; se ce non, si rencomence l’ovraige, car il revient; et s’il ne puet revenir ensi, si fai gesir lou malaide sor son dos sus terre, et fiche I passeil fermement en terre entre ses cuixes, et lie drapelz entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide; puis teigne li ministres la cuixe, et uns autres ministres estende lou piet a ses mains ou a I liien, k’il lie sus le col dou piet; puis estende chescuns ministres igalment, et li passelz soit adés entre les cuixes dou malaide por retenir le malaide quant on l’estent; puis mette li mires igal la dislocation a ses mains, et uns autres ministres teigne la jambe sainne au desoz, et li dislocation revenra hastanment.	And when it is dislocated all at once, so that you place the patient upright, and bend it away by the leg, over the ankle; then bring the foot to you with your right hand, and then again with your left twice, then extend it upwards, and tap it gently upwards; and do this twice, as we have said, by tapping and bringing the foot; if it returns, it is good; but if not, begin the process again, for it will return; and if it does not return thus, so that you make the patient walk on his back on the ground, and place the staff firmly in the ground between his hips, and tie the sheets around him, so that he does not slip; then bend the leg at the knee, and extends it with your hands or with the crutches, that he lie on the staff; then make each minister extend equally, and the staff be close to the hip of the patient for support when you extend him; then place the mires equally at the dislocation in your hands, and other ministers bend the healthy leg away, and the dislocation will return completely.
Et quant elle iert a point, si met l’emplastre et estoupes sus, et l’estrain forment, et lie lou piet a la jambe, et warde les ners qui sont sus la cheville derrier, que li liiens ne soit trop estrois; puis le laisse II jors ou III, et se li liiens amolist, si l’estrain; puis le deslie au tier jor ou au quart, et deffent a aler lou malaide par IIII jors; et s’il va devant cel termine, ce n’est mie seurtez qu’il ne desalue encor.	And when it is set in place, put on the plaster and press it down, and shape it, and fasten the foot to the leg, and hold back the tendons that are behind the ankle, so that the ties are not too tight; then leave it for II days or III, and let the ties become soft, if the splint; then take off the splint on the third day or fourth, and let the patient walk after III days. And if he goes forward this term, there is no sure thing than that he still dislocates.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si covient que tu l’apaises, si com nos avons dit autre part, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the abscesses come out, so that you calm them down, as we have said elsewhere, until they are healthy.
des dois	of two
Quant li doi sont desaluez, si les covient bellement estendre sens travail, et c’est legiere chose.	When the two are dislocated, so that you stretch them smoothly without work, and this is a light thing.
Et se li dislocations est en aucun nout dou dos dou piet, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide sus I leu plain ou sus .ie. table tot droit, et met ton piet sus ce qui apert de ces jointures, puis presse a ton piet forment, tant qu’il reviegne; et quant il est igalz, et il n’i apert nient, si met desoz la plante dou piet une table a II chiés, puis l’estrain forment, et le laisse III jors, puis le deslie; et le fai reposer, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the dislocation is in no way at the base of the foot, so that you make the patient sit on a level place or a table all straight, and put your foot on what opens from these joints, then press your foot down as it grows back, and when it is even, and there is nothing more to open, take off the splint from the base of the foot with a table at II degrees, then shape it, and leave it for III days, then take it off; and let him rest, until he is healthy.
de plaie et de dislocation ensamble	of wound and dislocation together
Quant plaie vient avec la dislocation, et on la vuet restorer, maintes fois avient que li malaides muert: si ne soies mie presumptuous en la cure, se tu n’es saiges en l’art et tu ne l’as useit longement, et se tu n’es pitous et misericors et tardis, ne mie hardis; et use au comencement de choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et laisse le malaide en la main Deu, se tu n’i vois esperance de santeit; et quant tu i vois esperance, si ramoinne maintenant le membre au leu, ainsois que li apostemes chaus i viegne; et quant li membres est a leu, si aministre choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et cure la plaie, si com il covient, d’oignemens desiccatis; et se avec la dislocation a brisure, et os menus desevrez, si les oste, et fai ce que nos avons dit en maladies simples; et te garde d’entrer en voie de paour, selonc ce que j’ai dit, car ce te vaut mues selonc ton Creator, et por la saveteit de t’arme et de ton cors.	When a wound occurs with dislocation, and it is restored, many times the patient dies: if you are not presumptuous in the cure, if you are not skilled in the art and have not practiced it for a long time, and if you are not pitiful and merciful and tardy, do not be too bold; and use at the beginning things that calm the abscess with hot, and leave the patient to God, if you see no hope of health; and when you see hope, now put the member back in place, so that the hot ones come; and when the member is in place, administer things that dry out the abscesses, and cure the wound, as is right, with ointments; and if there is fracture with dislocation, and small bones are broken, mend them, and do as we have said for simple illnesses; and guard yourself from entering the way of fear, according to what I have said, because that will cost you dear according to your Creator, and for the sake of arming and strengthening your body.
Amen	Amen
